601 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Fain v. State


NO. 03-95-00427-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


986 S.W.2d 666; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7746



December 17, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 30, 1999. Dissenting Opinion January 14, 1999.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 06/30/1999
Post-conviction relief denied at In re Fain, 83 S.W.3d 885, 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 5394 (Tex. App. Austin, 2002)
Post-conviction relief denied at Fain v. State, 2015 Tex. App. LEXIS 4620 (Tex. App. Austin, May 7, 2015)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Fain v. Davis, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 161463 (N.D. Tex., Nov. 21, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 12, 1998, Previously Reported at: 978 S.W.2d 149, 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1483.

FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY, 277TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. 95-112-K277, HONORABLE JOHN R. CARTER, JUDGE PRESIDING.
Fain v. State, 978 S.W.2d 149, 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1483 (Tex. App. Austin, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed a motion for rehearing en banc of the court's prior opinion, which reversed the judgment from the District Court of Williamson County, 277th Judicial District (Texas) convicting appellant of murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's conviction for murder was previously reversed by the court. The court granted the state's motion for rehearing en banc. The court's prior decision that the district court did not have jurisdiction because there had been no formal change of venue was withdrawn. The error was a procedural one, rather than jurisdictional as construed by the court in its original opinion. Thus, it was not a fundamental error and was not preserved for review. Accordingly, the court withdrew its prior decision and reviewed the points of error originally raised. Appellant was not denied due course of law when his motion for new trial was not heard. Appellant did not satisfy the two-pronged test for ineffective assistance of counsel. There was no error in allowing testimony of the victim's statements regarding her relationship with appellant because it fell within the state-of-mind exception to the hearsay rule, and its admission was harmless because appellant failed to object to similar evidence. There was no error in admitting evidence alleged to have been illegally seized because appellant had elicited evidence of the search first. Accordingly, the court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court granted the state's motion for rehearing en banc, withdrew its previous opinion, and substituted it for this one because the unassigned error upon which the court previously reversed appellant's conviction was a procedural error. Therefore, it was not a fundamental error and was not preserved for review. Upon rehearing, the court affirmed appellant's conviction, having found no merit with the points of error raised by appellant.

 

602 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ealoms v. State


No. 10-97-179-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


983 S.W.2d 853; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7718



December 16, 1998, Delivered  
December 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 9, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 54th District Court. McLennan County, Texas. Trial Court # 96-105-C.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the 54th District Court, McLennan County (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated assault, arguing that the trial court erred in overruling his objection to the prosecution's peremptory challenges and erred in denying discovery of an arresting officer's personnel file to support his claim of self-defense.


OVERVIEW: Officers witnessed defendant driving erratically and, believing he was intoxicated, attempted to stop him. When an officer reached into the car to take the keys out of the ignition, defendant hit the accelerator, dragged the officer down the street, and eventually ran him over. Defendant was charged with and convicted of aggravated assault. He appealed the judgment of conviction, arguing that the prosecution exercised peremptory challenges in a racially discriminatory manner and that he was improperly denied discovery of Brady materials. On review, the judgment of conviction was affirmed, as the prosecution offered appropriate race-neutral explanations for its challenges and defendant failed to establish that such explanations were mere pretext. Although the trial court erred in concluding that evidence of prior misconduct by the officer was subject to disclosure only if substantiated and erred in precluding discovery of material information favorable to defendant's claim of self-defense, reversal was not required where there was no reasonable probability that, had the evidence been disclosed, the result of the proceeding would have been different.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was affirmed, as the trial court did not err in overruling defendant's objections to the prosecution's peremptory challenges where the prosecution offered valid, non-discriminatory reasons for such exercise. Further, although the trial court erred in failing to permit discovery of material impeachment information, reversal was not required where disclosure would not have affected the proceeding's outcome.

 

603 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Van Gundy v. State


No. 06-97-00030-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7526


November 2, 1998, Argued  
December 4, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 1. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 9641378.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the County Criminal Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him of the misdemeanor offense of promotion of an obscene device in violation of Tex. Pen. Code § 43.23(c)(1) (1994).


OVERVIEW: An undercover officer purchased a clitoral stimulator from appellant. He later returned with other officers and confiscated other obscene merchandise from appellant's shop. Appellant was convicted of promotion of an obscene device in violation of Tex. Pen. Code § 43.23(c)(1) (1994). The court affirmed finding the state could deny access to obscene devices. The court held the obscene devices were not speech protected by U.S. Const. amend. I. The court found appellant's motion to quash the information was untimely. The court found the trial judge did not have to make a determination that the clitoral stimulator was obscene before issuing a warrant. The court held the plain view doctrine applied to items seized prior to the issuance of a warrant. The court found there was no abuse of discretion in the admission of extraneous evidence relevant to appellant's intent and knowledge concerning the character of the obscene device. The court held the trial court did not err in failing to instruct the jury on the definition of obscenity because that term was defined in the statute, thus, the jury was not required to make an independent determination that the device in question was obscene.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed because the statute was constitutional. Appellant's motion to quash the information was untimely. Because the legislature defined "obscene device," the jury did not have to make a finding of obscenity. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting evidence which was relevant to show appellant's intent and knowledge concerning the character of the device he sold to an undercover officer.

 

604 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


McClain v. State


No. 06-97-00035-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


984 S.W.2d 700; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7314


November 24, 1998, Submitted  
November 25, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Overruled January 7, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 32.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 9632879.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for driving while intoxicated in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 7, Harris County, Texas, on several grounds, including that there was no probable cause for his arrest and that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 (1998) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for driving while intoxicated on several grounds, including that there was no probable cause for his arrest. The court held that after an officer observed defendant speeding, the officer had probable cause to stop him pursuant to Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 543.001, 545.351, 545.352 (1998). After defendant admitted he had three beers and failed a subsequent field sobriety test, the officer had probable cause to take defendant to police headquarters. At headquarters, police made of videotape of defendant when he refused, after oral and written warnings, to take a breath test, all of which constituted probable cause for his arrest. The court also held that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 (1998), which allowed introduction of evidence of a person's refusal to submit to the taking of a specimen of breath or blood, was not unconstitutionally vague and that conflicting inferences did not render the statute unconstitutional. As the court found no error, the judgment of conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of driving while intoxicated was affirmed. The court held that the statute that permitted the admissibility of defendant's refusal to take a breath test was constitutional, and that there was probable cause for defendant's arrest.

 

605 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


State v. Minor


No. 11-97-00190-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


981 S.W.2d 481; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7326



November 25, 1998, Decided  
November 25, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 220th District Court of Comanche County.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged the order of the 220th District Court of Comanche County (Texas), which set aside an indictment of appellee on the charge of engaging in organized crime activity in connection with a burglary pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 71.01(a), 71.02(a)(1) (1994).


OVERVIEW: When a previous indictment for engaging in organized criminal activity in connection with a burglary had been set aside, appellee filed a motion to set aside a new indictment for the same offense. The court reversed the order of the trial court setting aside the indictment pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 71.01(a), 71.02(a)(1) (1994). The indictment, which alleged one criminal activity, a single burglary, was not defective because the statute referred to plural activities. Organized criminal activity included a combination of persons carrying on "one or more" criminal offenses by engaging in either a single criminal activity or multiple activities. Setting aside the prior indictment ended that prosecution without determining issues on the merits. Thus, neither res judicata, nor collateral estoppel prevented refiling the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that set aside the state's indictment because when the trial court set aside a previous indictment, there was no decision on the merits to prevent refiling the subject indictment on res judicata or collateral estoppel grounds.

Stewart v. State


NO. 14-98-00217-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7337



November 25, 1998, Rendered  
November 25, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9806921.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed an application for writ of habeas corpus to challenge an order from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County (Texas) that revoked his bond and set a new bond with conditions pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.44(a)(1) after he was arrested for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: After appellant was arrested for driving while intoxicated, the county court set bond with electronic monitoring and a curfew as conditions pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.44. Appellant violated the terms of the bond, causing the county court to revoke the bond and set a new bond with the same conditions. Appellant filed an application for a writ of habeas corpus, but the court affirmed the county court's order, holding that the imposed curfew as a form of home confinement and electronic monitoring were authorized as a condition of bond under the Texas statute. The court also ruled that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 17.44 was constitutional because it was rationally related to the legitimate state objective of ensuring appellant's appearance at trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the county court's order revoking appellant's bond and setting a new bond with conditions pursuant to Texas law because the curfew and electronic monitoring were authorized under the law, and the Texas law setting conditions for bond was constitutional because it was rationally related to a legitimate state objective.

Liedtke v. State


NO. 14-98-00310-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7338



November 25, 1998, Rendered  
November 25, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 773,331.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 248th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that denied his application for writ of habeas corpus after he was arrested for possession of methamphetamine pursuant to the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, having been arrested for possession of methamphetamine pursuant to Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115, applied for writ of habeas corpus on the grounds that the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.001 et seq. was unconstitutionally vague, that it violated separation of powers, and that it allowed arbitrary prosecution. Appellant also claimed that the prosecutor engaged in misconduct. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's order, holding that the statute gave appellant sufficient notice of the prohibited conduct and was therefore not unconstitutionally vague. The court also held that the statute did not allow for arbitrary prosecution under either Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.115 or § 481.129 because the two statutes did not address the same offense. The court determined that the Texas Controlled Substances Act did not improperly delegate legislative power to the executive branch because the commissioner could not change any controlled substance in the statute under which appellant was charged. The court concluded that the prosecutor did not engage in misconduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus after he was arrested for possession of methamphetamine because the Texas Controlled Substances Act was not unconstitutionally vague, nor did it violate separation of powers or allow for arbitrary prosecution. The court also found that there was no prosecutorial misconduct.

 

608 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Dallas v. State


NOS. 01-95-00666-CR & 01-95-00665-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7269



November 19, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 28, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 12. Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Nos. 9409126 & 9328755.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction from the County Criminal Court No. 12, Harris County (Texas) for operating an unlicensed guard dog company, in violation of the Private Investigators and Private Security Agencies Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of operating an unlicensed guard dog company in violation of the Private Investigators and Private Security Agencies Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4413(29bb). Appellant contended there was insufficient evidence to support such conviction because the dogs he sold were too timid to qualify as guard dogs. Appellant also alleged that § 13(a) and § 2(8) of the Act were unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's conviction. In order to qualify as a guard dog under the Act, a dog had to be sold for protective purposes. The ferocity or timidity of the dog and its ability to protect were irrelevant under the Act. Section 13(a) and § 2(8) were not vague because they specifically defined a guard dog company and prohibited a person from selling, without a license, a dog that was represented to be trained for protection of persons or property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for operating an unlicensed guard dog company. The Private Investigators and Private Security Agencies Act was not unconstitutionally vague because it specifically prohibited individuals from selling dogs for protection purposes without a license. The protective capabilities of such dogs were irrelevant under the Act.

 

609 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Loucadou v. State


NO. 01-97-00389-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7287



November 19, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9651992.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for driving while intoxicated in the County Criminal Court at Law No. 9, Harris County (Texas). Appellant claimed that the court erred in denying his motion to suppress appellant's refusal to take the intoxilyzer test and that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.06 (1998), which provided that a refusal to take such test was admissible, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped for speeding and weaving and arrested for driving while intoxicated based upon his failing the field sobriety tests, and the odor of alcohol. After his arrest, appellant refused to take a breath test. Appellant and appellee state entered into a stipulation as to the facts. The trial court denied appellant's motion to suppress his refusal to take the test and convicted him of driving while intoxicated. The court affirmed and held that appellant, under Tex. R. App. P. 33.1(a)(1)(A), waived his argument that the stipulated evidence was too conclusory to establish probable cause for the stop because he had not made the argument in his motion to suppress to the trial court. Additionally, the court held that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 (1998), which provided that appellant's refusal to take a breath test was admissible, was constitutional. The court held that § 724.061 was not vague and that appellee was not required to make a predicate showing of relevance or a predicate showing that the breath test instrument was reliable and accurate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction of driving while intoxicated because appellant's refusal to take the intoxilyzer test was admissible as evidence.

 

610 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Miller v. State


No. 06-97-00033-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7186


November 17, 1998, Submitted  
November 18, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 724669.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 339th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), after entering a plea of not guilty to the charge of driving while intoxicated and pleas of true to two enhancement paragraphs, which alleged that defendant previously committed two offenses of possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the felony offense of driving while intoxicated and, in two enhancement paragraphs, was alleged to have previously committed two offenses of possession of a controlled substance. Defendant was convicted after entering a plea of not guilty to the offense and pleas of true to the allegations in the two enhancement paragraphs, and the trial court sentenced defendant to 25 years confinement. Defendant argued that his sentence was cruel and unusual under U.S. Const. amend. IX and Tex. Const. art. I, § 13. Defendant also claimed that Tex. Penal Code §§ 49.04 and 49.11 were unconstitutional, and that the jury charge and the indictment were fundamentally erroneous because they failed to allege or require a culpable mental state. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence. Defendant could not complain that his punishment was cruel because he did not object timely and specifically at trial. Also, a culpable mental state was not required for the offense of driving while intoxicated. Finally, the failure to allege a culpable mental state was not grounds for quashing a charging instrument.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction of the felony offense of driving while intoxicated. Defendant's objection to his 25-year sentence, enhanced by his two previous offenses of possession of a controlled substance, as cruel and unusual was not preserved for appellate review because of defendant's failure to object at trial. Also, proof of a culpable mental state was not required for his conviction.

 

611 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Trehern v. State


NO. 03-97-00600-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6898



November 5, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 OF BELL COUNTY NO. 2C96-5760, HONORABLE JOHN BARINA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a criminal action, defendant appealed a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2 of Bell County (Texas), which convicted him of telephone harassment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07 (Supp. 1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of telephone harassment under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07 (Supp. 1998) for calling his victim at work and threatening to kill him. On appeal defendant argued that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction, that there was insufficient proof of criminal intent, and that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal the court affirmed. Although defendant and his sister testified that defendant did not make a threat during the phone call, there was testimony by another witness to the call that a threat was made, which the trier of fact was free to believe. That testimony was also sufficient to support a finding beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant intended to harass, annoy, alarm, abuse, torment, or embarrass. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague because it sufficiently defined telephone harassment as a threat, by telephone or in writing, to inflict bodily injury on the person, or to commit a felony against the person, a member of his family, or his property. Thus, the conviction was proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment convicting defendant of telephone harassment. There was sufficient evidence to support the verdict, including a finding of intent to harass, annoy, alarm, abuse, torment or embarrass, and the criminal statute was not unconstitutionally vague.

 

612 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Letson v. Vanaman


NO. 07-98-0263-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6906



November 4, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied October 7, 1999. Appellees' Motion for Rehearing Overruled December 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 47TH DISTRICT COURT OF POTTER COUNTY; NO. 84,857-A; HONORABLE DAVID L. GLEASON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law enforcement officials sought review after the 47th District Court of Potter County (Texas) temporarily enjoined appellants from seizing appellee proprietor's quasigambling machines under Tex. Penal Code Ann. 47.01. Appellants alleged that the trial court lacked jurisdiction and that there was no evidence to support the decision.


OVERVIEW: Appellee proprietor brought suit seeking injunctive relief. After a hearing, the trial court temporarily enjoined appellant law enforcement officers from seizing appellee's quasigambling machines under Tex. Penal Code Ann. 47.01. The court revered and remanded with instructions to dismiss and held that the trial court lacked jurisdiction to issue the injunction because a complainant had to both attack the constitutionality of a penal provision and aver that its enforcement would irreparably injure vested property rights. Appellee failed to allege unconstitutionality. To the extent the trial court lacked jurisdiction, the trial court had no power to interpret section 47.01 and declare appellee's rights. Moreover, the court held that a party seeking a temporary injunction had to present evidence of a probable injury and a probable right of recovery and that this requirement was not satisfied by sworn pleadings and legal argument unless the parties agreed. And although that argument was not presented to the trial court, the court held that no predicate was required to preserve the argument that findings rendered in a nonjury trial were legally or factually insufficient.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the temporary injunction, dissolved the injunction, and remanded with instructions to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. The court held that appellee proprietor had failed to allege that a penal statute was unconstitutional. As an additional ground for dismissal, the court noted that there was no evidence supporting the injunction and no agreement allowing the use of pleadings and affidavits in its stead.

Letson v. Barnes


NO. 07-98-0264-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


979 S.W.2d 414; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6908



November 4, 1998, Decided

OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the temporary injunction, dissolved the injunction, and remanded with instructions to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction. The court held that appellee proprietors had failed to allege that a penal statute was unconstitutional. As an additional ground for dismissal, the court noted that there was no evidence supporting the injunction and no agreement allowing the use of pleadings and affidavits in its stead.

 

614 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re W.A.B.


NO. 14-97-00871-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


979 S.W.2d 804; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6754



October 29, 1998, Rendered  
October 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 314th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 87189. Mary Craft, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action brought by the Texas Department of Protective and Regulatory Services under Tex. Fam. Code § 161.001 (1998), the mother appealed the decision of the 314th District Court, Harris County (Texas), to terminate the parent-child relationship, contending that the evidence was factually and legally insufficient and the termination order did not require the showing of any causal connection between her behavior and actual endangerment.


OVERVIEW: The mother appealed the order terminating the parent-child relationship in a suit brought by the Texas Department of Protective and Regulatory Services, arguing the evidence was both factually and legally insufficient and that the termination order did not require the showing of any causal connection between her behavior and any actual endangerment to her child. Affirming the decision, the court explained that a mother's use of drugs during pregnancy was conduct which endangered the physical and emotional well-being of her child. The court also held that, although parental rights were of constitutional magnitude, she had waived her challenge to the interpretation of Tex. Fam. Code § 161.001 (1998) by attempting to raise the issue for the first time on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order terminating the parent-child relationship in a suit brought by the Texas Department of Protective and Regulatory Services, explaining that the trial court found by clear and convincing evidence that the termination was in the best interest of the child and that the mother engaged in conduct which endangered the physical or emotional well-being of the child.

 

615 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Segovia v. Texas Dep't of Protective & Regulatory Servs.


NO. 14-97-01363-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


979 S.W.2d 785; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6755



October 29, 1998, Judgment Rendered  
October 29, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied February 18, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 314th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 90,729. David Longoria, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the 314th District Court, Harris County (Texas) which terminated his parental rights to his son.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's parental rights to his son were terminated because the trial court found by clear and convincing evidence that the termination was in the child's best interest, appellant knowingly endangered his child, and he was adjudicated criminally responsible for the serious injury of a child. On appeal, he challenged the sufficiency of the evidence. The court affirmed because even if the evidence were insufficient to support the finding that appellant endangered his child, his adjudication of criminal responsibility for the serious injury of a child due to abandonment or endangerment proscribed in Tex. Penal Code § 22.041 would justify the termination. Since appellant introduced no evidence anyone could properly provide for the child until appellant's release from prison, the court agreed that it was in the child's best interest to terminate parental rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment terminating appellant's parental rights was affirmed because it was justified by the adjudication that appellant was criminally responsible for the serious injury of a child, and the termination was in the child's best interest.

In the Interest of A.J.F.


No. 04-98-00251-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6710



October 28, 1998, Delivered  
October 28, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From County Court at Law No. 1, Webb County, Texas. Trial Court No. C-95-00881-C1. Honorable Raul R. Vasquez, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant putative father challenged an order of the County Court at Law No. 1, Webb County (Texas), which rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellant in his suit to establish paternity.


OVERVIEW: A child was born during a marriage. When the couple divorced, the child was named as the couple's child in the divorce decree. Later, the couple reconciled and remarried. Appellant, the child's putative father, filed suit to establish himself as the child's biological father. In response, the couple alleged that the suit was barred because the divorce decree constituted a prior adjudication of paternity for the purposes of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 160.007(a)(1). After blood tests established that appellant was the child's biological father, the parties asked for a bench trial to determine whether § 160.007(a)(1) barred the action. The trial court rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellant. Appellant sought review, but the appellate court affirmed the trial court's order. The court held that § 160.007(a)(1) did not violate appellant's rights under Tex. Const. art. I, § 19 when it limited appellant's standing to the period before the husband was adjudicated the child's biological father. The court found that § 160.007(a)(1) represented a reasonable means of promoting the state's legitimate interests in the finality of judgments and the stability of families.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed an order that rendered a take-nothing judgment against appellant putative father in his suit to establish paternity. The court found that appellant was not entitled to challenge an established paternity order because the child's paternity had already been adjudicated in a divorce decree.

 

617 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


NO. 03-97-00372-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6553



October 22, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 147TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0954572, HONORABLE WILFORD FLOWERS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and Remanded for Award of Jail-Time Credit.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of order from the District Court of Travis County, 147th Judicial District (Texas) revoking community supervision. Appellant contended that he was not given credit on his sentence for the time he was incarcerated prior to the final revocation proceeding. Appellant also argued that the trial court erred in reassessing and increasing his punishment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order revoking community supervision. He alleged that he was not given credit on his sentence for the time he was incarcerated prior to the final revocation proceeding. The court held that because appellant was indigent, did not make bond, and received the maximum possible punishment, the trial court did not have discretion to deny appellant credit for jail-time prior to his plea. The court held that appellant would be granted credit on his sentence for the time he was incarcerated between his arrest on the revocation warrant and the imposition of sentence. Appellant argued that the trial court's denial of credit on his sentence for time incarcerated between his arrest on the revocation warrant and his sentencing after revocation of community supervision violated constitutional rights of due process and due course of law under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 19. The court held that judicial discretion allowed by Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12, § 15(h)(2) (1998) violated the due course of law provision of Texas Constitution.


OUTCOME: The order of revocation was affirmed. The cause was remanded to the trial court which was ordered to credit appellant for the jail-time to which he was entitled. The court held that appellant would be granted credit on his sentence for the time he was incarcerated prior to his guilty plea. Appellant was granted credit on his sentence for the time he was incarcerated between his arrest on the revocation warrant and imposition of sentence.

 

618 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re Pleasant Glade Assembly of God


NO. 2-98-222-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


991 S.W.2d 85; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6567



October 22, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended December 3, 1998. Real Parties in Interest's Motion for Rehearing Denied December 3, 1998. Relator's Petition for Writ of Mandamus Conditionally Granted October 22, 1998.



DISPOSITION: Writ of mandamus conditionally granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner church and ministers sought a writ of mandamus to determine whether respondent parishioners' claims of false imprisonment, negligence, intentional infliction of emotional distress, child abuse and child neglect, were barred by the free-exercise clause of the U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner church and ministers sought a writ of mandamus to review whether claims of false imprisonment, negligence, intentional infliction of emotional distress, child abuse and neglect, pursued by respondent parishioners were barred as violative of the free-exercise clause of U.S. Const. amend. I. The court provisionally granted the writ and would have issued it if the trial court did not grant petitioners' motion to dismiss respondents' complaint and petitioners' motion for protective order. The court found that respondents' claims would have resulted in an impermissible inquiry into petitioners' religious beliefs and the validity of those beliefs. The court found that the issue of petitioners' negligent application of religious doctrine was not a justiciable controversy. The court held that the complained of conduct would have inexorably intertwined petitioners' religious beliefs, and any inquiry into the appropriateness of conduct would have involved and unconstitutional inquiry into the underlying religious beliefs.


OUTCOME: A petition for a writ of mandamus was provisionally granted if the trial court did not grant petitioner church and ministers' motion to dismiss and motion for protective order, because the complained of behaviors inextricably intertwined conduct with religious beliefs, because any inquiry into religious beliefs was constitutionally impermissible, and because the negligent application of religious doctrine was not justiciable.

 

619 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Motorola, Inc. v. Tarrant County Appraisal Dist.


NO. 2-97-266-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


980 S.W.2d 899; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6564



October 22, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 17TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a corporation, sought review of the order from the 17th District Court of Tarrant County (Texas) that granted the motion of appellee, the county appraisal district, on appellant's petition to review appellee's order denying appellant's application for a freeport exemption under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1-j(a)(3) for failure to provide information within 30 days of appellee's request pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 11.251(h) (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a corporation, applied for an ad valorem tax exemption of its freeport goods pursuant to Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1-j(a)(3), but did not provide appellee, the county appraisal district, with the additional information that appellee requested within the 30-day period as required by Tex. Code Ann. § 11.251(h) (1992). Appellee denied the exemption, appellant petitioned the district court for review, and the district court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court held that art. VIII was not totally self executing because it did not prescribe rules on how its requirements were to be enforced. Because there was nothing to indicate that the exemption procedures in Tex. Tax. Code Ann. § 11.45 (1992) did not apply to § 11.251(h), and because the 30-day deadline in § 11.251(h) was not unreasonable and was related to the purpose of art. VIII, § 1-j(a)(3) to promote the economic development of Texas, § 11.251 did not offend the equal protection clause of U.S. Const. amend. XIV, and was thus constitutional. Therefore, the court affirmed the order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting appellee county appraisal district's motion for summary judgment on appellant corporation's petition to review appellee's denial of appellant's application for a freeport tax exemption for not providing information within 30 days of appellee's request. The court held that the statute allowing only 30 days to comply with the request was related to the purpose of the exemption and was thus constitutional.

 

620 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Jackson Hotel Corp. v. Wichita County Appraisal Dist.


NO. 2-97-112-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


980 S.W.2d 879; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6563



October 22, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended, December 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 78TH DISTRICT COURT OF WICHITA COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner sought review of a decision from the 78th District Court of Wichita County (Texas), dismissing plaintiff's suit challenging an unfavorable property appraisal by defendant county on the ground that plaintiff's challenge to the appraisal was barred as being untimely filed after the delinquency date for payment of taxes had expired under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08(b)(1988).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff landowner challenged the trial court's dismissal of his challenge to a real property appraisal made by defendant county. The trial court held that plaintiff's suit was barred as untimely because it was filed after the date for payment of taxes had expired. On appeal, the court held that under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08(b)(1988) as interpreted by the state's highest court, plaintiff was entitled to a hearing to determine whether he had substantially complied with the statutory requirement of paying the assessed taxes before the delinquency date. If plaintiff had substantially complied, he would retain his right to challenge defendant's appraisal. The fact that plaintiff was financially unable to pay the taxes before the delinquency date did not render the trial court's dismissal harmless error because, at the time plaintiff's 1994 taxes became delinquent, the state legislature had not yet enacted the provision for filing an oath of inability to pay as required by Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08 (1996). The court reversed and remanded for a hearing to determine whether plaintiff had substantially complied with Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 42.08(b)(1988).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiff landowner's challenge to defendant county's appraisal and assessment of property taxes on plaintiff's land because the trial court failed to determine whether plaintiff had substantially complied with statutory requirements for preserving his right to appeal. Therefore, the court remanded for a substantial compliance hearing.

 

621 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. State


No. 05-92-01700-CR


COURT OF APPEALS FIFTH DISTRICT OF TEXAS AT DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6511



October 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court Number Two. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F86-95053-I.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged the Criminal District Court Number Two. Dallas County (Texas), judgment of conviction for delivery of cocaine, and assessment of a 60 year sentence and a $ 1000 fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was indicted for delivery of cocaine and entered into a plea for community supervision and deferred adjudication. Subsequently, appellant was found in violation of his community supervision conditions and sentenced to 60 years in prison. Appellant contended that he was entitled to a new trial because he made a timely request for the statement of facts, the court' reporter's notes were lost through no fault of his, and the parties could not agree on the facts. The court held that appellant failed to make a timely request for the reporter's record. The only delay attributable to the lost reporter's record was the five months appellant waited. The court held that this was not an inordinate delay of the appellate process and did not deprive appellant of due process. The court further held that appellant entered his guilty plea freely and voluntarily because where the record was otherwise silent, the court presumed that there was a recital in the judgment relative to the voluntariness of a guilty plea. The trial court also had jurisdiction to revoke appellant's community supervision after it had expired because a capias was issued before the period had expired.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that appellant inmate did not make a timely request for the reporter's record, he was not deprived of due process, he pled guilty freely and voluntarily, he did not receive ineffective assistance of counsel, the trial court properly denied appellant's motion for a new trial without a hearing, the trial court had jurisdiction to revoke his community supervision, and appellant failed to object to his sentence.

Favaloro v. State Bar of Texas


No. 05-96-01461-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6430



October 16, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 191st District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-3626-J.

This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of July 22, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4378.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant moved for rehearing in its challenge to an order of the 191st District Court, Dallas County (Texas), that dismissed appellant's injunctive and declaratory relief claims against appellees, the state bar and the state bar's employees.


OVERVIEW: A grievance proceeding was filed against appellant by the state bar. Appellant then sought injunctive and declaratory relief against appellees, the state bar and the state bar's employees. The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant's complaint. The court held that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the matter. The court held that the trial court had no jurisdiction to hear appellant's claims because it would have interfered with a pending grievance proceeding filed against appellant. The court also held that the state bar was entitled to governmental immunity as to appellant's claims. The court held that the state bar did not waive said immunity. The court also held that the sovereign immunity extended to the state bar's employees because they were sued as individuals in their official capacities.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellant's motion for rehearing, but to correct typographical errors, the court vacated and withdrew its earlier judgment, and issued this decision. The court affirmed the dismissal of appellant's complaint because the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction over the claims.

Seminole Pipeline Co. v. Broad Leaf Partners, Inc.


NO. 14-96-00825-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


979 S.W.2d 730; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6677; 142 Oil & Gas Rep. 338



October 15, 1998, Judgment Rendered  
October 15, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 55th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-24087.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part, Reversed and Remanded in Part, Reversed and Rendered in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellee property owners' suit for damages arising out of an explosion at appellant pipeline companies' underground storage facility, appellants sought review of an order of the 55th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found that all appellants were negligent, grossly negligent, acted with malice, proximately caused appellees' damages, created a permanent nuisance, and awarded punitive damages for past and future mental anguish.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners sued appellant pipeline companies after an explosion occurred at appellants' storage facility. The trial court found that appellants were negligent, grossly negligent, acted with malice, proximately caused appellees' damages, created a nuisance, and awarded actual damages for property damage and mental anguish, as well as punitive damages. Appellants sought review. In reversing the judgment against one appellant, the court found that its limited involvement in the facility's operations was insufficient to establish the type of control necessary for a finding of negligence under the doctrine of res ipsa loquitur. As to the remaining appellants, the court found that the evidence was sufficient to establish that appellants acted with gross negligence, but not malice, in that they proceeded with conscious indifference to the rights, safety, and welfare of others. The court reversed the trial court's award of mental anguish because, where a claim of mental anguish was based solely upon property damage resulting from gross negligence, recovery was contingent upon evidence of some ill will, which appellees did not show. The modified judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, in part, and affirmed a modified judgment. Modified judgment was rendered in favor of one appellant pipeline company because of its limited involvement, and the court vacated only the award for past and future mental anguish and the finding of malice as to other appellant pipeline companies. The court remanded for recomputation of the punitive damage cap and prejudgment interest.

Newsome v. State


NO. 07-97-0179-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6276



October 8, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT OF HALE COUNTY; NO. 96C-360; HONORABLE BILL HOLLARS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction of assault by the County Court of Hale County (Texas) and from the resulting punishment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for assaulting his wife one year after his indictment for aggravated assault from the same occurrence was dismissed. Thirty months after his arrest, defendant was convicted. However, the state was only responsible for 18 months' delay. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. Eighteen months delay was not presumptively prejudicial because the purpose of the two-year assault statute of limitations was the same as the speedy trial right. Defendant failed to make a prima facie showing of prejudice. In any case, defendant failed to timely assert his speedy trial right. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding evidence of his wife's substance abuse prior to determining its relevance because the trial court implicitly made findings of fact and conclusions of law when it ruled upon the admissibility of the evidence. Defendant did not always give the trial court reasons why witnesses' testimony should have been admissible, and failed to present the same arguments on appeal as he had at trial. The trial court could conclude that evidence that defendant's wife had fallen and hurt herself in the past was inadmissible character evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction because he did not make a prima facie showing of prejudice, and he failed to timely assert his speedy trial right. The court also held that defendant's wife's substance abuse was inadmissible to impeach her credibility because there was no evidence that it was in temporal proximity to the assault.

Hansen v. State


NO. 01-96-01463-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6408



October 8, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 3. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9632250.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorcyclist sought review his conviction in the County Criminal Court at No. 3, Harris County (Texas) for operating a motorcycle without protective headgear under Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 661.001.


OVERVIEW: Appellant motorcyclist was convicted of operating a motorcycle without wearing proper protective headgear under Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 661.003(a). Appellant challenged the ruling and filed a motion to quash the traffic citation on the ground that it violated the U.S. Const. amend. I, V, XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, §§ 3, 8, 19. The county court affirmed the conviction. The court affirmed the conviction and held that it had jurisdiction because appellant raised constitutional issues. The court held that the law was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad because appellant knew what the law required, specifically that he was required to wear a helmet with a department of transportation sticker on it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order convicting appellant motorcyclist of operating a motorcycle without protective headgear because the law was clear in stating that appellant was required to wear a helmet with a department of transportation sticker; thus, the law under which appellant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague or overbroad.

Texas Dep't. of Pub. Safety v. Chavez


NO. 2-96-272-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


981 S.W.2d 449; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 7027



October 8, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion to Publish Opinion Granted November 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and render judgment reinstating the suspension of appellee's driver's license for a period of ninety days.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Texas Department of Public Safety challenged a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 3 of Tarrant County (Texas), which reversed an administrative decision allowing appellant to suspend appellee's driver's license for driving while intoxicated and held that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 724.015, 522.102, and 522.103 were unconstitutionally vague when applied to a commercial driver's license holder.


OVERVIEW: Appellee driver was arrested for driving while intoxicated. At an administrative hearing, appellant Texas Department of Public Safety (department) was authorized to suspend appellee's driver's license for 90 days. The county court reversed and held that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 724.015, 522.102, and 522.103 were unconstitutionally vague when applied to a commercial driver's license holder who was stopped in a non-commercial vehicle and who refused to provide a breath or blood sample. On appeal the court reversed and held that the county court erred in not reviewing the administrative record because its review should have been confined to such record pursuant to Tex Transp. Code Ann. § 523.043. The court further held that §§ 522.102 and 522.103 did not apply to appellee because he was stopped while driving a private vehicle. The court further held that § 724.015 was not unconstitutionally vague because it clearly stated that a driver, whether driving a commercial or non-commercial vehicle, who refused to submit to the taking of a specimen would have had his driver's license suspended for at least 90 days.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment reinstating appellee's driver's license after it was suspended by appellant Texas Department of Public Safety for driving while intoxicated because state law concerning license suspensions was not unconstitutionally vague when applied to appellee, who was a commercial driver's license holder driving a private vehicle.

In the Interest of Digges


No. 04-98-00252-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


981 S.W.2d 445; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6216



October 7, 1998, Delivered  
October 7, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 131st Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 80-CI-7431. Honorable Frank Montalvo, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged an order of the 131st District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which denied his motion to stay and entered a wage withholding order to pay child support arrearages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant husband and appellee wife were divorced in 1980 and husband was ordered to pay child support until the children reached 18. After appellant stopped paying child support, appellee filed an application for judicial writ of withholding. Appellant filed a motion to stay, contending that the support was barred by limitations, that the arrearage had not been reduced to judgment, that the action was barred by laches, and that the applicable statute violated his constitutional rights. The trial court denied the motion to stay and ordered the arrearage to be withheld from appellant's wages. On appeal the court affirmed, because the only grounds to challenge the withholding were as a dispute over the identity of the obligor or the amount of the arrearage. The court found that there were no constitutional protections applicable to a wage withholding order and laches was not an available defense. The court was allowed to consider whether the withholding order would impose an undue financial burden on the obligor.


OUTCOME: The denial of appellant husband's motion to stay an entry of a wage withholding order for back child support was affirmed, because constitutional protections did not extend to wage withholding orders, there were no limitations periods, and laches was inapplicable.

 

628 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re State ex rel. O'Connell


No. 05-97-02062-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


976 S.W.2d 902; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6200



October 6, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING. PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of August 26, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5346.



DISPOSITION: Conditionally Granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: State and defendant sought rehearing of the court's prior opinion regarding the mandamus proceeding initiated by state to compel the Collin County Court at Law No. 1 (Texas) to impanel a jury in a matter in which defendant was charged with misdemeanor indecent exposure.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with indecent exposure, a misdemeanor. He signed a written jury waiver and announced his intent to plead either guilty or nolo contendere to the charge. State refused to consent to defendant's waiver and requested that a jury be impaneled. The trial court accepted the waiver and set the case for a plea hearing. State sought a writ of mandamus to compel the trial court to empanel a jury. The court rendered an opinion, but the parties sought rehearing thereof for clarification. The court granted the request for rehearing and issued a new opinion explaining its reversal of the trial court's decision. The court concluded concluding that defendant's jury waiver was invalid because state did not consent to the waiver and such consent was required under Tex. Crim. Proc. Ann. § 1.13(a). The court further held that state's consent was required even though defendant planned to enter a guilty or nolo contendre plea because it was the jury's responsibility to assess punishment where such a plea was entered and the penalty to the offense was not fixed by law. Thus court thus concluded that state was entitled to a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court granted the parties' request for rehearing, vacated its prior opinion, and issued a new opinion conditionally granting state's request for a writ of mandamus to compel the lower court to empanel a jury because state did not consent to defendant's jury trial waiver and the waiver was therefore invalid. The court remanded the matter with directions for the lower court to set the cause for the jury docket.

McBride v. City of New Braunfels


NO. 03-97-00555-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6136



October 1, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMAL COUNTY, 274TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. C95-1035C, HONORABLE CHARLES RAMSAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant arrestee sought review of a decision of the District Court of Comal County, 274th Judicial District (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, city and police officer, in appellant's suit claiming damages for injuries suffered while he was incarcerated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant arrestee brought a suit against appellees, city and police officer, for injuries suffered when appellees took blood and hair samples pursuant to court order, while appellant was incarcerated following his arrest on charges of aggravated assault. Appellant first brought the claims in federal court. The federal district court dismissed appellant's federal claims with prejudice and his state-law claims without prejudice. Appellant sought review, and the court of appeals affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded the cause to the federal district court, which again dismissed the cause. Nearly six years after the incident, appellant brought suit in state court, alleging that the taking of the samples violated state law. The trial court granted appellees' motion for summary judgment without specifying a basis, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment, holding that the acts complained of in appellant's complaint filed after the summary judgment motion were essentially unchanged from those alleged before, and that the federal-court dismissal, which was not based on lack of jurisdiction, did not toll the running of limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to appellees, city and police officer, in appellant arrestee's suit claiming damages for injuries suffered while he was incarcerated, because the grounds considered in the summary judgment motion encompassed those raised in appellant's later petition and dismissal of appellant's federal claim had not tolled the running of limitations.

KTRK TV, Inc. v. Fowkes


NO. 01-96-01290-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


981 S.W.2d 779; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 6399



September 30, 1998, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied April 1, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-47773. Hon. Scott Link, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered for media defendants.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, television station and reporter, sought interlocutory review of the partial denial of their motion for summary judgment by the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas) in an action brought by appellees, city employee and wife, for libel, tortious interference with an employment contract, emotional distress, and negligence. Appellees also sought review of the partial grant of summary judgment in appellants' favor.


OVERVIEW: Appellant reporter aired a story suggesting that appellee, a city employee, withheld information during an investigation of a city department and that the department reassigned him as a result. Appellees, manager and his wife, filed suit against appellants, reporter and television station, for libel, tortious interference with an employment contract, intentional infliction of emotional distress, and negligence. Appellants sought interlocutory review of the partial grant of its summary judgment motion. Over appellees objection, the court held that Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 51.014(6), which provided for interlocutory appeals for media defendants in libel cases, was constitutional. The court declined jurisdiction over appellees request for review of the dismissal of their emotional distress claim, as it did not fall within § 51.014(6). The court reversed the denial of appellants' summary judgment motion as to the libel and tortious interference claims because the claims fell within § 51.014(6), appellant reporter's story was substantially true, and appellee manager did not suffer an adverse employment action sufficient to support a tortious interference claim.


OUTCOME: The court granted interlocutory review and reversed the partial denial of the summary judgment motion brought by appellants, television station and reporter, because the allegedly libelous story about appellee manager was substantially true and appellee manager did not suffer sufficient harm to sustain a tortious interference claim. The court declined jurisdiction over appellees' cross-appeal and remanded for further proceedings.

Jackson v. State


NO. 07-97-0239-CR, NO. 07-97-0240-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5931



September 23, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 3, 1999. Appellant's Motions for Rehearing Overuled October 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 64TH DISTRICT COURT OF HALE COUNTY; NOS. B12,341-9604 & A12,544-9611; HONORABLE JACK R. MILLER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his convictions in the 64th District Court of Hale County, Texas, for driving while intoxicated, each enhanced by a prior felony conviction. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in not affording him a competency hearing, that he was denied effective assistance of counsel, that one of his cases was improperly transferred, and that his sentences were improperly enhanced.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his convictions for driving while intoxicated, each enhanced by a prior felony conviction. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to conduct a competency hearing before accepting appellant's guilty pleas. The trial court had inquired into appellant's competency, and appellant's counsel stated that appellant was competent to stand trial, therefore, nothing was preserved for appellate review. The court also held that appellant's counsel's conduct did not fall below an objective standard of reasonableness, and appellant failed to establish that absent counsel's errors, he would not have pled guilty. Appellant contended that the indictment underlying his prior felony conviction was defective and therefore, his current convictions were improperly enhanced by the use thereof. The court held that because the indictment alleged with reasonable certainty the reckless act relied upon, it was not defective. Further, the court held that when the judge in one district court mistakenly believed that he was disqualified from hearing appellant's case, his transfer of the case was not improper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for driving while intoxicated, each enhanced by a prior felony conviction. The court found that the trial judge did not improperly transfer the case, appellant's counsel was not ineffective, the trial court did not err in not affording appellant a competency hearing before accepting his guilty pleas, and the indictments underlying his prior felonies were not fundamentally defective.

Jackson v. State


NO. 07-97-0470-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5934



September 23, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 137TH DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 96-421894; HONORABLE CECIL G. PURYEAR, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the 137th District Court of Lubbock County, (Texas) for unlawfully carrying a weapon in a prohibited place.


OVERVIEW: Appellant walked onto school grounds and was noted by the principal as having a rifle with him. The principal was able to obtain the rifle and appellant was wrestled to the ground by two other school officials. Appellant was convicted of unlawfully carrying a weapon in a prohibited place. Appellant contended that the trial court erred when it overruled his motion to quash the indictment and that the trial court gave an incorrect definition of premises in the guilt innocence jury charge. The court determined that the indictment against appellant was not so vague as to hinder appellant's defense. The court found that pursuant to Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 311.011(a) words like premises were to be read in context and construed according to the rules of grammar and common usage. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and sentence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction having determined that the indictment alleged that appellant intentionally carried a firearm onto the grounds of a specific school and that there was no reversible error as the result of the definition of premises in the jury charge.

 

633 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Marcum v. State


NO. 14-96-01567-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


983 S.W.2d 762; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5865



September 17, 1998, Rendered  
September 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 185th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 579,561.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the revocation of his probation in the 185th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which was imposed upon his conviction of the charge of sexual assault of a child pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1987). Defendant was to serve his original 10 year prison sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the trial court's revocation of his probation imposed upon his conviction of sexual assault of an child, pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.021 (1987), and reimposition of his 10 year prison sentence. Defendant asserted that it was error to admit statements made during a polygraph test and to admit his statements in violation of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 38.22 (1997). Defendant argued that it was an abuse of discretion to revoke his probation, and dismiss his motion to quash the state's motion to revoke his probation. On appeal, the court affirmed and found that defendant's statements made to a polygraph examiner were voluntary and not the results of a polygraph test, and that there was no violation of statute because while defendant had to undergo a polygraph exam as a condition of his probation, there was no custodial interrogation. The court found no abuse of discretion in the revocation of defendant's probation because proof of one violation was sufficient to revoke probation. The court held that it was not unreasonable to require defendant to stay away from persons below age 17, and complainants were known to defendant.


OUTCOME: A revocation of defendant's probation and a reimposition of a 10 year prison sentence was affirmed because statements made to a polygraph examiner were voluntary, because although defendant was required to take a polygraph, it was not a custodial interrogation, and revocation was not an abuse of discretion where defendant violated a condition, and because the conditions of probation were not unreasonable and defendant knew the complainants.

 

634 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re C.E.M.


NO. 01-97-00729-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


981 S.W.2d 771; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5866



September 17, 1998, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 315th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-00858J.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of a judgment of the 315th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which found that appellant had engaged in delinquent conduct by committing the state jail felony offense of possession of cocaine weighing less than one gram and ordered the suspension of appellant's driver's license for 36 months, pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code § 54.042(a)(1) (1996).


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that appellant juvenile had engaged in delinquent conduct by committing the state jail felony offense of possession of cocaine weighing less than one gram, and the trial court placed appellant on probation for nine months in the custody of his mother. The trial court ordered the suspension of appellant's driver's license for 36 months and ordered appellant to participate in a drug counseling and tutoring program, to maintain a minimum C average in school, and to complete 20 hours of community service. The appeals court reversed that part of the order that suspended appellant's driver's license pursuant to Tex. Transp. Code § 521.342 (1998), holding that the code applied to misdemeanor offenses and was not applicable to appellant's felony conviction. Accordingly, Tex. Fam. Code § 54.042(a)(1) (1996) did not apply and the trial court erroneously suspended appellant's driver's license. The court concluded that the suspension of the driver's license was void. The action was remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that part of the district court's order that ordered the suspension of appellant's driver's license for 36 months, holding that the applicable statute applied to misdemeanor offenses and was not applicable to appellant's felony conviction. The suspension of the driver's license was void. The court affirmed the judgment that found juvenile had engaged in delinquent conduct by committing the state jail felony offense.

Jackson v. Golden Eagle Archery


NO. 09-96-302 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


974 S.W.2d 952; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5886


January 29, 1998, Submitted  
September 17, 1998, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Granted January 7, 1999.
Petition for review granted by, 01/07/1999
Reversed by, Remanded by Golden Eagle Archery, Inc. v. Jackson, 24 S.W.3d 362, 2000 Tex. LEXIS 74, 43 Tex. Sup. Ct. J. 989 (Tex., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the 136th Judicial District Court Jefferson County, Texas Trial Cause No. D-145,418. Honorable Milton Gunn Shuffield, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff sought review of an inadequate jury award for damages from the 136th Judicial District Court Jefferson County (Texas) in plaintiff's trial seeking compensation for permanent eye and head injuries caused by an archer's bow made by defendant.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff challenged as inadequate the jury's award of damages for severe personal injuries plaintiff suffered in a bow accident. On appeal, the court held that during voir dire, a juror blatantly failed to reveal under questioning by plaintiff's counsel that she was biased against personal injury claimants. However, the juror's bias, which she freely expressed to other jurors during trial and jury deliberations, was not reversible error under Tex. R. Civ. P. 327 or Tex. R. Evid. 606(b) because the testimony and affidavits other jurors were not admissible to prove that the biased juror was incompetent to serve on the jury. However, the court held that the biased juror's misconduct prevented plaintiff from receiving a fair trial as guaranteed by Tex. Const. art. I, § 15. Therefore, Tex. R. Civ. P. 327(b), which prevented impeachment of the jury verdict based on evidence emanating from jury deliberations rather than outside influence, was unconstitutional. The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the jury's damage award and remanded for a new personal injury trial. A state procedural rule that prevented plaintiff from using other jurors' testimony and affidavits to show that a biased juror had harmed plaintiff's chances for a more favorable damage award was unconstitutional because the rule abrogated the state constitution's guarantee of a fair trial.
