Lott v. Bexar County Sheriff's Dep't


No. 04-97-00088-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5805



September 16, 1998, Delivered  
September 16, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 225th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95-CI-17758. Honorable Henry Schuble, Judge Presiding. 1


1 The Honorable Henry Schuble, sitting by assignment, presided over the hearing and orally rejected Lott's constitutional challenge and affirmed the suspension; the judgment was signed by the Honorable Andy Mireles, Judge of the 73rd Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sheriff's deputy sought review of the 225th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), which upheld appellant's suspension without pay imposed by appellee county sheriff's civil service commission. Appellant was suspended after an inmate escaped from his custody. Appellant contended that appellee's rules were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the ruling of the trial court, which approved of the decision by appellee county sheriff's civil Service commission to suspend appellant sheriff's deputy following an incident in which an inmate escaped from appellant's custody. Appellant contended that Bexar County Sheriff's Department Civil Service Commission, Texas, R. 11.07, which was enacted pursuant to Tex. Loc. Gov't. Code Ann. § 158.035(a)(5) (1998), was an unconstitutional violation of his property right under U.S. Const. amend. XIV because R. 11.07 placed on appellant, the burden of proving that an adverse action by the sheriff's department should not be upheld. The court disagreed with appellant and held that in light of Bexar County Sheriff's Department Civil Service Commission, Texas, R. 11.10, which required that the sheriff's department present its case first at a review hearing, that R. 11.07 did not place an unconstitutional burden of production on a disciplined employee. The court held that appellee's action could be supported because appellant failed to meet a burden of persuasion and not an unconstitutional burden of production.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of appellee Bexar County Sheriff's Department Civil Service Commission to suspend appellant sheriff's deputy for sixty days without pay. The court held that the decision was based on the fact that appellant did not meet his burden of persuasion and not a burden of production that was of questionable constitutionality.

Huff ex rel. Harrison v. Lomba


NO. 09-97-095 CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5715


June 18, 1998, Submitted  
September 10, 1998, Opinion Delivered


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled October 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 217th District Court. Angelina County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 28909-95-9.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, mother of decedent, on behalf of decedent's heirs sought review of an order by the 217th District Court, Angelina County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee dentist in a case arising out of appellee's purported negligent treatment of decedent prior to his death from cancer.


OVERVIEW: Appellee dentist treated decedent prior to his death. Appellant, mother of decedent, on behalf of decedent's heirs contended that appellee misdiagnosed lumps in decedent's mouth and a lesion on his lip by not determining that they were cancerous. Appellee filed a motion for partial summary judgment with respect to medical negligence based upon the two-year statute of limitations as provided in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (1998). The limitations period began to run on the last day of appellee's treatment of the decedent and no claim was filed until well after the expiration of the limitations period. Decedent learned of the misdiagnosis six months before the end of the limitations period. The court further found upon the open courts provision of the Texas Constitution that decedent did not bring his claim within a reasonable time after discovery of facts sufficient to put him on notice of the claim. The court remanded appellant's claim for intentional infliction of emotional distress because there was a fact issue as to whether appellee added the entry of a missed appointment in order to demonstrate contributory negligence on the part of the decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part. The court held that decedent was barred by the two-year statute of limitations from bringing a cause of action for medical negligence, but that there was a fact issue pertaining to appellee's possible intentional infliction of emotional distress claim that required remand for trial.

Neuland v. State


NO. 01-97-00590-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5843



September 10, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 10. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9702661.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his Criminal Court of Harris County (Texas) conviction for driving while intoxicated, alleging the trial court erred by denying his motions to suppress because the stipulated evidence was too conclusory to establish probable cause for his arrest.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted appellant for driving while intoxicated. Appellant sought review, alleging the trial court erred by denying his motions to suppress a breath test and other sobriety tests because the stipulated evidence was too conclusory to establish probable cause for his arrest. The court affirmed, first holding that evidence that appellant disregarded a red light gave police sufficient authority to stop and investigate pursuant to Tex. Transp. Code Ann. §§ 543.001, .004 (1998). Furthermore, appellant smelled strongly of alcohol, and his speech was slurred. Appellant had also argued that his stipulation was so detailed that no inferences or deductions could properly be drawn from it, under the "agreed case" doctrine utilized in civil cases. The court, however, rejected the agreed case analysis for a criminal case.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated was affirmed because the stipulated evidence and reasonable inferences therefrom were sufficient to support a finding of probable cause for his arrest.

City of Manvel v. Tholen


NO. 14-97-01014-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5676



September 3, 1998, Judgment Rendered  
September 3, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 239th District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96G2656.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant municipality challenged a ruling of the 239th District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, which granted appellee lion owners a permanent injunction and enjoined the enforcement of a city ordinance against them, and granted appellees attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee lion owners moved to a new city, and one month later appellant municipality passed an ordinance which prohibited the keeping of pet lions. Appellees sought a permanent injunction to enjoin the enforcement of the ordinance against them. Appellees claimed the ordinance constituted an ex post facto law as applied to them and that appellant lacked authority to pass the ordinance, which deemed pet lions a nuisance per se. The trial court found for appellees and granted injunctive relief. The court also awarded appellees attorney's fees. Appellant challenged the trial court ruling, and the court reversed. The court held that the ordinance at issue, which did not punish or increase the punishment for acts previously committed, but only attempted to prevent future actions, was not an ex post facto law. The court held that appellant was justified when it declared pet lions a nuisance per se, and therefore had the authority to do so, where the evidence showed that lions posed a threat to humans. Because the trial court lacked a basis upon which to grant injunctive relief, the court reversed the trial court ruling and ordered that appellees take nothing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court ruling, which granted a permanent injunction and attorney's fees to appellees, who owned a pet lion. The court held that appellant municipalities' ordinance was not an ex post facto law where it did not punish prior actions and that appellant had the authority to deem a dangerous animal a nuisance per se.

City of Fort Worth v. Zimlich


NO. 03-97-00475-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


975 S.W.2d 399; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5489; 14 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 486



August 31, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand May 17, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 3164.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 201ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-08668, HONORABLE MARY PEARL WILLIAMS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city employer sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Travis County, 201st Judicial District (Texas), in favor of appellee employee where the jury found retaliatory discrimination in violation of the Whistleblower Act, 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 583, 609-11, amended by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 554.001- 554.009, and awarded future lost earnings, mental anguish, and punitive damages. Eleven points of error were brought.


OVERVIEW: Appellee employee was a peace officer who took a promotional position in policing illegal environmental dumping. In response to investigating and reporting an illegal disposal site owned by a former city official, appellee's reputable career deteriorated, he received his first disciplinary action in fourteen years of work, and was demoted. Appellee filed suit against appellant city employer for retaliatory discrimination under the Whistleblower Act, 1993 Tex. Gen. Laws 583, 609-11 (amended by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 554.001- 554.009). A jury returned a verdict for appellee. The court affirmed the judgment reviewing 11 points of error, holding the pleadings and evidence were factually and legally sufficient. An inference of reasonable cause supported discrimination when appellee's protected report was filed on illegal dumping in good faith. Exemplary or punitive damages, mental anguish damages, and future lost earning damages, were proper where sufficient evidence supported the awards, proper calculation was made, and the amounts were not excessive. A motion for change of venue was properly denied weighing the interests of the parties for a fair trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for retaliatory discrimination as a peace officer under the Whistleblower Act, favoring appellee employee, against appellant city employer. Eleven points of error were overruled including claims of improper lost earnings, mental anguish, and punitive damages, insufficient evidence, no discrimination causation, and denial of venue change.

Voegtlin v. Perryman


NO. 2-97-047-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


977 S.W.2d 806; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5351



August 27, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 342ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant victim challenged the order of the 342nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which dismissed appellant's claim for medical malpractice against appellee doctor because the suit was filed after the two-year statute of limitation set forth in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01.


OVERVIEW: Appellant victim filed suit against appellee doctor for medical malpractice. The trial court dismissed the suit on summary judgment because the cause of action was barred by the two-year statute of limitations set forth in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01. The court affirmed the dismissal and held that appellant knew of the injury, had a reasonable opportunity to bring suit within the statutory period, and failed to do so. The court held that appellee negligently failed to recognize appellant's cancer for the final time more than two years prior to the filing of the suit. The court held that appellant knew of the facts giving rise to her cause of action and should have known that she had a cause of action prior to the running of the statute of limitations. The court held that no issue of material fact existed as to whether appellant discovered or could have discovered the injury and brought suit within the statutory period. The court held that the statute of limitations was not unconstitutional; as a matter of law, appellant failed to file suit within a reasonable time after discovering the injury and thus was not entitled to relief under the open courts provision.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that dismissed appellant victim's suit for medical malpractice against appellee doctor. Appellant knew of the injury, had a reasonable opportunity to bring suit within the statutory period, and failed to do so. Appellant failed to file suit within a reasonable time after discovering the injury and thus was not entitled to relief under the open courts provision.

Fargo v. State


No. 05-95-01593-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5358



August 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 204th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F94-18147-WQ.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the jury verdict of the 204th Judicial District Court of Dallas County, Texas, which convicted appellant of felony driving while intoxicated and assessed an eight-year sentence and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and convicted of driving while intoxicated (DWI), but contended several points of error in the trial court's admission of evidence. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence because the officer's decision to pull his car over was unconstitutional. The court held that the officer had a reasonable suspicion to justify a Terry stop from the totality of the circumstances. There was reasonable suspicion because appellant's vehicle was weaving back and forth in its lane. Appellant also contended that the trial court abused its discretion in overruling his objections to admission of an "intoxication video," which filmed appellant taking field sobriety tests at the police station following his arrest. The court held that a trial court had broad discretion to admit the videotape over an objection to the video's quality and that videos were admissible under Tex. R. Crim. Evid. 901, 1001(2). An observing officer properly authenticated the video. Additionally, the audio portion of the videotape was admissible because appellant had been properly advised of his Miranda rights before the custodial interrogation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the jury verdict of felony driving while intoxicated and appellant's sentence and fine. The officer had reasonable suspicion to justify a Terry stop from the totality of the circumstances and evidence regarding an intoxication video and audio was properly admitted under the trial court judge's discretion.

Loya v. State


NUMBER 13-97-785-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5375



August 27, 1998, Delivered  
August 27, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 28, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 156th District Court of Bee County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed for want of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 156th District Court, Bee County (Texas), which adjudicated him guilty of aggravated kidnapping pursuant to a guilty plea, imposed incarceration, and revoked his community supervision.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to aggravated kidnapping under a plea agreement that adjudication be deferred with community supervision. Appellant violated his supervision and after pleading true to the assertions in the state's motion to adjudicate his guilt, he was found guilty and incarcerated. The court dismissed the appeal and found that it had no jurisdiction to review appellant's argument regarding his indictment because it was not raised under Tex. R. App. P. 25.2(b)(3); that the court could not consider appellant's claim of the unconstitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12(5)(b) because the right to appeal a criminal conviction was given only by the legislature and that the article prohibits an appeal from the determination of guilt; that the court could not consider appellant's equal protection claim as the right to appeal did not create a suspect class or infringe on a fundamental right; and that appellant was prohibited by statute from appealing any errors at his hearing on the state's motion to adjudicate his guilt.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal for want of jurisdiction because appellant could not appeal any claims regarding his indictment, the unconstitutionality of the criminal code provision prohibiting an appeal of his criminal conviction, his alleged denial of equal protection, or any errors that took place at the hearing to adjudicate his guilt.

 

645 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Lowery v. State


No. 05-95-01793-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


974 S.W.2d 936; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5434



August 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 194th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F95-03032-UM.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 194th Judicial District Court of Dallas County (Texas) that convicted and sentenced appellant for indecency with a child, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1) (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for indecency with a child. After finding appellant guilty, the trial court sentenced appellant to prison. The appeals court reversed, holding that the denial of appellant's right to a jury trial was a constitutional structural error and not subject to a harm analysis. Thus, the error was harmful. The right to a jury trial at the guilt stage was both a statutory right and a constitutional right, pursuant to U.S. Const. art. III, § 2 & amend. VI; Tex. Const. art. I, § 15; and Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.12 (1977). The right could not be relinquished, except by an express waiver. As appellant did not waive his right to a jury trial, the conviction and sentence were reversed and the action was remanded. The court affirmed that part of the judgment which found that the facts asserted in the indictment were a violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 21.11(a)(1) (1994). The testimony established that appellant committed the charged offense prior to and within 10 years of the presentment of the indictment and was sufficient to support appellant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a judgment of the district court that convicted and sentenced appellant for indecency with a child, holding that the denial of appellant's right to a jury trial was a constitutional structural error and not subject to a harm analysis. Thus, the error was harmful. The action was remanded.

In re Jones


NO. 07-98-0283-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


978 S.W.2d 648; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5354



August 26, 1998, Decided



DISPOSITION:  [**1] Relator's petition denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Relator filed a writ of mandamus to compel respondent political party chairman to remove a candidate's name from an election ballot because that candidate did not satisfy the requirements of Tex. Gov't Code Ann. 25.0014(3) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Candidate's license to practice law was placed in inactive status. Candidate applied to return to active status on June 14, 1989 and resumed the practice of law in September 1994. She was reinstated to practice law on November 18, 1994. On March 10, 1998, candidate won a nomination to run for a judicial position. Relator candidate filed a request for a writ of mandamus to compel respondent political party chairman to remove candidate's name from the ballot because she did not practice law for four years before the election, as required by Tex. Gov't Code Ann. 25.0014(3) (1998). The court had jurisdiction under Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 273.061 (1986). Relator had standing because he was a candidate for the same election and he had an interest in not being opposed by an ineligible candidate. The court held that candidate returned to active status when her application and fees were received, which was a question of fact. The court could not grant mandamus relief because such relief was only available when the law clearly spelled out a duty to perform, and there was no clear duty because it was not established when candidate returned to active status.


OUTCOME: The court denied relator's request for a writ of mandamus because such relief was only available when the law clearly spelled out a duty to be performed. Because a question of fact existed as to whether a candidate satisfied all of the requirements before she could run for office, the court could not order mandamus relief.

 

647 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Laura T. v. Baylor Univ. Med. Ctr.


No. 05-96-01505-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5238



August 21, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 192nd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-13077-K.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient appealed a decision of the 192nd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) granting summary judgment in favor of defendant health care providers in plaintiff's suit alleging fraud, false imprisonment, battery, negligence, gross negligence, negligence per se, deceptive trade practices, invasion of privacy, intentional infliction of emotional distress, negligent misrepresentation, and conspiracy.


OVERVIEW: As a minor, plaintiff was hospitalized for psychiatric treatment under the care of defendant health care providers. Following her release she brought a malpractice suit alleging numerous claims related thereto. Defendants filed motions for summary judgment on the basis of limitations, which the trial court granted. After plaintiff nonsuited her fraud claim, the trial court entered final judgment ordering plaintiff take nothing against defendants. Plaintiff appealed and the court affirmed. The court concluded that she was required to bring suit on or before her twentieth birthday and thus, unless an exception to the statute of limitations applied, her claims were barred by limitations. The court found that because her injuries were not inherently undiscoverable, the discovery rule did not apply to her claims as a matter of law. The court also found that she could not rely on the doctrine of fraudulent concealment to defeat defendants' limitations claim. Finally, the court concluded that the evidence relied on by plaintiff was not sufficient to raise a fact issue as to whether the unsound mind doctrine applied to toll limitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in defendant health care providers' favor because under the applicable statute of limitations, absent an exception, plaintiff patient was required to bring suit on or before her twentieth birthday. Plaintiff failed to demonstrate that the discovery rule, the doctrine of fraudulent concealment, and the unsound mind doctrine defeated defendants' limitations claim.

Sisto Mirando Cuero v. State


NOS. 01-96-01340-CR 01-96-01341-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5182



August 20, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 230th District Court. Harris County, Texas Trial Court Cause Nos. 679,090 & 679,091.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pleaded guilty to delivery of a controlled substance and no contest to aggravated robbery and received; the 230th District Court, Harris County, Texas, sentenced him to confinement. The sentences were to run concurrently. Appellant alleged that Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 1.15 (Supp. 1998) was unconstitutional, fundamental error was committed, and the sentences constituted cruel and unusual punishment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded guilty to the delivery of a controlled substance, and the trial court assessed punishment of confinement. Appellant also pleaded no contest to aggravated robbery and the trial court assessed punishment of confinement. The two sentences were to run concurrently. The court affirmed. Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 1.15 (1998) was unconstitutional, because it denied appellant the right to compulsory process. The court considered and rejected the contention in a previous case. Appellant also contended that the trial court committed fundamental error by accepting his plea when the record was silent about whether he waived his right to compulsory process. However, there was no requirement that appellant specifically waive his right, so the court overruled that point of error. Appellant additionally contended that the sentences constituted cruel and unusual punishment. Appellant had not objected at the sentencing hearing nor had he filed a motion for new trial. Therefore, appellant waived these points of error. The court affirmed the judgments.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the district court convicting and sentencing appellant for delivery of a controlled substance and aggravated robbery were affirmed. The court previously rejected the contention that the applicable statute was unconstitutional. Fundamental error was not committed, as appellant need not waive his right to compulsory process in order for the trial court to accept his plea.

Moore v. State


NOS. 01-97-00631-CR, 01-97-00632-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


981 S.W.2d 701; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5396



August 20, 1998, Date of Opinion  
August 20, 1998, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of June 11, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3610.

On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 97-03541, 97-07342. Hon. J. Hughes, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a motion for rehearing, defendant appealed his conviction from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15, Harris County (Texas) for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped twice for routine traffic violations. Each time he was arrested for DWI and he refused to perform a breath test. At trial, he filed pretrial motions to suppress his refusals to take breath tests and all evidence arising out of his initial stops, and to declare Tex. Transp. Code § 724.061 unconstitutional. The trial court denied the motions, except it suppressed the audio portion of the video of his first arrest. Defendant then pled no contest to both charges of misdemeanor DWI. Defendant appealed, asserting error as to the trial court's denial of his pretrial motions. The court affirmed. The court found the warnings defendant received substantially complied with the language and purpose of the statute. Finally, the court held that the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The court overruled defendant's motion for rehearing, withdrew its earlier opinion, and affirmed defendant's conviction. The court found that defendant's contentions as to the suppression of the breath tests and evidence obtained during the initial traffic stop lacked merit as did his argument regarding the constitutionality of the transportation statute making certain testimony concerning breathalyzer tests admissible.

Neeble v. Sepulveda


NO. 01-96-01253-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4970



August 13, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled July 29, 1999. Opinion on Motion for Rehearing Denied January 14, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tex. App. LEXIS 266. As Amended January 14, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-054308.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a judgment of the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which ruled in favor of appellee doctors and granted appellee hospital a directed verdict. Appellant alleged negligence and lack of actual consent as to appellee doctors and negligent credentialing as to appellee hospital with respect to two of four surgeries.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient fell in a bathtub, injured his back, underwent surgery, and subsequently re-injured his back in three other incidents. Appellant underwent four surgeries. At trial, a doctor testified that appellant's condition had improved as a result of the four surgeries. Appellant sued as to the last two surgeries. The trial court bifurcated the negligence claims against appellee doctors from the negligent credentialing claims against appellee hospital. The jury found for appellee doctors and the trial court granted appellee hospital a directed verdict. The court held that a physician's failure to disclose was not a cause of a patient's injury if the patient was not injured by the risk of which he was not informed. The court held that the trial court properly severed the actions because trying both claims simultaneously would have prejudiced appellee doctors. Character evidence admissible in appellee hospital's defense was inadmissible as to appellee doctors. The trial court properly overruled appellant's objection to a new and independent cause jury instruction because there was evidence in the record that the additional surgeries were not caused by appellee doctor's actions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of appellee doctors and the directed verdict in favor of appellee hospital. The court held that even if appellant had rebutted the statutory presumption of disclosure, appellant had not experienced any injury from the risks that he contended should have been disclosed. A directed verdict as to appellee hospital was appropriate because appellee hospital's liability was derivative of appellee doctors.

Grocers Supply Co. v. Sharp


NO. 03-97-00749-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


978 S.W.2d 638; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 5030



August 13, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied February 18, 1999. As Corrected January 4, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 261ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-13035, HONORABLE MARGARET COOPER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grocery company challenged a decision of the District Court of Travis County, 261st Judicial District (Texas), which ruled in favor of appellee comptroller and denied appellant's request for a refund of sales taxes paid under a two-party contract pursuant to appellee's adoption of the judicial interpretation of 1961 Tex. Gen. Laws 71, 84.


OVERVIEW: Appellant grocery company filed a tax refund claim with appellee comptroller for sales taxes paid to the power company. Appellant had a two-party contract with the power company. Appellee based the claim on two new exemptions enacted in 1987 and 1990. A previous exemption under 1961 Tex. Gen. Laws 71, 84 contained language almost identical to the new exemptions. The 1961 exemption was judicially interpreted as applying only to prior three-party contracts. Appellee initially followed the judicial interpretation. Appellee later permitted two-party contract exemptions, and appellant filed the claim. Appellee then readopted the judicial interpretation, and the claim was denied. Appellant exhausted the administrative remedies. The trial court ruled for appellee. Appellant sought review, but the court affirmed the trial court. Appellee did not contravene its prior rule, rather it changed the prior unwritten policy. There was no unconstitutional retroactive application because the interpretation had not created a vested right. The legislative acceptance doctrine did not apply. All taxpayers were treated equally and the classification was rational under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 1(a).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that ruled in favor of appellee comptroller and denied appellant grocery company's request for a refund of sales taxes paid under a two-party contract because the comptroller only changed the prior unwritten policy, the change was not unconstitutionally retroactive since there was no vested right, the legislative acceptance doctrine did not apply, and all taxpayers were treated equally.

Shelby Operating Co. v. Miller


No. 06-98-00018-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4792


July 16, 1998, Submitted  
August 7, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied January 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 71st Judicial District Court. Harrison County, Texas. Trial Court No. 97-0837.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant drilling company challenged the judgment of the 71st Judicial District Court, Harrison County (Texas), which granted appellee property owners' request for injunctive relief to prevent appellant from drilling a well within 500 feet of their residence, pursuant to Waskom, Tex., Ordinance No. 96, § A-2(a) (as amended), awarded appellees damages plus attorney fees, and denied appellant's request for declaratory and injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: Appellee property owners sued to enjoin appellant drilling company from drilling a well within 500 feet of their buildings. They also sought damages resulting from work that appellant already had done at the well site. The trial court found that appellant had violated Waskom, Tex., Ordinance No. 96, § A-2(a), as amended, awarded appellees damages plus attorney fees, granted appellees' request for a permanent injunction, denied appellant's requested declaratory and injunctive relief, and held that oil well operations within 500 feet of buildings and residences endangered the public. Appellant challenged the judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed. By enacting the amended ordinance, the city, pursuant to its police power, created a valid restriction on appellant's rights under the original gas lease, which allowed drilling operations within 200 feet of existing buildings. The denial of appellant's request for a drilling permit did not involve a retroactive application of the amended ordinance, which was valid. Appellees' pleading sufficiently stated claims for trespass and conversion. Appellees' failure to segregate the fees did not prevent them from recovering the entire amount.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which granted appellee property owners' request for permanent injunctive relief to prevent appellant drilling company from drilling a well within 500 feet of their buildings, awarded appellees damages plus attorney fees, and denied appellant's request for declaratory and injunctive relief. The challenged amended ordinance was a valid exercise of the city's police property.

Dunn v. State


NO. 07-98-0126-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4766



August 5, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 297TH DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY; NO. 0601684A; HONORABLE EVERETT YOUNG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 29th District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which revoked appellant's probation and denied him credit for time served in jail from the date of his arrest for probation violation until his probation revocation hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for delivery of a controlled substance. He was sentenced to 180 days imprisonment was placed on probation for two years. When appellant violated two conditions of his probation, he was arrested and confined to jail. After a hearing, the trial court revoked appellant's probation and sentenced him to 180 days imprisonment. The trial court declined to award credit for time served from the date of appellant's arrest for probation violation until his hearing on the matter. On appeal, the state conceded that the trial court abused its discretion in denying appellant credit for time served, but the state disagreed with appellant regarding the number of days to be credited. The court concluded that appellant was entitled to credit for any time served pursuant to the execution of a pre-revocation warrant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as modified. The trial court abused its discretion in denying appellant credit for time served, because appellant was entitled to credit for any time served pursuant to the execution of a pre-revocation warrant.

In re Marriage of Hale


No. 06-98-00013-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


975 S.W.2d 694; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4684


July 16, 1998, Submitted  
July 31, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 5th Judicial District Court. Cass County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-D-647.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of the decision of the 5th Judicial District Court, Cass County (Texas), which awarded appellee ex-wife post divorce spousal maintenance for three years, in appellant's action for divorce.


OVERVIEW: Appellant ex-husband was ordered to pay appellee ex-wife post divorce spousal support for a period of three years. Appellant argued that the lower court abused its discretion because the evidence was legally and factually insufficient to support the court's decision. The court affirmed and stated that viewing all the circumstances of ex-wife's limited earning capacity and lack of education supported an order by the lower court for spousal maintenance. The court stated that an order for spousal maintenance was similar to an award of child support and would only be reversed upon a showing of abuse of discretion. The court further stated that the minimum reasonable needs was not defined in the federal minimum wage statute and thus was a fact specific determination that should be made by the trial court. The court refused to address appellant's argument regarding the unconstitutionality of the maintenance statute because appellant did not raise the argument in the lower court.


OUTCOME: Judgment awarding appellee ex-wife post divorce spousal maintenance affirmed because the lower court did not abuse its discretion where there was some probative and substantive evidence to support the award.

Slaughter v. State


No. 05-96-01113-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4699



July 31, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 1. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MB92-65711-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the County Criminal Court No. 1, Dallas County, Texas, which convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated and sentenced him to probation and a fine.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped after an officer followed him for approximately one mile and observed appellant weaving the entire time. After the stop, the officer gave field sobriety tests and then waited for another patrol car with a video camera, and administered further tests. The videotapes were admitted at trial, despite motions to suppress. Following his conviction for driving while intoxicated appellant sought review. On appeal the court affirmed, holding first that the officer required reasonable suspicion, rather than probable cause, to stop appellant and the officer's experience and observation satisfied this requirement, and no violation of statute was needed. The court also held that warnings under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. § 38.22 applied only to custodial arrests, and the video was taken before arrest. Finally, the court held that the trial court's failure to allow defense counsel more time to read a police report did not have a substantial and injurious effect on the verdict as appellant's attorney had ample time to read the report at subsequent recesses and examine the officer who wrote it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant defendant's conviction of driving while intoxicated because an officer had the necessary reasonable suspicion to stop appellant based on experience and a mile of observed weaving, video was properly taken before custodial rights adhered, and appellant's counsel had ample time to read a police report and examine the author after allowing counsel only five minutes to initially read it.

Alvarez v. State


NO. 03-97-00438-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4608



July 30, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR-94-0151, HONORABLE CHARLES R. RAMSAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order by the District Court for the District of Hays County, 22nd Judicial District (Texas), which revoked probation due to appellant's failure to comply with the conditions of his probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of an order revoking his probation for the sexual assault of a child. Appellant contended that the enactment of a new law provided him with an affirmative defense to the underlying charge. The court stated that the record contained no facts to support the applicability of the new law to appellant's case. The court found that the revocation was properly based on evidence that appellant had violated several conditions of his probation including the failure to pay required fees and his failure to participate in a mandatory sex offender treatment program. However, the court also found that the community service obligation that had been imposed on appellant was unenforceable because it failed to specify when or how he was to complete his community service hours. The court ruled that the unenforceability of the community service condition did not prevent the revocation of appellant's probation because proof of appellant's violation of any one of the valid probation conditions was sufficient to support an order of revocation. Therefore, the court affirmed the trial court's order revoking appellant's probation.


OUTCOME: The judgment revoking appellant's probation was affirmed because proof that appellant had violated even one of the conditions of his probation was sufficient to support an order of revocation.

Crumpton v. State


NO. 2-96-390-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


977 S.W.2d 763; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4686



July 30, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE 158TH DISTRICT COURT OF DENTON COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the 158th District Court of Denton County (Texas), which convicted and sentenced appellant of the felony offense of engaging in organized criminal activity predicated on theft. Appellant contended that the statute under which he was convicted was facially unconstitutional in that it violated the double jeopardy clause of the U.S. Const. amend. V.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a plea bargain agreement, appellant convict entered a plea of guilty to the felony offense of engaging in organized criminal activity pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02, the predicate offense was theft. Appellant challenged the judgment contending that the Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02 was facially unconstitutional as it authorized multiple punishments for the same offense in violation of U.S. Const. amend. V, the double jeopardy clause. Although appellant had not raised the double jeopardy issue in the trial court, the court heard the appeal as it found that it would have been an injustice to apply the new appellate rules and as appellant was contending that the statute was facially unconstitutional. The court determined that the statute had not violated the double jeopardy clause as the legislature intended that each violation was a separate offense. Thus, appellant could be charged for both the theft offense and the offense of engaging in organized criminal activity, predicated on theft. Accordingly, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted appellant of the felony offense of engaging in organized criminal activity predicated on theft as appellant's conviction had not violated the double jeopardy clause.

Brown v. Commission for Lawyer Discipline


No. 04-96-00398-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


980 S.W.2d 675; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4581



July 29, 1998, Delivered  
July 29, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 37th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 94-CI-06941. Honorable John R. Carter, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AS REFORMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney challenged the judgment form the 37th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas, which found that he had violated two rules of professional conduct, suspended him from the practice of law, and ordered him to pay attorneys fees to appellee, Commission for Lawyer Discipline.


OVERVIEW: After a non jury trial, the trial court determined that appellant attorney had violated the Tex. Disciplinary R. Prof. Conduct, 1.14(c)and 8.04(a)(3) and suspended him and ordered him to pay attorney fees to appellees, the Commission for Lawyer Discipline. The court found that the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support fining that appellant had violated both rules. Appellant had deposited settlement funds into a joint account which he used for personal expenses without consent of the client and as the deposited funds were to be used for other litigation, instead of the payment of medical fees which he had promised the client's medical providers. Rules were not unconstitutionally vague, as a lawyer of common intelligence would have realized that the use of the misleading letters of protection and use of settlement funds for personal expenses demonstrated a lack of probity, integrity, and straight forwardness. As the reference to the repealed rule was a clerical error in the judgment, the court exercised its authority to correct the error. Thus, the court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment as the evidence was legally and factually sufficient to support the findings that appellant attorney violated the rules of professional conduct. The court found that the rules were not unconstitutionally vague, the trial court had not held him responsible for violating a repealed rule, and appellee Commission for Lawyer Discipline was entitled to the award of attorneys fees.

OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of harassment in a jury trial. Ireland v. State


NO. 01-97-00408-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4523



July 23, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 97-02434.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from County Criminal Court at Law No. 15, Harris County (Texas), that convicted and sentenced him for driving while intoxicated after denying his motions to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was stopped in his vehicle by police officers who thought he was intoxicated. He was arrested based on his demeanor, his admissions, his failure of field sobriety tests, and the odor of an alcoholic beverage and was taken to the station where he refused to submit to a breath test. Appellant was found guilty after a plea of nolo contendere. On appeal, the court affirmed the criminal court's judgment, holding that the stipulated evidence and reasonable inferences from those stipulations were sufficient to support a finding of probable cause for his arrest. Appellant's failure to drive in a single marked lane, coupled with the odor of alcohol, gave the officers authority to stop, investigate, and arrest him. The court also held that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 (1998) was not unconstitutionally vague in providing that refusal evidence might be admitted into evidence and that the admission of refusal evidence did not violate appellant's right against self-incrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that convicted appellant of driving while intoxicated because the stipulated evidence and resulting inferences were sufficient to support a finding of probable cause for his arrest. The court also found that a Texas statute on refusing to take a breath or blood test was not unconstitutionally vague and that the admission of refusal evidence did not violate appellant's right against self-incrimination.

Guinn v. State


NO. 01-97-00624-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4555



July 23, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 2. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-53674.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 2, Harris County (Texas), that convicted him of driving while intoxicated and denied his motions to suppress evidence obtained, which appellant alleged resulted from an illegal, warrantless arrest because the written stipulation was too conclusory to establish probable cause for his arrest.


OVERVIEW: After appellant pled nolo contendere to driving while intoxicated, he sought review of the trial court's denial of his motions to suppress, alleging the written stipulation that appellant agreed to was too conclusory to establish probable cause for his arrest. The court found that appellant stipulated that the officer pulled him over because he committed the traffic offense of disregarding a police officer and that violation, alone, gave the officers authority to stop, investigate, and arrest appellant. Further, it was stipulated that appellant's arrest was based upon his balance and demeanor, the condition of his eyes and speech, his failure of the field sobriety tests, and the odor of an alcoholic beverage. The court held that appellant lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.061 (1998) because his rights were not adversely affected as that he did not refuse to take a breath test and there was no danger of having refusal evidence introduced at trial. The court affirmed appellant's conviction because the stipulated evidence and reasonable inferences drawn therefrom were sufficient to support a finding of probable cause for his arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of appellant's convictions because the reasonable deductions and inferences drawn from the stipulated evidence were sufficient to support a finding of probable cause for appellant's arrest.

 

663 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Martinez v. State


No. 04-96-00642-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


980 S.W.2d 662; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4439



July 22, 1998, Delivered  
July 22, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused March 17, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 144th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 94-CR-5200. Honorable Susan Reed, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the 144th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), that enhanced his punishment for the crime of serious bodily injury to a child based on reckless conduct. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to enhance his punishment under the Texas Hate Crimes Act, Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.014 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the third-degree felony offense of serious bodily injury to a child based on reckless conduct, and his punishment range was enhanced to that of a second-degree felony based on the Texas Hate Crimes Act (Act), Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.014 (1993), and Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 12.47 (1994). On defendant's appeal of his sentence enhancement, the court affirmed, holding that defendant was properly sentenced under the Act and § 12.47. The court found that the evidence established that defendant consistently abused the victim because of the dark color of his skin and used racial slurs in referring to him. Even though the victim was not African-American, the court ruled that the Act applied because defendant's actions were based on his perception of the victim's race. The court concluded that enhancement under the Act could be based upon circumstantial evidence, and that a bias motivation for the crime charged could reasonably be inferred from defendant's pattern of abuse based on prejudice. The court also ruled that the jury's finding of reckless conduct did not preclude a finding by the trial judge that defendant intentionally selected his victim.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's sentence enhancement because the evidence that defendant had a pattern of abusing the victim based on the victim's perceived race was legally and factually sufficient to support the enhancement under the Texas Hate Crimes Act.

 

664 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Perez v. State


NUMBER 13-97-095-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


973 S.W.2d 759; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4258



July 16, 1998, Delivered  
July 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand January 11, 2001, Reported at: 2001 Tex. App. LEXIS 322. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted December 2, 1998.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the lower court (Texas) that convicted appellant of aggravated assault with a firearm where the lower court denied appellant's motion for a new trial when the parties discovered after the verdict that a juror serving on the panel was a convicted felon, in violation of Tex. Const. art. XVI, § 2.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of aggravated assault with a firearm, and his punishment was assessed at 15 years of imprisonment. After the verdict, the parties discovered that one of the impaneled jurors was a convicted felon, in contravention of Tex. Const. art. XVI §2. Appellant moved for a new trial, and the lower court denied the motion, stating that appellant had not shown significant harm from the felon's jury service, as required by Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.46 (1988). The court held that appellant did not receive a fair trial before a jury composed of 12 qualified persons, as was absolutely required by Tex. Const. art. XVI § 2. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.46(2), which required appellant to show that the juror's service caused significant harm beyond the mere fact of conviction, was incompatible with Tex. Const. art. XVI § 2. The court held that the purpose of Tex. Const. art. XVI § 2 was to prohibit felons from sitting on juries, and appellant's right to trial by jury could not be maintained if the jury composition in the case included a convicted felon. The court reversed the judgment and remanded the case for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the case for a new trial and held that appellant was denied his constitutional right to a jury trial when one of the impaneled jurors was a convicted felon in violation of the Texas Constitution, and appellant did not need to show that the juror's service rendered appellant significant harm.

 

665 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Bailey v. City of Austin


NO. 03-97-00789-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


972 S.W.2d 180; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4334; 77 Fair Empl. Prac. Cas. (BNA) 1169



July 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Petition for Review Denied January 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 94-07318, HONORABLE F. SCOTT McCOWN, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed and Remanded in Part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city employees sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Travis County (Texas) that granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment in appellants' action to have amendment to city charter declared unconstitutional. Appellants asserted that amendment, which eliminated health benefits for domestic partners, violated equal protection rights, impaired existing contract rights, and was prohibited by promissory estoppel.


OVERVIEW: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city in appellants' action that asserted that amendment to city charter, which effectively discontinued extension of health benefits to domestic partners of city employees, was unconstitutional. The court held that the amendment did not violate the equal protection clause. The court found that the amendment was aimed at unmarried domestic partners, not homosexuals. Under the rational relation test, the court found that the amendment was rationally related to the aims of fiscal responsibility and favoring the legally cognizable relationship of marriage. The court held that the amendment did not retroactively impair appellee's existing contractual obligations. The court found that the employee handbook, which expressly granted right to amend benefits, did not created a protected interest for appellants in those benefits. However, the court held that there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether appellants acted in detrimental reliance on benefits granted and then taken away.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee city when there was a genuine issue of material fact as to whether appellant city employees detrimentally relied on extension of benefits. The court held that amendment did not violate equal protection under rational relation test and did not impair existing contractual rights when appellants had no vested interest in benefits. The court remanded for further proceedings.

Ex parte Elliott


NO. 03-97-00674-CR, NO. 03-97-00816-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


973 S.W.2d 737; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4296



July 16, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 10, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 331ST JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 0954859 & 0954865, HONORABLE LARRY L. FULLER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on Both Causes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of denial of two writs of habeas corpus with regard to conviction for transportation of hazardous waste under the Texas Solid Waste Disposal Act, Tex. Health & safety Code § 361.221(a)(1) and 361.221(a)(2), in the District Court of Travis County, 331st Judicial District (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of the denial of his two writs of habeas corpus based on the alleged unconstitutional delegation of legislative power to an administrative agency under the Texas Solid Waste Disposal Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code §§361.221(a)(1) and 361.221(a)(2). The court rejected appellant's argument and affirmed the denial of relief from the conviction for transpiration of hazardous waste. The court explained the state statute's incorporation by reference of the federal definition of hazardous waste was constitutional and not an impermissible delegation of authority. The court further explained the state legislature adopted the federal administrative definition of waste that was in existence at the time the statute was enacted and did not attempt to adopt future federal administrative definitions. As a result, the court reasoned the state statute did not need to include procedural standards to limit the agency's future rulemaking power. The court determined the agency's rulemaking power was limited to those past rulemaking acts that had been approved by the state legislature.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed denial of appellant petitioner's request for writs of habeas corpus under Texas Solid Waste Disposal Act because the statute was constitutional and not an impermissible delegation of authority to define a crime when the statute incorporated by reference a then existing definition of hazardous waste contained in a federal statute, but did not attempt to incorporate future definitions.

In the Interest of A.M.


No. 04-97-01022-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


974 S.W.2d 857; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4205



July 15, 1998, Delivered  
July 15, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 38th Judicial District Court, Real County, Texas. Trial Court No. 93-11-01943-CV. Honorable Charles Sherrill, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND RENDERED IN PART, AND REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother sought review of the decision of the 38th Judicial District Court, Real County (Texas), which modified a prior child custody order, disqualified appellant's attorney, and assessed costs and ad litem fees against appellant. Appellant raised 55 points of error on appeal.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, the mother of a minor child, sought review of the trial court's decision in an action regarding custody of the child. Appellant originally made several motions to attempt to enforce the original custody order after a subsequent modification failed to work out between appellant and appellee father. The trial court entered a final judgment in response to appellant's motions that actually modified the original order and also disqualified appellant's attorney. The appellate court held that the trial court should not have modified the original agreement in response to appellant's motion, which was a motion to enforce the agreement. The court also held that the trial court erred in disqualifying appellant's counsel for behavior that the appellate court found did not warrant disqualification. The court reversed the trial court's decision, and remanded in part for redetermination of costs and ad litem fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment modifying child custody, and remanded in part for redetermination of costs and ad litem fees. The court found that the trial court improperly modified the original child custody order, and also improperly disqualified appellant's attorney.

Bonds v. Texas Dep't of Crim. Justice


No. 06-98-00034-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4155


July 13, 1998, Submitted  
July 14, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied November 5, 1998. Appellant's Pro Se Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 4, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 369th Judicial District Court. Anderson County, Texas. Trial Court No. 369-96-1367.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 369th Judicial District Court for Anderson County (Texas), which dismissed his suit against the Texas Department of Criminal Justice and imposed costs; appellant made several contentions in his appeal.


OVERVIEW: The trial court entered an order dismissing appellant's suit against the Texas Department of Criminal Justice and imposed costs against him. He challenged the dismissal, raising several arguments in his appeal. The court overruled appellant's contention that the trial court's order was erroneous and unenforceable, as it failed to specify the exact amount of costs charged against him. Instead, the court found that the order imposed costs in the precise language of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 14.006 (Supp. 1998); although the total amount of costs was not specified, the order did give specific directions for the calculation of those costs and the method of paying them. Moreover, it was sufficient to give notice of the amount and the method of payment of such costs. The court also disagreed with appellant that the trial court should have taxed the costs as permitted by Tex. R. Civ. P. 141, as there was no proof that appellant was unable to pay the costs. The court also found that § 14.006 provided for a notice and hearing, as written and applied, and that it did not violate the separation of powers doctrine; the statute was thus constitutional. The order below was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order dismissing appellant's suit and imposing costs upon him, was affirmed. The court found that although the total amount of cost was not specified, the order did give specific directions for calculation of those costs and the method of paying them, and it was sufficient to give notice of the amount and the method of payment of such costs. Amongst other things, the court also found that the applicable statute was constitutional as well.

Armstrong v. State


No. 05-96-02026-CR, No. 05-96-02027-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4162



July 14, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused February 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 382nd Judicial District Court. Rockwall County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 2-96-116 and 2-96-115.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment from the 382nd Judicial District Court, Rockwall County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of more than 400 grams of cocaine and of engaging in organized criminal activity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(5) (1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was involved in interstate transport of cocaine. He was arrested and convicted of possession of more than 400 grams of cocaine and of engaging in organized criminal activity in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a)(5) (1998). On appeal, the reviewing court found that evidence was legally and factually sufficient to convict defendant of possession of cocaine as either a principal or party. When viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, evidence was sufficient to prove defendant's guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Evidence was not so uncertain, inconsistent, improbable, or unbelievable that it would be clearly unjust to allow the verdicts to stand. Although distribution of a controlled substance was not an enumerated offense in the penal code, distribution was defined as a means of delivery and delivery was an offense. Thus, distribution of cocaine was an offense and the statute under which defendant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague. Defendant's objection to admissibility of evidence dealt with an improper predicate and not the admission itself, so the issue of admissibility was not preserved for appeal. Judgment of conviction was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for possession of more than 400 grams of cocaine and of engaging in organized criminal activity was affirmed. Evidence was both legally and factually sufficient to support the convictions; the statute under which defendant was convicted was not unconstitutionally vague; and defendant failed to preserve the issue of evidence admissibility for appeal.

Simpson v. Dunlap


NO. 07-97-0147-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4152



July 13, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petition for Review Denied November 5, 1998. Appellee's Motion for Rehearing Overruled August 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 237TH DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 95-554,131; HONORABLE JOHN R. McFALL, JUDGE.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 16, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2462.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed and cause remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individuals sought review from the 237th District Court of Lubbock County (Texas) which granted summary judgment to appellee individuals in appellants' trespass to try title action based upon claims of adverse possession. On original submission the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. After further consideration, the court granted appellants' motion for rehearing and withdrew its original opinion and judgment.


OVERVIEW: The trial court granted summary judgment to appellee individuals in appellant individuals' trespass to try title action based upon claims of adverse possession. After initially affirming, the court granted appellants' motion for rehearing and withdrew its original opinion and judgment. The court then reversed and remanded the trial court's grant of summary judgment for appellees. Appellants alleged that their mother established limitation title to all, or in the alternative, an undivided one-half interest in the tract at issue and that upon her intestate death that they had succeeded to her interest. Appellees contended that appellants' claims to title based upon adverse possession were barred because the alleged 10 year adverse possession period was interrupted by prior court order. The reviewing court found that there was a fact question as to whether a particular individual abandoned his prior action for specific performance of a written contract to sell the subject property. The court therefore concluded that appellees failed to establish the absence of any genuine issue of material fact and that they were entitled to judgment as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for appellee individuals was reversed and remanded. The court withdrew its original opinion and judgment. The court determined that there was a fact question as to whether a particular individual abandoned his suit for specific performance of a written contract to sell the subject property. Therefore, appellees failed to establish the absence of any genuine issue of material fact or entitlement to judgment as a matter of law.

Kerr v. Texas Dep't of Pub. Safety


No. 06-97-00069-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


973 S.W.2d 732; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3956


May 21, 1998, Submitted  
July 3, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court at Law. Harrison County, Texas. Trial Court No. 97-4258-CCL.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant driver sought review of a ruling of the County Court at Law, Harrison County (Texas), finding that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.011 and Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.012 were not vague, arbitrary, and capricious and, therefore, unconstitutional and affirming the suspension of his driver's license for ninety days for refusing to submit to a breath test.


OVERVIEW: Appellant driver was stopped for speeding, submitted to a breath test, and was subsequently arrested for driving while intoxicated. Appellant refused to take a second breath test and his license was suspended for ninety days. Appellant claimed that Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.011 and Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 724.012 were unconstitutional because the language permitting "one or more" specimens was vague and allowed arbitrary and capricious enforcement. The court noted that because it was a civil statute it was subject to a less strict vagueness test and found that it was not vague and that appellant had fair warning that refusal to submit to the tests would result in suspension. Because appellant was not under arrest during the first test, he was only asked to submit to one test under the statute. Because there was no evidence of actual abuse by officers when requesting tests, the court refused to hold the statute facially invalid merely because it could be unconstitutionally applied under hypothetical facts. Because appellant failed to show the statute was unconstitutionally vague or enforced arbitrarily or in a discriminatory manner as applied to him, the judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment the trial court's finding that a Texas statute allowing for one or more specimens was constitutional and affirming the suspension of appellants' driver's license because the statute was not unconstitutionally vague and there was no evidence that it was enforced arbitrarily.

Fowler v. Bryan Indep. Sch. Dist.


NO. 01-97-01001-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 4036



July 2, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 361st District Court. Brazos County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 44,241-361.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant female students challenged an order of the 361st District Court, Brazos County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee school district and district employees in appellants' suit stemming from their sexual harassment by fellow students.


OVERVIEW: Appellant female students brought suit against appellee school district and district employees for failing to stop sexual harassment by fellow students. Appellees moved for summary judgment, arguing sovereign and statutory immunity, collateral estoppel, failure to state a claim, lack of standing, mootness, and vagueness. The trial court granted appellees' motion, and appellants challenged the adverse decision. While the order granting summary judgment failed to set forth the grounds upon which summary judgment was granted, summary judgment was to be affirmed if any asserted ground was valid. Summary judgment in favor of appellees was affirmed, as appellants' claim was void under the mootness doctrine where the wrongful behavior had ceased and there was no showing that it was expected to recur. Appellants failed to establish the capable of repetition exception to the mootness doctrine where there was no reasonable expectation that the same controversy involving the same complaining parties would recur if not address and failed to establish a collateral consequences exception where there was no showing that the effects of the events continued to stigmatize them.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee school district and district employees was affirmed, as appellants claim was void for mootness where the wrongful behavior that was the subject of their complaint had ceased and where there was no showing that such conduct was expected to recur.
