Tullis v. State


No. 05-97-00167-CR, No. 05-97-00168-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3779



June 24, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 7. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. MA94-26042-H & MB94-26043-H.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgments of County Criminal Court No. 7, Dallas County (Texas) that found appellant guilty of the offenses of resisting arrest and driving with a suspended license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere to the offenses of resisting arrest and driving with a suspended license. Appellant was arrested after a computer check showed appellant's driver's license was suspended. Appellant challenged the trial court's decisions denying his motion to suppress evidence and his motion to dismiss the driving with a suspended license case. On appeal, the court affirmed appellant's convictions. The court held that appellant had waived his complaints concerning the admissibility of the police report because appellant did not object to the police report in the trial court on the grounds raised on appeal, but instead offered the report into evidence. The court found that there was probable cause for appellant's warrantless arrest because the police officers were entitled to rely on the computer check that showed appellant's driver's license was suspended. The court held that the requirement that a person possess a driver's license does not abrogate a person's right to travel and that the suspension of a driver's license for violation of a state traffic law did not unconstitutionally burden the right to travel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that found appellant guilty of resisting arrest and driving with a suspended license because appellant failed to object to the introduction of a police report, the police had probable cause to arrest appellant when a computer check showed that appellant's driver's license was suspended, and the requirement that a person possess a drivers license did not abrogate the right to travel.

Cabello v. Ziafat


NO. 07-96-0360-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3788



June 24, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 281st JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF HARRIS COUNTY; NO. 94-00981; HONORABLE WILLIAM BELL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee challenged an order of the 281st District Court of Harris County (Texas) that granted summary judgment to appellee former employer on appellant's claims for intentional infliction of emotional distress, negligence, breach of a duty of good faith and fair dealing, and violation of the Americans with Disabilities Act, 42 U.S.C.S. 12112(a), and the Texas Commission on Human Rights, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 21.051 (1996).


OVERVIEW: Appellant former employee brought claims against appellee former employer for wrongful termination after she was fired in front of a co-worker and some patients. The trial court granted appellee summary judgment on each claim. On appeal, the court held that appellee's behavior did not rise to the level of outrageous conduct necessary to support an intentional infliction of emotional distress action. The court held that the Americans with Disabilities Act, 42 U.S.C.S. 12112(a), and the Texas Commission on Human Rights, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. § 21.051 (1996) did not apply because the acts were limited to employers engaged in commerce who employed 15 or more people for a proscribed time period. The court found that appellant was not deprived of equal protection under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Tex. Const. art. I, § 3 because the statutes rationally furthered their stated purpose. The court held that there was no general duty of good faith and fair dealing where there was nothing in the record indicating the parties had any type of express agreement altering their at-will employment relationship. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee on all of appellant's claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment to appellee former employer on all of appellee former employee's claims for wrongful termination because appellant's behavior in firing at-will employee was not extreme and outrageous.

McGriff v. State


No. 05-96-00223-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3616



June 15, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 363rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F95-03589-W.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed his conviction for burglary of a building in the 363rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) and argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress and assessing punishment under the wrong penal code section.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to burglary. Although he pleaded not true to a paragraph alleging a 1990 murder conviction, the trial court found the allegation true. At the punishment hearing, defendant requested sentencing under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §12.35(a) (1994), which provided a punishment range of not less than 180 days or more than two years. The trial court assessed punishment as a third-degree felony and sentenced appellant to seven years' confinement and an $ 800 fine. On defendant's claim that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress, by which he sought to exclude from evidence items found in his truck, the court held that his nonnegotiated guilty plea was conclusive as to his guilt and waived all nonjurisdictional defects occurring prior to the guilty plea. The court further held that defendant's prior conviction which occurred prior to the enactment of a statute providing for increased punishment upon his subsequent conviction could be used for enhancement purposes under that statute, and that such usage was not unconstitutional as being ex post facto application.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of conviction on the basis that defendant's guilty plea was conclusive as to his guilt and because the statute which enhanced his punishment for having a prior conviction was not unconstitutional.

 

676 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In re J.L.C.


NO. 01-97-01077-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3541



June 11, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 313th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 85067.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his transfer by the 313th District Court, Harris County, Texas from the Texas Youth Commission to the Institutional Division for the Texas Department of Criminal Justice.


OVERVIEW: Appellant confessed to having committed attempted capital murder, aggravated robbery and assault when he was 14. Appellant was adjudicated delinquent and committed to the Texas Youth Commission for a determinate sentence of 25 years pursuant to Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 54.04(d)(3). The state filed a motion for release and transfer. A hearing was held and it was determined that appellant would be transferred to the Texas Department of Corrections. The court determined that appellant's juvenile court petition functioned as an indictment, and that appellant was not incarcerated without the benefit of an indictment in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 10. The court determined that it was within the discretion of the trial court to determine whether appellant should be transferred and that there had been no abuse of that discretion. The court affirmed appellant's transfer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the transfer ordered by the trial court, having determined that absent an abuse of discretion the determination of the trial court had to be upheld.

 

677 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of Austin v. L.S. Ranch


NO. 03-98-00024-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


970 S.W.2d 750; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3601



June 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected September 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 207TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 97-1048, HONORABLE JACK ROBISON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Appeal Dismissed for Want of Jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought interlocutory review of a decision of the 207th District Court, Hays County, Texas, that denied appellant's plea to the jurisdiction which asserted the absence of a justiciable controversy in appellee landowners' declaratory action against appellant regarding a proposed annexation of appellees' property by appellant.


OVERVIEW: Appellee landowners filed a declaratory action against appellant city to prevent appellant from carrying out a proposed annexation of appellees' property. Appellant sought interlocutory review of the decision of the trial court that denied appellant's plea to the jurisdiction. Appellees then amended their complaint and alleged that appellant had actually annexed appellees' property. The court dismissed appellant's appeal for want of jurisdiction. The court found that because appellees' petition was at most merely insufficient to demonstrate jurisdiction, without affirmatively showing a lack thereof, the trial court was required to give appellees an opportunity to amend before dismissing. Although the pleading of a mere threat to annex appellees' property was not enough to demonstrate a ripe controversy, the court found that appellees' second amended complaint alleged an actual annexation of property by the city and thereby demonstrated a ripe controversy. The court dismissed appellant's appeal as moot because the relief it would have granted, namely leave to amend the complaint, was accomplished.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant's interlocutory appeal for want of jurisdiction because appellee landowners amended their complaint, which is the relief the court would have granted, to allege that appellant city actually annexed appellees' property, which demonstrated a ripe controversy and thereby conferred jurisdiction upon the trial court.

 

678 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Wright v. State


NO. 01-97-01414-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


976 S.W.2d 815; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3611



June 11, 1998, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 351st District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 767,587. Hon. Mark Ellis, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the 351st District Court, Harris County (Texas), denying her request for a writ of habeas corpus to lower her bond in an aggravated assault case.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for murder and was released after she posted bond. After appellant's release, she was charged with aggravated assault. No bond was set. Appellant challenged the no bond status and bond was set at $ 500,000. Appellant filed a writ of habeas corpus. The trial court granted the writ and conducted an evidentiary hearing. At the hearing, evidence was admitted that established appellant expected money from an inheritance, appellant would flee, and that no bail bondsman would write a $ 500,000 bond. The trial court refused to lower the bond. The court found that it was appellant's burden to show that the bail was excessive. Appellant failed to show that the application of Tex. Code. Crim. P. Ann. art. 17.15(5), which allowed consideration of community safety in determining the amount of bail, was unconstitutional as it applied to her. The ability of appellant to post bond did not control the amount. The court refused to place a cap on the amount of bail that could be set. The lower court's order that refused to lower bail was affirmed because the amount of bail was justifiable based on evidence that appellant would flee.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the trial court that denied appellant's request for a writ of habeas corpus to lower her bond in an aggravated assault case was affirmed because appellant's ability to post bond did not control the amount of the bond. Because there was evidence that appellant would flee, the amount of bond was justified.

Acosta v. State


No. 08-96-00289-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


972 S.W.2d 95; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3384



June 4, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of September 25, 1997.

Appeal from County Court at Law No. 1 of El Paso County, Texas. (TC # 940C12375). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Ricardo Herrera.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction, which was entered in the County Court at Law No. 1 of El Paso County (Texas), for illegal dumping. Subsequent to the appeal, he moved for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his son used a pick-up truck to take dirt from a home under construction to another construction site and dumped it near dirt from that site. Appellant was convicted of illegal dumping and sentenced to 30 days in jail, suspended, and a fine. During the punishment phase of the trial, appellant admitted his guilt. In an opinion substituted for a previous one in the same case, the court held that, because appellant testified at the punishment stage of the trial and admitted his guilt of the crime, for legal purposes, he entered the equivalent of a plea of guilty. The court held that appellant waived any evidentiary complaints by so testifying. The court examined appellant's federal constitutional argument on the merits and found that a person of ordinary intelligence would not mistake the specific statutory exception in Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 365.012(a), (f)(2) (1998), for dirt and rock "used to fill land" as an open invitation to dump dirt and rock at any convenient construction site. Therefore, the court overruled appellant's motion for rehearing and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court overruled appellant's motion for rehearing and affirmed his conviction for illegal dumping because appellant admitted his guilt at the punishment phase of the trial.

Miller v. State


NO. 14-96-00845-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3419



June 4, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 208th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 721,808.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 208th District Court, Harris County (Texas), for engaging in organized criminal activity, under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a) (1998). Appellant asserted error in the denial of his motion to dismiss the indictment and his motion to instruct the state to disclose the identity of a confidential informant.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of engaging in organized criminal activity. The court affirmed. First, the court rejected appellant's assertion that the organized crime statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 71.02(a) (1998), was improperly and unconstitutionally applied to his case because his activities were not meant to be covered by the statute. The court held that there was no basis to sustain this point of error because appellant cited, and the court found, no authority providing that a statute was unconstitutionally vague merely for extending beyond its intended scope. Next, the court rejected appellant's request to reveal the identity of a confidential informant referred to in the affidavit that supported the search and arrest warrant. The court held that appellant did not demonstrate that the informant's testimony was so necessary to a fair determination of guilt that the trial court's denial of his motion to disclose the informant's identity was outside the zone of reasonable disagreement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and held that appellant failed to provide the court with any authority which supported his contention that the statute he violated was unconstitutionally vague simply for extending beyond the scope the legislature intended. The court also held that appellant failed to show that testimony of an informant was necessary for a fair determination of guilt.

Courtney v. State


NO. 01-97-00541-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3452



June 4, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused January 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court of Law No. 1. Fort Bend County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 70411.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the County Court of Law No. 1, Fort Bend County, Texas, which denied his pretrial motions to have Tex. Transp. Code Ann. § 24.061 declared unconstitutional, and to have certain evidence suppressed after defendant was charged by information with misdemeanor driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted for misdemeanor driving while intoxicated, he received permission from the trial court to appeal the denial of his pretrial motions. The court disagreed with defendant that the stipulated evidence was too conclusory to establish probable cause to stop him in the first place. Defendant had stipulated that based on his glassy, bloodshot eyes, slurred speech, smell of alcoholic beverage on his body and breath, and his failure of three field sobriety tests, the officer arrested him for DWI. At the hearing on his pretrial motions, defendant failed to explain why he thought the officer lacked probable cause to stop him, argue the substance of his appellate attack on such probable cause, or claim that stipulated evidence was insufficient to support a conviction to the trial court. Thus, any error arising out of the conclusory stipulated facts was waived. Furthermore, the trial court did not err in overruling defendant's motion to suppress evidence of a breath test refusal or that the statute permitting the introduction of such refusal was unconstitutional, because defendant did not refuse to take the breath test.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for misdemeanor driving while intoxicated was affirmed. Defendant had stipulated that based on his glassy, bloodshot eyes, slurred speech, the smell of alcoholic beverage on his body and breath, and his failure of three field sobriety tests, the officer arrested him for DWI. The court held that such stipulated evidence was sufficient to establish probable cause for the officer to stop defendant in the first place.

Hipps v. State


No. 05-96-01420-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 3108



May 26, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court Number Two. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MB94-51660-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged her conviction of telephone harassment arguing that it was error for the lower court to have allowed the state to amend the information without giving her notice, and that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(4) was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of her conviction of telephone harassment, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.07(a)(4), contending that the lower court erred in permitting the state to amend the information without notice to her, and that § 42.07(a)(4) was unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous. On appeal, the conviction was affirmed. In support of its ruling, the court noted that the information was amended to reflect the correct spelling of complainant's name. The court further noted that the record indicated no objection by appellant as the amended information was read in open court, and no objection when she was asked whether she understood the charges in the information. The court held that if the amendment to the information was objectionable to appellant she could have filed a motion to quash the information, or objected to the state's motion to amend. The court further held that § 42.07(a)(4) was not unconstitutionally vague and ambiguous as it contained a reasonable person standard, and sufficiently defined the offense of telephone harassment so as to put appellant on notice that her conduct was unlawful.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed as appellant failed to object to the amendment of the information without notice to her, and because the penal code statute in question adequately defined the offense described and the conduct that was impermissible.

Drew v. Unauthorized Practice of Law Comm.


NO. 03-97-00254-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


970 S.W.2d 152; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2993



May 21, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 126TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-13424, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation president sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Travis County (Texas) that enjoined appellant from engaging in the unauthorized practice of law and found appellant in contempt for violating the injunction.


OVERVIEW: Appellant corporation president, unlicensed to practice law, prepared and filed writs of habeas corpus applications on behalf of criminal defendants who believed their civil and constitutional rights had been violated. Appellee committee filed suit to enjoin appellant from practicing law without a license. A temporary injunction was issued, and following trial, a permanent injunction was ordered. After appellant violated the injunction, appellant was found in contempt. Appellant sought review of the injunction and contempt order. The court affirmed. Appellant alleged that the order was entered in error because the trial court refused to hold a hearing to determine his ability to afford an attorney and also refused to appoint an attorney to represent him during the contempt hearing. The validity of a contempt judgment could be attacked only collaterally and by writ of habeas corpus. The rule extended to decisions regarding appointment of an attorney during the contempt hearing as well. The injunction was properly drafted because it spelled out the details of compliance in clear, specific, and unambiguous terms so that appellant readily knew exactly what he was prohibited from doing.


OUTCOME: Judgment that permanently enjoined appellant corporation president from engaging in the unauthorized practice of law and finding him in contempt of the injunction order was affirmed. Appellant could not attack the contempt order by direct appeal because the validity of a contempt judgment could only be attacked collaterally and by writ of habeas corpus. Injunction gave appellant clear notice of what he was prohibited from doing.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a judgment of the 11th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee county bail bond board, affirming appellee's denial of appellant's application for a bail bond license.


OVERVIEW: Appellant applicant previously held a bail bond license, which had been renewed twice. Subsequently, renewal was refused because appellee county bail bonds board determined that appellant had an unpaid final judgment on a bond forfeiture more than 30 days old, a statutory ground for rejection of renewal. Unable to renew her license, appellant submitted an application for a new license, which was denied. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court held that where an applicant had previously held a license, appellee could investigate the applicant's past history as a licensee in determining whether the applicant was entitled to a new license.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the district court's denial of appellant applicant's application for a bail bonds licensee because the decision was based upon sufficient grounds the district court properly construed the statute to allow appellee county bail bonds board to consider information other than that required for application for a new license.

Sanchez v. State


No. 04-96-00140-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


974 S.W.2d 307; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2950



May 20, 1998, Delivered  
May 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted November 18, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 144th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95-CR-6046. Honorable Susan D. Reed, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND ACQUITTAL ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for official oppression under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 39.03(a)(3), (c) (1994), entered in the 144th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), asserting that the statute under which he was convicted was vague on its face and as applied to him, and was overbroad and impinged on his freedom of speech, in violation of the Due Process Clause and the First Amendment of the U.S. Constitution, respectively.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a chairman and board member of a transit authority, was charged with official oppression under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 39.03(a)(3), (c) (1994), for sexually harassing a subordinate female employee. He challenged his conviction, alleging that the oppression statute was unconstitutional both because it was vague, in violation of his federal due process rights, and because it was overbroad, offending his right to free speech. The court agreed, reversing his conviction and acquitting him of the crime. The court found that the conduct requirement of the statute, which prohibited intentionally subjecting another to sexual harassment, was vague, and that a reasonable person standard could not be read into the law. Furthermore, the statute could not be narrowly construed to eliminate the definition of sexual harassment because doing so would significantly alter the meaning of the statute. As an alternative basis for its holding, the court found that the statute was overbroad and violated U.S. Const. amend. I, because it was not narrowly tailored to prohibit only disorderly conduct, fighting words, obscene or opprobrious language, or unprotected speech.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction of official oppression and acquitted him of the crime, holding that the statute proscribing such conduct was vague on its face and as applied to him, in violation of federal due process protections. As an alternative basis for its holding, the court found the statute unconstitutionally overbroad, infringing on appellant's right to free speech.

In re A.D.D.


No. 04-96-01014-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


974 S.W.2d 299; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2989



May 20, 1998, Delivered  
May 20, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 73rd Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95-JUV-02048. Honorable Andy Mireles, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 73rd Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), which found him engaged in delinquent conduct by committing the offense of possession of less than one gram of cocaine and placed him on probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found engaged in delinquent conduct by committing the offense of possession of less than one gram of cocaine and placed on probation. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence, asserting that it was the product of an unconstitutional search. The state contended the evidence was seized as the product of a valid investigative detention and search for weapons. The court reversed the judgment, finding that defendant was searched twice and that the second search was characterized as a protective weapons search. The court held that the purpose of a weapons search was not to discover evidence of a crime, but to allow an officer to pursue his investigation without fear of violence. The court found that the second search was not justified as a protective weapons search after the first patdown revealed that defendant was not carrying a weapon. The court held that if a protective search went beyond what was necessary to determine if defendant was armed, it was no longer valid and it fruits would be suppressed. The court remanded for further proceedings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a judgment that found defendant engaged in delinquent conduct by committing the offense of possession of less than one gram of cocaine and placed him on probation. The court held that evidence seized during a protective weapons search was inadmissible where a patdown search had already revealed that defendant was not carrying a weapon.

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN

May 14, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected June 2, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-12285, HONORABLE JERRY DELLANA, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Comptroller of Public Accounts and Attorney General of the State of Texas, challenged the decision of the 200th District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted declaratory relief and ordered appellants to refund more than half a million dollars plus interest and attorney's fees to appellee corporation in appellee's action to recover taxes paid under protest.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation was granted declaratory relief and appellants, Comptroller of Public Accounts and Attorney General of the State of Texas, were ordered to pay appellee more than half a million dollars plus interest and attorney's fees in appellee's action to recover taxes paid under protest. The court reversed the judgment and rendered judgment that appellee take nothing, holding that the trial court's declaratory relief and conclusions supporting the refund of taxes to appellee were legally erroneous. The court held that appellant's shuttle service was incident to its parking service and was therefore taxable. The court held that the doctrine of legislative acquiescence did not require the treatment of appellant's shuttle service as nontaxable. Further, the court held that the application of the tax was rationally based on whether the transportation service provided was incident to a taxable service and did not violate the requirements of equal protection. The court held that the rule requiring the tax was not an unconstitutionally retroactive law in violation of Tex. Const. art. I, § 16.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment against appellants, Comptroller of Public Accounts and Attorney General of the State of Texas, and rendered judgment that appellee corporation take nothing because the trial court's declaratory relief and conclusions supporting the refund of taxes to appellee were legally erroneous.

Overhead Door Corp. v. Sharp


NO. 03-97-00748-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


970 S.W.2d 74; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2808



May 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 353RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-15316, HONORABLE SUZANNE COVINGTON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation challenged the decision of the 353rd District Court of Travis County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees, Comptroller of Public Accounts and Attorney General of the State of Texas, in an action brought by appellant for a refund of franchise taxes previously paid.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, Comptroller of Public Accounts and Attorney General of the State of Texas, were granted summary judgment because the statute of limitations had run in the action brought by appellant corporation for a refund of franchise taxes. In 1989, appellees refunded a portion of the tax and appellant took no further action until 1993. The court rejected appellant's contention that the statute of limitations did not bar the refund request, holding that the refund claim expired on one of two dates: four years from the date the tax was due and payable; or four years, plus any applicable tolling period, from the date the tax was actually paid. The court held that the only way appellant could overcome the limitations argument was to establish that the period was tolled for over three, and appellant failed to do this. Appellant next contended that the appellees violated appellant's right to fair and equal taxation under Tex. Const. art. VIII, § 2, by refusing to settle the refund claim. The court rejected this argument and affirmed the judgment, holding that it was within the discretion of appellee Attorney General to decide whether to settle the dispute or whether to go to trial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of appellees, Comptroller of Public Accounts and Attorney General of the State of Texas, because the statute of limitations barred appellant corporation's refund claim for franchise taxes and appellant failed to establish that appellees violated appellant's right to fair and equal taxation.

City of Garland v. Dallas Morning News


No. 05-95-01350-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


969 S.W.2d 548; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2788



May 13, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 134th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 93-10526-G.



DISPOSITION: REVERSE and REMAND in part, AFFIRM in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants city and city manager challenged an order of the 134th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee news agency in appellee's suit seeking disclosure of information under the Texas Open Records Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 552.001-.353, arguing that the requested information was excepted from disclosure.


OVERVIEW: Appellee news agency submitted a request under the Texas Open Records Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 552.001-.353, for written information concerning the termination of appellant city's finance director. Appellant city manager declined the request, contending that any documents were excepted from disclosure. Appellee brought suit against appellants city and city manager seeking disclosure of the requested information. Both parties moved for summary judgment, and appellants challenged the order granting summary judgment in appellee's favor and denying their motion for summary judgment. In affirming summary judgment in favor of appellee, the appellate court concluded that the information was not excepted from disclosure under § 552.111, the agency memorandum exception, where it was not a deliberate communication related to the policy-making process of appellant city. Policy-making functions did not encompass internal administrative or personnel matters. Thus, a memorandum concerning problems related to a particular employee did not involve appellant city's policy-making function, and no agency memorandum exception applied.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment in favor of appellee news agency was affirmed, as information concerning a city employee's termination was public information subject to disclosure upon request. While agency memoranda, deliberate communications related to policy-making processes, were excepted from disclosure, a memorandum concerning one employee did not concern policy-making functions but concerned a personnel matter and was thus subject to disclosure.

Dallas County Dist. Atty. v. Doe


No. 05-97-02111-CV, No. 05-98-00243-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


969 S.W.2d 537; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2735



May 11, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 160th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 97-06986-H.



DISPOSITION: Dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county attorney and state, sought review of the declaratory judgment entered by the 160th Judicial District Court, Dallas County, Texas, holding Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 255.001 unconstitutional. Appellants challenged whether the trial court's properly exercised its equity jurisdiction to declare the statute unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee political consultant, filed a petition in the civil district court, seeking a declaration that Tex. Elec. Code Ann. § 255.001 violated U.S. Const. amend I. Appellee subsequently filed a motion for summary judgment. The trial court granted the motion, and appellants, county attorney and state, sought review, arguing the statute was constitutional and challenging the court's jurisdiction to declare the statute unconstitutional. The court vacated and dismissed the trial court judgment, holding that the civil district court did not have jurisdiction to declare § 255.001 unconstitutional, and the trial court should have dismissed appellee's declaratory judgment action. The court held that a request for declaratory relief could not confer subject matter jurisdiction on a court, nor could it change the basic character of a suit. The court further held that the meaning and validity of a penal statute should ordinarily be determined by a court exercising criminal jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's declaratory judgment holding a section of the Texas Election Code, unconstitutional. The court held that the criminal district court and not the civil district court had jurisdiction to rule on the constitutionality of the statute. The action was dismissed.

Mosby v. State


NO. 14-95-01108-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2653



May 7, 1998, Rendered  
May 7, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused October 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 178th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 670,471.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for capital murder from the 178th District Court, Harris County (Texas). Appellant asserted that the capital murder statute shouldn't have applied to him under the theory of the criminal responsibility statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.02 (1994), without specific proof of intent. Appellant asked court to remand for clarification of communication between trial court and jury that was not on the record.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder. Appellant and several accomplices robbed a club. When one of appellant's accomplices began to fight with the victim, appellant used his weapon to shoot victim in the chest. The court rejected appellant's argument that it was unconstitutional to apply the capital murder statute to him as a participant in the commission or attempted commission of a robbery which resulted in the shooting death of victim without specific proof of intent. The court held that the criminal responsibility statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 7.02 (1994), eliminated any necessity on the part of the state to prove appellant had any specific intent to kill the decedent in a capital case. The court also held that when appellant failed to object to a communication between the trial judge and the jury during deliberations not being recorded, the appellate court would not remand for a clarification of what the communication was pursuant to Tex. R. App. P. 80(c).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction. The court held that the criminal responsibility statute eliminated the need for the state to prove specific intent in a capital murder case. The court held that when appellant failed to object to the communication between the jury and trial court not being on the record, the court would not remand for clarification.

Martinez v. State

COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the 299th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas) which convicted him of aggravated robbery and sentenced him to 98 years in prison under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03(a)(1), (2) (1994).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of aggravated robbery and sentenced to 98 years in prison under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 29.03(a)(1), (2) (1994), he sought review. On appeal, the record showed that, after defendant and two juveniles entered a pawn shop, defendant leapt over the counter and began stabbing the clerk. The court affirmed the conviction. Such factors as defendant's intent to kill witnesses weighed so strongly against the possibility that the jury might have been concerned with the application of good time, and disobeyed the court's directions not to consider it, that the court determined beyond a reasonable doubt that the alleged error, if any, made no contribution to the punishment, and even if it was error, it was harmless. The court did not consider defendant's U.S. Const. Amend. VI claim because defendant did not make a sufficiently specific reference to the amendment to preserve the issue.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction because any alleged error made no contribution to the punishment, and any error was harmless.

Tracy v. State


NO. 14-94-00732-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2657



May 7, 1998, Rendered  
May 7, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 16, 1998.
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Remanded by Tracy v. Johnson, 226 F.3d 641, 2000 U.S. App. LEXIS 18440 (5th Cir. Tex., 2000)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 184th Judicial District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 676,456.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 184th Judicial District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied his motion for a new trial in his conviction for aggravated robbery.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for aggravated robbery and his motion for a new trial was denied. On appeal, the court held that pursuant to the first prong of the Strickland test, defendant's attorney did not fall below an objective standard of reasonableness when he assessed that appellant's confession was admissible and recommended that appellant should plead guilty. Appellant's confession was found to be admissible because although his arrest was without a warrant, it was justified under Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 14.04 (1977). Next, the court held that since appellant failed to establish that any factually inaccurate information in the pre-sentence investigation (PSI) was materially inaccurate, there was no denial of due process and appellant's counsel was not ineffective for failing to object to the PSI. Last, the court held that there was no constitutional requirement that a comparative proportionality review be conducted of appellant's sentence to that of his co-defendant, and because his sentence fell within the statutory limits for aggravated robbery, it did not constitute cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction for aggravated robbery was affirmed because his ineffective assistance of counsel claims were without merit, he was not denied due process of law, and his sixty-year sentence was not unconstitutionally disproportionate to the sentences of his co-defendants.

Garza v. State

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teenager challenged the decision of the 79th Judicial District Court, Jim Wells County, Texas, which entered an order convicting him of murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant teenager was driving his mother's car when the victim through a bottle at the car, cracking the windshield. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, holding that appellant teenager did not have a constitutionally protected interest in being tried in a particular county. The court further held that even though the trial court violated a statute which required that a hearing be held before a change in venue, the trial court did not deprive appellant of his due process rights.

Polk v. Ball


NO. 07-97-0169-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2621



May 1, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 47TH DISTRICT COURT OF RANDALL COUNTY; NO. 41,524-A; HONORABLE JOHN T. FORBIS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, wife and husband, sought review of the order of the 47th District Court of Randall County (Texas), that granted a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellees, doctor and cancer center, in a medical malpractice case arising out of an alleged failure to diagnose breast cancer in appellant wife.


OVERVIEW: Appellants, wife and husband, filed suit, after the statute of limitations had run, against appellees, doctor and cancer center, alleging that appellees negligently misinterpreted the results of appellant wife's mammogram, thereby allowing her cancer to go undetected for 16 months. Appellant patient discovered the cancer 10 months before the statute of limitations barred the claims against appellee. The trial court granted a take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellee. The court affirmed because statute of limitations had run, and the application of the statute of limitations did not violate the "open courts" provision of the Texas Constitution, which provides that all courts shall be open, and every person for an injury done him, in his lands, goods, person, or reputation, shall have remedy by due course of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of the take-nothing summary judgment in favor of appellees, doctor and cancer center, in the malpractice case because the action was barred by the statute of limitations. The "open courts" doctrine did not apply because appellants, wife and husband, had more than 10 months to file suit from the time they learned of appellant wife's breast cancer until the statute of limitations barred their claims against appellees.

Auster v. State


NO. 01-96-00266-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2565



April 30, 1998, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Criminal Court at Law No. 12. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9543706.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision by the County Criminal Court at Law No. 12, Harris County (Texas), which denied appellant his motion to suppress evidence in a charge of misdemeanor theft.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pleaded nolo contendere to the charge of misdemeanor theft. Appellant challenged the trial court's denial of his motion to suppress evidence. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and found the evidence used against appellant to be admissible. Two private citizens, the manager of the rental storage company and a renter who had claimed some items had been taken from her storage unit, discovered that appellant had several items in his storage unit that did not belong to him. After appellant had left to get a lock for his unit, the manager and renter entered appellant's unit and discovered the items and called the police. The court found that the search of appellant's storage unit did not violate U.S. Const. amend. IV or Tex. Const. art. 1, § 9 since these provisions do not apply to actions by private citizens. Under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23(a) (1998), the court found that the private citizens did not violate the criminal trespass statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 30.05(a) (1994), when entering the storage space since the manager had a right to inspect open units under the lease agreement and did not violate the statute in obtaining the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence in a charge of misdemeanor theft. The evidence seized from appellant's storage unit was not seized in violation of the Fourth Amendment of the Constitution, nor was it in violation of the Texas Constitution or state statutes.

Horsley-Layman v. Angeles


No. 06-97-00088-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


968 S.W.2d 533; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2490


April 1, 1998, Argued  
April 29, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 352nd Judicial District Court. Tarrant County, Texas. Trial Court No. 352-168060-97.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, husband and wife, sought review of a judgment from the 352nd Judicial District Court, Tarrant County (Texas), which dismissed appellants' medical malpractice claim against appellee physician pursuant to § 13.01(d) of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (Supp. 1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, husband and wife, brought suit against appellee physician, alleging negligence in the care and treatment of appellant wife. Although appellants filed the expert opinion required by § 13.01(d) of the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act (the Act), Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (Supp. 1998), as to another defendant physician, they did not timely file any reports specifically addressing appellee. As a result, the trial court granted appellee's motion to dismiss pursuant to § 13.01(e). The court reversed and remanded the judgment, finding that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to grant appellants the extension of time provided by § 13.01(g) to file the required report. The court determined that the failure to file a specific report related to appellee was not the result of conscious indifference or intentional conduct, but rather the result of a mistaken belief that the reports supplied were sufficient to comply with the act. The court overruled appellants' constitutional challenge to art. 4590i, finding that the requirements of the act were not unreasonable and arbitrary when balanced against the purpose of the act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a judgment that dismissed the medical malpractice claim of appellants, husband and wife, against appellee physician. The trial court abused its discretion in refusing to grant appellants an extension of time to file a required expert opinion report. The court overruled appellants' constitutional challenge to the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act.

Odum v. State


No. 04-97-00147-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO

April 29, 1998, Delivered  
April 29, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the District Court for Bexar County (Texas), in which she pled no contest to possession of cocaine and was sentenced to two years' confinement and five years of probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested, released on bond the following day, and thereafter indicted for possession of cocaine. Appellant moved to dismiss her indictment because she was not indicted within two court terms as statutorily required. Conversely, the state contended that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. § 32.01 and §28.061 were unconstitutional and offered no other reason for the delayed indictment. Appellant challenged the judgment. The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded with instructions for dismissal of the indictment. The court held that the state failed to offer a good cause for the delay of the indictment and the aforementioned criminal provisions were constitutional and did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment convicting appellant of possession of cocaine. The court held the trial court erred when it failed to dismiss appellant's indictment, where the state did not present a good cause for the delay. The court reasoned the criminal provisions held by the trial court as unconstitutional, were indeed constitutional, thus the court remanded with instructions to dismiss the indictment against appellant.

Warren v. State


No. 05-96-00092-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


971 S.W.2d 656; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2455



April 27, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 194th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F95-47687-PM.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the 194th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him for possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, in an amount of one gram or more but less than four grams, enhanced by two prior felony convictions, contending that there was insufficient evidence and that it was error to overrule his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted and sentenced for possession of a controlled substance, cocaine, in an amount of one gram or more but less than four grams, enhanced by two prior felony convictions. On appeal, the court held that new legislation required the state to simply prove that adulterants or dilutants increased the bulk or quantity of the controlled substance, without having to prove intent to increase the bulk or quantity or that they did not affect the chemical activity of the controlled substance. Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.002(49) (1998). Therefore, the court found that the .85 grams pure cocaine and .17 grams of other material was sufficient to constitute "at least one gram." The court also held that there was both legal and factual sufficiency to prove possession of the cocaine and that defendant lacked standing to contest the search and seizure of the automobile where the cocaine was found, because he was a mere passenger without a possessory interest in the car.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed because there was sufficient legal and factual evidence to prove that he possessed at least one gram of cocaine, and the trial court did not err in overruling defendant's motion to suppress because as a mere passenger without a possessory interest in the car, defendant did not have standing to contest the search and seizure of the automobile.

Thompson v. City of Austin


NO. 03-97-00490-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


979 S.W.2d 676; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2387; 8 Am. Disabilities Cas. (BNA) 167



April 24, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 200TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 95-03722, HONORABLE W. JEANNE MEURER, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judges sought review of a summary judgment issued by the District Court of Travis County (Texas) for appellee city in a suit alleging discrimination under the Texas Commission on Human Rights Act, Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 21.001-.405 (1996 & Supp. I 1998), and violation of the Texas Open Meetings Act, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 551.001-.146 (1994 & Supp. I 1998) and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 29.005 (1988 & Supp. I 1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellants, former municipal court judges, sued appellee for failure to reappoint them as municipal court judges, alleging discrimination under the Texas Commission on Human Rights Act (TCHRA), Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §§ 21.001-.405 (1996 & Supp. I 1998), and violations of the Texas Open Meetings Act (TOMA), Tex. Gov't Code Ann. §§ 551.001-.146 (1994 & Supp. I 1998), and the Texas Government Code, Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 29.005 (1988 & Supp. I 1998). The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee on all causes of action. The principal issue presented on appeal was whether appellants, as municipal court judges, were employees under the TCHRA. Also at issue was whether appellee violated TOMA by allegedly making a final decision regarding appellants' employment in a closed session and whether appellants were terminated early. The court affirmed the summary judgment. Appellants were public officials rather than appellee's employees, precluding protection under the TCHRA. Appellants failed to preserve or present evidence showing appellee's violation of TOMA. Appellee did not terminate appellants' appointments early; by law appellants had a tenure of less than two years.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of appellee city. Appellant former municipal court judges, as public officials rather than employees, were not entitled to the protections of the Texas Commission on Human Rights Act. Appellants failed to preserve any complaint under the Texas Open Meetings Act. Appellee did not terminate appellants' appointments early. Judicial appointment deliberations were properly held in a closed meeting.

Wilson v. State


No. 05-95-01000-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2420



April 24, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 291st Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F94-25673-PU.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a decision of the 291st Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted defendant of sexual assault, contending that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction under the version of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.07 that was in effect at the time of his offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of sexual assault. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to support the conviction under the version of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.07 that was in effect at the time of his offense. On appeal, the court stated that between the time of the offense and the time of defendant's trial, the legislature amended art. 38.07. The amendments eliminated the necessity of corroboration and a timely outcry in cases where the complainant was under the age of 18. The court further stated that because art. 38.07 was a procedural statute, the amendments to the statute applied to defendant's case in the absence of an express legislative enactment giving them prospective application only. The record reflected that the complainant was 15 years old at the time of the offense. Thus, under the version of art. 38.07 in effect at the time of trial, the complainant's uncorroborated testimony was sufficient to convict defendant. Because complainant's uncorroborated testimony provided factually and legally sufficient evidence to support the conviction, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which convicted defendant of sexual assault. Under the version of the statute in effect at the time of trial, complainant's uncorroborated testimony was sufficient to convict defendant of sexual assault.

Green v. State


NO. 14-96-00419-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


971 S.W.2d 639; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2314



April 23, 1998, Rendered  
April 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 337th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 690,287. Jim Barr, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the 337th District Court, Harris County (Texas) that found him guilty of murder pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 19.02, 19.03.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review of his conviction for murder, contending that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence obtained as the result of an unlawful search, denying his motion to declare Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 unconstitutional, and admitting improper extraneous offense evidence. The court found that appellant did not have standing to challenge the constitutionality of the search because he had moved out of the house and, therefore, had no expectation of privacy therein. Appellant argued that the amended § 19.02 was unconstitutional because it shifted the burden of showing sudden passion to the accused. The court disagreed finding the section to be constitutional. The court concluded that the testimony that appellant had assaulted the victim the day before the murder was admissible because it was probative of the previous relationship between appellant and the victim and his state of mind at the time of the offense; therefore, it was relevant for purposes other than showing appellant's character. The court concluded that the probative value of the evidence was not substantially outweighed by the danger of unfair prejudice and affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment finding appellant guilty of murder, concluding that he did not have standing to challenge the legality of the search of a home in which he no longer lived, that the statute under which he was charged was constitutional, and that it was not error to admit evidence regarding an extraneous offense where it was probative with respect to the relationship between appellant and the victim.

State v. Robinson


No. 05-97-01540-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2349



April 23, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from County Court at Law No. 2. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 002-81914-97.



DISPOSITION: REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Prosecution appealed an order by the County Court at Law No. 2, Collin County (Texas), which dismissed with prejudice prosecution's information charging defendant with telephone harassment based on its grant of her special plea that the statute under which she was charged was unconstitutional under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 44.01(a)(1)(1998).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with telephone harassment and she brought a motion to dismiss claiming that the statute under which she had been charged was unconstitutional. The trial court agreed and dismissed the charges with prejudice. The prosecution recharged, but defendant claimed that double jeopardy and collateral estoppel barred the prosecution from recharging her. The court disagreed and held that the whole idea behind pre-trial motions under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 27.05(1989), was that all issues be determined before trial so that no double jeopardy problems arose. The court held that the pre-trial hearing, special plea, at which the trial court dismissed the first case was not a bar to recharging defendant because the case had never been before a jury. It held that jeopardy, under the U.S. Const. Amend V and Tex. Const. art. I. § 14, had not attached, and the prosecution was not barred from re-charging defendant. Similarly, the court held that collateral estoppel also did not apply because defendant was never put in jeopardy in the first case. The case was remanded for the information could be reinstated.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the prosecution's information be reinstated because neither the double jeopardy clause of the United States nor the Texas Constitutions barred prosecution of defendant as no jury was ever empanelled. It also held that collateral estoppel was also not appropriate because defendant must have first showed that jeopardy already attached to be successful.

Hixson v. State


NUMBERS 13-97-288-CR AND 13-97-349-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


969 S.W.2d 102; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2369



April 23, 1998, Delivered  
April 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 11, 1998. Rehearing Denied June 11, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 28th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 28th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which denied his pre-trial writ of habeas corpus and his pre-trial motion to dismiss, and found him guilty of the felony offense of driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of driving while intoxicated after the lower court denied his writ of habeas corpus and his motion to dismiss, both based on the argument that because he was not indicted timely, the charge should have been dismissed. The court found that Tex. Gen. Laws 317, 441 (current version at Tex. Code Crim. Pro. Ann. art. 32.01), required that the indictment be presented against a defendant at the next term of the court which was held after his commitment or admission to bail. The court determined that whether the section had been complied with depended upon which court's terms applied. It held that the relevant terms were those of the district court in which the initial appearance, where the decision to detain in custody or hold to bail, was made. Because appellant did not include the name of the court that set his bail, the court held that he failed to meet his burden of showing a violation of the statute. As such, it concluded that it the lower court did not err in denying appellant's writ of habeas corpus or his motion to dismiss. The court affirmed the denial of both motions and affirmed his conviction of driving while intoxicated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of appellant's writ of habeas corpus and his motion to dismiss holding that he failed to meet his burden of showing that the delay in his indictment violated the law, and affirmed his conviction.

Salvatierra v. Via Metro. Transit Auth.


No. 04-96-00897-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


974 S.W.2d 179; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2448



April 22, 1998, Delivered  
April 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 224th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 91-CI-04281. Honorable David Berchelmann, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a negligence and product liability action, appellant parent sought review of the decision from the 224th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas) that found for appellant but limited the damages to $ 100,000 on a theory of sovereign immunity under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 101.023(b).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, parent of minor, sued appellee transit authority, in negligence and product liability for injuries the minor child sustained when a bus hit him. The trial court granted partial summary judgment in favor of appellant. Appellee tendered $ 100,000 to the trial court, which entered a summary judgment limiting the damages to that amount on a theory of sovereign immunity under the Texas Tort Claims Act, Tex. Civ. Appellant challenged the constitutionality of the cap on damages provided in the Texas Tort Claims Act as applied to a personal injury claim against appellee, claiming that the statute violated the open courts doctrine and the equal protection provision under Tex. The fact that bus transportation was at one time provided by private bus companies did not abrogate the legislature's authority under its general police powers to later reclassify the function of a regional transit authority as exclusively governmental. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the constitutionality of the cap on damages provided in the Texas Tort Claims Act as applied to appellant's personal injury claim against appellee because appellee was a public entity created in accordance with a statute which provided limited waiver of liability pursuant to the Tort Claims Act.

Smith v. State


No. 06-97-00105-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


968 S.W.2d 490; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2298


February 26, 1998, Submitted  
April 21, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 102nd Judicial District Court. Red River County, Texas. Trial Court No. 102-CR-8-96.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the 102nd Judicial District Court, Red River County (Texas), for aggravated sexual assault of a child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that his conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child was improper because he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The reviewing court upheld the conviction. A defendant claiming ineffective assistance of counsel must prove that counsel's representation fell so below an objective standard of reasonableness that it undermined the proper functioning of the adversarial process that the trial cannot be relied on as having produced a just result. Here, the lack of an accomplice witness instruction was harmless error, given other detailed corroborating testimony. His counsel's failure to cross-examine the victim's mother was merely a reasonable trial strategy. Additionally, Tex. Penal Code § 8.04 (1994), which disallowed proof of intoxication to negate intent, was constitutional. Intoxication is self-induced, in contrast with a disease or mental defect.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for aggravated sexual assault of a child was affirmed because certain reasonable trial strategies did not constitute ineffective assistance of counsel.

 

708 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


McMorris v. State


No. 05-92-02893-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2285



April 20, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 363rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-42016-RW.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction from the 363rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas) for capital murder while committing a burglary of a habitation, in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1994). Appellant alleged that the evidence was factually and legally insufficient to establish his specific intent to murder and that he received ineffective counsel due to the discriminatory exclusion of jurors.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of capital murder committed during a burglary in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.03(a)(2) (1994). Appellant claimed that there was insufficient evidence to establish that he specifically intended to kill the victim. Appellant also alleged that he received ineffective counsel because of the discriminatory exclusion of prospective jurors. Appellant claimed that he did intend to burglarize the house and rape the victim, but when she pulled the gun from under the bed, he accidentally shot her after they struggled. The court affirmed appellant's conviction and held that appellant's use of a gun and his failure to seek medical attention for the victim and the theft from the premises inferred that appellant specifically intended to kill the victim. The court found that one juror was properly excused for cause after she vacillated and stated that her beliefs biased her against appellee state. Appellee state properly used a peremptory challenge to excuse a juror because, in finding racial neutrality in the strike, counsel's failure to seek complete racial information on the jury did not prejudice the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for capital murder. The court held that appellant's specific intent to murder was found by his use of a gun, his failure to seek medical attention for the victim, and his theft from the residence after the shooting was committed. The court also held that there were no racially motivated reasons for exclusion of jurors, and that counsel did not commit any errors that prejudiced appellant's case.

Booher v. State


NO. 14-96-01126-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2260



April 16, 1998, Judgment Rendered  
April 16, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 232nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 704966.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the 232nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which adjudicated defendant guilty after revoking a plea bargain agreement on the basis of defendant's violation of community supervision pursuant to Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 §5 (1998). Defendant had pled no contest to the offense of indecent exposure, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §21.08 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had pled no contest to the offense of indecent exposure, Tex. Penal Code Ann. §21.08 (1994), pursuant to a plea bargain agreement. The trial court subsequently found that defendant had violated the terms of community supervision, pursuant to Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, §5 (1998), and sentenced him to serve a jail term. The court dismissed defendant's appeal for lack of jurisdiction. The court refused to hear defendant's appeal on the merits because they held that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, §5(b) prohibited defendant from appealing the trial court's determination to proceed with an adjudication of guilt from a deferred adjudication. Defendant had sought to challenge the validity of the conditions imposed as part of his deferred adjudication and the adequacy of the state's motion alleging a violation of one of the conditions.


OUTCOME: The court refused to hear defendant's appeal for lack of jurisdiction. The court held that the Texas Code Criminal Procedure prohibited defendant from challenging the validity of the condition imposed as part of a deferred adjudication or the adequacy of the state's motion alleging a violation of one of the conditions.

Holford v. City of Houston


NO. 01-97-00296-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2265



April 16, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 295th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 95-034862.

This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Appellant's Motion for Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of March 19, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1743.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment of the 295th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which denied his claims for an injunction against appellee city to enjoin abatement of the mowing of his grass and for a declaratory judgment that his lawn was not in violation of a penal ordinance, Houston, Tex., Code of Ordinances ch. 10, art. XI, § 10-451(b)(10) (1985), and for damages for his lost time and expenses.


OVERVIEW: Appellant sued appellee city to enjoin abatement of the mowing of his grass, and for a declaratory judgment that his lawn was not in violation of appellee city's ordinance, Houston, Tex., Code of Ordinances ch. 10, art. XI, § 10-451(b)(10) (1985), and for damages for his lost time and expenses. Section 10-451(b)(10) was a criminal misdemeanor ordinance, and appellant was being prosecuted for its violation in municipal court. The district court denied appellant any relief. Appellant sought review. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that a court of equity could not interfere with enforcement of a penal ordinance unless it was unconstitutional and enforcement threatened irreparable injury to personal rights or property rights. The court found that appellant did not argue on appeal that he would have suffered irreparable harm or that the ordinance was unconstitutional, and thus the court held that the district court did not have jurisdiction to interfere with the criminal prosecution. Whether or not appellant violated appellee's ordinance had to be decided by the municipal court. The court found that a number of the other points raised were moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of appellant's request for an injunction, holding that the ordinance in question was penal, and equity could not interfere with a penal ordinance unless it was unconstitutional and its enforcement threatened irreparable injury to personal rights or property rights. The court found that appellant did not argue that he would have suffered irreparable harm or that the ordinance was unconstitutional.
