Faerman v. State


NO. 14-96-00112-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


966 S.W.2d 843; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2127



April 9, 1998, Judgment Rendered  
April 9, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of January 29, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 641.

On Appeal from the 262nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 660801.



DISPOSITION: Motion for Rehearing Overruled; Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 262nd District Court (Texas) adjudicating him guilty of possession of cocaine for failing to abide by the conditions of probation and sentencing him to 12 years confinement. Appellant argued that the trial court erred in failing to conduct a punishment hearing before sentencing him to the penitentiary and that his counsel was ineffective when he failed to object to the absence of a punishment hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant plead guilty to possession of less than 28 grams of cocaine, but the trial court deferred a finding of guilt and placed him under the terms and conditions of probation for a period of five years in accordance with the terms of a plea bargain agreement. Two years later, the trial court adjudicated appellant's guilt for failing to abide by the conditions of probation and sentenced him to 12 years confinement. On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court erred in failing to conduct a punishment hearing before sentencing him to the penitentiary and that his counsel was ineffective when he failed to object to the absence of a punishment hearing. The appeals court affirmed. The court ruled that although the trial court erred in failing to conduct a second phase punishment hearing after adjudicating the previously deferred finding of guilt, appellant failed to preserve the error by not objecting or filing a motion for a new trial. The court also rejected appellant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel because his counsel had called numerous witnesses at the adjudication hearing and had presented testimony aimed at mitigating appellant's punishment.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the trial court judgment adjudicating appellant on a previously deferred finding of guilt and sentencing him to 12 years confinement. The court ruled that appellant did not preserve the trial court's error in failing to conduct a separate punishment hearing because he did not object or file a motion for a new trial.

Tex. Bar v. McGee


NUMBER 13-96-378-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


972 S.W.2d 770; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2136



April 9, 1998, Delivered  
April 9, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On appeal from the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Order granting McGee's motion for summary judgment REVERSED, and take-nothing judgment RENDERED in favor of State Bar.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state bar sought review of the judgment of the 93rd District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas) after it granted summary judgment in favor of appellee attorney. Before the court was whether the lower court had jurisdiction over a declaratory judgment action filed by appellee.


OVERVIEW: Appellant state bar initiated internal grievance committee proceedings against appellee attorney because of appellee's television and billboard advertisements. The lower court granted appellee's motion for a summary judgment. Before the court was whether the lower court had jurisdiction over a declaratory judgment action filed in another court by appellee. The lower court judgment was reversed. The court held that under the doctrine of primary jurisdiction, the appropriate standard of review was to ascertain whether the lower court abused its discretion in assuming jurisdiction. The court found that the lower court abused its discretion. The court determined that as a general rule, an action for declaratory judgment would not be entertained if there was another action pending between the same parties and in which the issues involved in the declaratory action could be adjudicated. The court concluded that the lower court was without jurisdiction to consider appellee's petition for declaratory judgment. Accordingly, a take-nothing judgment was rendered in favor of appellant.


OUTCOME: The lower court judgment that granted summary judgment to appellee attorney was reversed. The court held that the lower court was without jurisdiction over the declaratory action brought by appellee and entered a take-nothing judgment in favor of appellant state bar.

Villalobos v. State


NUMBER 13-95-293-CR &, 13-95-294-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2139



April 9, 1998, Delivered  
April 9, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 357th District Court of Cameron County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant convict challenged the judgment of the 357th District Court (Texas), which convicted him of aggravated robbery and aggravated kidnapping. Appellant raised numerous issues on appeal, including that the trial court erred by not having him execute a written waiver of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was tried for aggravated robbery and aggravated kidnapping. He was found guilty and sentenced by a jury after he represented himself pro se, having demanded the discharge of his court appointed counsel and the right to represent himself at trial. On appeal, appellant argued that the trial court erred by not having him execute a written waiver of counsel and did not adequately admonish him about the dangers of self-representation. Appellant also argued that the trial court erred in letting the jury view him inside the courtroom wearing restraints. The appeals court affirmed the convictions. The court ruled that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in trying the case with leg restraints on appellant because he had been belligerent and violent during several court hearings, including on the day of trial. The court also ruled that while it was mandatory for the trial judge to provide appellant with a written waiver form to sign pursuant to Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 1.051(g), appellant waived the right to a written waiver by failing to object to the trial court's failure to provide the form.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed appellant's aggravated robbery and aggravated kidnapping convictions because the trial court committed no reversible error. The court ruled that although the trial court failed to follow the mandatory provisions requiring a written waiver of counsel, appellant waived his right to such written waiver by failing to object at trial.

Reynolds v. State


NO. 01-96-00779-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


967 S.W.2d 493; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 2152



April 9, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted October 21, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6 Harris County, Texas. J. R. Musslewhite, JUDGE. Trial Court Cause No. 9554573.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 6, Harris County (Texas), for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: A police officer observed defendant operating his vehicle in an erratic manner. After defendant was pulled over, the officer noticed that defendant's eyes were red and his speech slurred. Defendant was charged with driving while intoxicated. At an administrative license revocation hearing, the judge declined to suspend defendant's license because there was no reasonable suspicion to stop defendant. Defendant was convicted and contended that the doctrine of collateral estoppel barred the state from relitigating the reasonable suspicion issue. Defendant also contended that the trial court gave an incomplete charge. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction. The state was not barred from relitigating the reasonable suspicion issue because the doctrine of collateral estoppel did not arise from administrative license revocation hearings. The charge, regarding the officer's reasonable suspicion, sufficiently complied with Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 38.23 and did not need to include the article's specific language to be proper.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction. Collateral estoppel did not bar the state from relitigating the reasonable suspicion issue because such doctrine did not arise from administrative license revocation hearings. The jury charge, regarding the officer's reasonable suspicion, was sufficient, even though it did not contain specified statutory language.

DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the 209th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which convicted defendant of two counts of credit card abuse and revoked his community service due to a violation of Tex. Penal § 37.10 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of credit card abuse and the trial court placed him on community supervision. The state filed a motion to revoke probation, alleging that defendant tampered with governmental records, specifically an application for an identification card, in violation of Tex. Penal § 37.10 (1994). Defendant filed a motion to dismiss, claiming that § 37.10 was invalid because it was void and overbroad, sought to criminalize actions that were not criminal, and failed to give adequate notice as to what was the penalty for the acts considered a violation. The motion to dismiss was overruled and defendant appealed, contending that § 37.10 was constitutionally vague as to what was a governmental record. The court affirmed the trial court's order revoking defendant's community supervision because § 37.10 was not unconstitutional because defendant had fair notice that a state-issued identification card and the application therefor were issued or received by state government and would have constituted government records.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which revoked defendant's community supervision, because defendant had fair notice that a state-issued identification card and the application therefor were issued or received by the state government and would have constituted government records.

Hawk Leasing Co. v. Texas Workforce Comm'n


No. 05-96-01116-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


971 S.W.2d 598; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1926



March 31, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 68th Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 96-10025-C.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employer sought review of an order of the 68th Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which denied his motion for summary judgment and granted appellee Texas Workforce Commission's motion for summary judgment in an action regarding appellee's administrative order requiring appellant to pay one of its former employees disputed wages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employer sought review of an order that denyied his motion for summary judgment and granted the motion for summary judgment of appellee Texas Workforce Commission, formerly known as the Texas Employment Commission (TEC), in an action regarding appellee's administrative order requiring appellant to pay a former employee disputed wages. The court found that, because the trial court's judgment provided that the employee both could and could not recover on his wage claim, the judgment was void for being irreconcilable on its face. On appellee's cross-point regarding jurisdiction, the court held that Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §61.063(b), which conditioned the right to judicial review of the administrative order on payment of the disputed wages, violated Tex. Const. art. I, § 13 by unconstitutionally restricting access to the courts. However, because Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §63.062(a)(2) did not have the same condition, the trial court erred in declaring it unconstitutional. Accordingly, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment to the extent that it declared Tex. Lab. Code Ann. §61.063(b) unconstitutional, but reversed it in all other respects.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment to the extent that it declared unconstitutional a statute, which conditioned the right to judicial review of the administrative order on payment of the disputed wages. It reversed, however, the order in all other respects because the judgment was void for being irreconcilable on its face and improperly declared unconstitutional a statute that did not improperly restrict assess to the courts.

DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision from the 144th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas), wherein defendant was indicted for first degree offense of intentional injury to a child resulting in serious bodily injury pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04(a)(1)(1994) and was found guilty by a jury of the lesser included offense of reckless injury to a child and was sentenced to four years' confinement with a fine of $ 5000.00.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for first degree offense of intentional injury to a child resulting in serious bodily injury pursuant to Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.04(a)(1)(1994). At trial, defendant required that the trial court include in its charge to the jury the lesser included offense of reckless injury to a child. On appeal, defendant raised 14 points of error including that the evidence was legally insufficient to support a charge of the lesser included offense. Lerma v. State


NO. 03-96-00678-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1842



March 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BURNET COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 7996, HONORABLE CLAYTON E. EVANS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant, convicted of assaulting a police officer by a jury sitting in the District Court of Burnet County, 33rd Judicial District (Texas), challenged his conviction and sentence on multiple grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant, convicted of assaulting a police officer, unsuccessfully challenged his conviction on multiple grounds. The court rejected his claim that the evidence against him was legally insufficient because the record revealed a basis for the jury to conclude that the officer assaulted was performing his duties at the time. The court also rejected his claim that he was entitled to certain lesser-included offense instructions because of the lack of evidence supporting such offenses. The court found that the error in denying appellant permission to cross-examine a prosecution witness about her prior arrests was harmless. The court held that appellant's claim that the trial court erroneously failed to instruct the jury at the sentencing phase regarding his parole eligibility was waived and was not fundamental error. Finally, the court held that appellant had not been denied his right to the effective assistance of counsel given the totality of counsel's performance.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence were affirmed. The evidence was legally sufficient, omitted lesser-included offense instructions were not supported by the evidence, the erroneous restriction on his cross-examination was harmless, a sentencing instruction was waived, and counsel's performance overall was effective.

Gonzales v. State


NUMBER 13-97-836-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1874



March 26, 1998, Delivered  
March 26, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the County Criminal Court of Harris County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the County Criminal Court of Harris County (Texas), which convicted him pursuant to a guilty plea of abuse of a corpse in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.08. The appeal was based on the denial of appellant's pre-trial motion to quash the information on the grounds that § 42.08 was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: Appellant plead guilty to the offense of abuse of a corpse in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 42.08 and was sentenced to 85 days confinement in the county jail. He appealed, contending that the trial court erred by denying his pre-trial motion to quash the information. Appellant had contended that § 42.08 was unconstitutionally vague. The statute stated that a person committed the offense of abuse of a corpse if, not authorized by law, he intentionally or knowingly disinterred, disturbed, removed, dissected, in whole or in part, carried away, or treated in a seriously offensive manner a human corpse. The court affirmed, holding that it did not consider § 42.08 to be unconstitutionally vague. In particular, a statute was not unconstitutionally vague merely because the words or terms used were not defined. Moreover, the court rejected appellant's argument that literal enforcement of the statute could prevent persons such as nurses, ambulance drivers, and gravediggers from doing their jobs. This argument ignored the clause "not authorized by law" in the first sentence of the section.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for abuse of a corpse because the court did not consider the statute prohibiting abuse of a corpse to be unconstitutionally vague.

 

722 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


In the Interest of Shaw


No. 08-96-00351-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


966 S.W.2d 174; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1968



March 26, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 7, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted on Denial of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of November 6, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5813.

Appeal from 318th District Court of Midland County, Texas. (TC # DR-25,412). TRIAL COURT JUDGE: Hon. Royal Hart.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged an order from 318th District Court of Midland County (Texas), which terminated the parental rights of appellant as to three children, and which terminated the parent-child relationship between two children and their father.


OVERVIEW: Appellant mother failed to maintain contact with her children following their placement in state care. This was a violation of her service plan and as a result the state was successful in seeking a termination of her parental rights. The appellate court found that while appellant's behavior did constitute constructive abandonment of her children, the penalty imposed was inappropriate. Under statutes in effect at the time appellant violated her service plan, the penalty for this conduct would have been an inability for appellant to regain managing conservatorship of her children. Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 161.001(N), which implemented the penalty of termination of parental rights for constructive abandonment, became effective nearly a year after the date that the requisite statutory period of abandonment commenced for appellant. The appellate court held that the statute was applied retroactively in violation of appellant's constitutional protections. That portion of the trial court's order terminating appellant's parental rights was reversed and remanded to the trial court. The portion of the order terminating the father's rights to two of the children was not appealed and was affirmed.


OUTCOME: An order terminating appellant's parental rights was reversed and the cause was remanded because the statute which imposed the termination penalty for constructive abandonment became effective after the start of the statutory period under which appellant's abandonment was determined. The father of two of the children did not appeal the termination of his rights, and that portion of the order was affirmed.

Steinmetz v. State


No. 06-97-00080-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


968 S.W.2d 427; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1788


February 12, 1998, Submitted  
March 24, 1998, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 276th Judicial District Court. Morris County, Texas. Trial Court No. 7503.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision of the 276th Judicial District Court, Morris County, Texas, which convicted appellant for the delivery of marihuana, denied a writ of habeas corpus for failure to present a timely indictment under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01, 28.061 (1989), and denied a motion to quash the indictment on speedy trial grounds under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.05 (1977).


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted for the delivery of marihuana, assessed a punishment of two years confinement, and fined. Defendant filed a writ of habeas corpus, which sought a dismissal for failure to present a timely indictment under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01, 28.061 (1989). Defendant also filed a motion to quash the indictment on speedy trial grounds under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 1.05 (1977). The trial court denied appellant's writ and motion. Defendant sought review, but the court affirmed the trial court. The court held that under art. 32.01 a defendant was required to be indicted by the next term of the trial court after commitment or admission to bail. Appellant was arrested and released on bond during the January 1996 term of the trial court and was timely indicted during the next term in May 1996. The complaint was moot, however, because appellant did not file before the indictment. There was no right to counsel before indictment. The state showed good cause for the delay. The right to a speedy trial was not violated under the balancing test because appellant actively sought continuances and did not timely assert the speedy trial right.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision that convicted appellant for the delivery of marihuana, and the writ of habeas corpus was properly denied because the indictment was timely filed in the next term after appellant's arrest. Appellant's right to a speedy trial was not violated under the balancing test because appellant sought continuances and the right was not timely asserted.

Ex parte Torres


No. 04-96-00161-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


966 S.W.2d 723; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1960



March 18, 1998, Delivered  
March 18, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied March 18, 1998. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted in part and Refused in part and Judgment Vacated June 16, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Tex. Crim. App. LEXIS 76.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 226th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95-CR-3923. Honorable Sid L. Harle, Judge Presiding.

Original Opinion of February 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 841.



DISPOSITION: MOTION FOR CONSIDERATION EN BANC GRANTED; MOTION FOR REHEARING DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state filed motions for rehearing and for consideration after defendant filed a pre-trial habeas corpus appeal from the 226th Judicial District Court, Bexar County (Texas) for a delayed indictment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed a petition for habeas corpus resulting from a delayed indictment. After the court's review, the state filed motions for rehearing and for consideration, claiming the court did not have jurisdiction. The court held that it had jurisdiction to review the timeliness of an indictment as a habeas corpus appeal because timeliness was not a sufficiency issue; it was more akin to a limitations issue. The court determined that Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. §32.01 and Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. §28.061 did not unduly interfere with the prosecutor's preparation of a case because it was similar to the interference of statutes of limitations. The court determined that a prosecutor could request an extension of time in which to file an indictment and held that while a speedy indictment is not expressly guaranteed, a prosecutor cannot hold a person under arrest or its equivalent indefinitely. The court held that the statutes were constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court denied the relief requested and determined it had standing to hear a pre-trial habeas corpus challenge based on a delayed indictment and held that the combination of statutes which required an indictment be timely filed were constitutional.

State v. Read


NO. 03-97-00186-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


965 S.W.2d 74; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1532



March 12, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 2 OF HAYS COUNTY. NO. 43,663, HONORABLE LINDA A. RODRIGUEZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state challenged an order from the County Court, Hays County (Texas), where the court granted appellee's motion for a new trial after learning that a juror failed to disclose her criminal record during voir dire.


OVERVIEW: Appellee was convicted of driving while intoxicated and sought a new trial on the grounds that one of the juror's failed to disclose her criminal record during voir dire. The trial court granted appellee's motion for a new trial and the state appealed. The state argued that appellee failed to show significant harm from the juror's misconduct. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment. According to the appeals court, the rules of appellate procedure list specific grounds for which a new trial must be granted. The appeals court held that the grounds included when a juror had been bribed to convict or was guilty of any other corrupt conduct, and when the jury had engaged in such misconduct that the accused did not receive a fair and impartial trial. The appeals court continued and held that a juror's intentional misrepresentation of material information in the voir dire process was grounds for a new trial. In addition, the appeals court held that trial court had discretion to grant a new trial for other reasons not listed in the appellate rules. The appeals court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in granting appellee's motion for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgment granting appellee's motion for a new trial because a juror's intentional misrepresentation of material information in the voir dire process was grounds for a new trial.

Wyatt v. Bass, Higdon & Hardy, Inc.


No. 04-97-00672-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1443



March 11, 1998, Delivered  
March 11, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion for Rehearing Denied May 19, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the County Court at Law No. 2, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 233,892. Honorable Shay Gebhardt, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant client sought review of a judgment of the County Court at Law No. 2, Bexar County, Texas that was in favor of appellee lawyer and appellee law firm in appellant's suit for conversion and on appellee law firm's counterclaims for sworn account and breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: Pending finalization of appellant client's divorce, all payments made to appellant and his wife on their property were made to appellee lawyer as their trustee. After appellant fired appellee lawyer, appellant's wife sold the property without his consent and forwarded the proceeds to appellee lawyer who deposited the money in a trust account. Appellee sued appellee lawyer and appellee law firm for conversion. Appellee law firm counterclaimed for sworn account and breach of contract. The trial court entered judgment in favor of appellees on the conversion claim and appellee law firm's counterclaims. Appellant sought review, and the court affirmed. Appellant alleged on appeal that he was denied his right to a jury trial. The right to jury trial in a civil matter was not absolute; rather, the right had to be perfected by requesting a jury and paying the jury trial fee. Even so, the right could be waived by failing to object when the trial court proceeded without a jury, which appellant failed to do. Even had appellant not waived his right, it was not error to proceed without a jury because no other judgment could have been rendered but the judgment that was rendered.


OUTCOME: Judgment in favor of appellee lawyer and appellee law firm on appellant client's claim of conversion and appellee law firm's counterclaims for sworn account and breach of contract was affirmed. The trial court did not err by proceeding without a jury, as requested by appellant, because appellant failed to object at trial, and no other judgment could have been rendered but for appellees.

Hawkins v. State


NO. 09-96-180 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


964 S.W.2d 767; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1542


January 8, 1998, Submitted  
March 11, 1998, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the County Court. Tyler County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 94-0083. Honorable Jerome Owens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Court of Tyler County (Texas), which convicted him of driving while intoxicated. Defendant contended the court erred because his federal and state rights to due process were violated by the police officers' failure to act upon his request for a blood test.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for driving while intoxicated. A game warden saw defendant driving into a park at 1:00 a.m., administered field sobriety tests that indicated defendant was intoxicated, and called in sheriff's officers who took defendant to the county jail. Defendant agreed to take a breath test, but the officers could not make the machine work. Defendant testified that he asked for a blood test, but none of the officers recalled the request and an officer testified that a blood test was not performed because defendant was belligerent. Defendant therefore had no objective evidence with which to refute the officers' opinions regarding his inebriated state. The appellate court affirmed the judgment and sentence because as a prerequisite to presenting a complaint for review, the record must demonstrate the complaint was made to the lower court by a timely request, objection, or motion. Holding the lower court did not abuse its discretion in overruling defendant's motion for new trial, the court held claims presented by defendant for the first time on appeal involved constitutional rights for which he sought no relief from the lower court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of driving while intoxicated. The court found that the lower court properly overruled defendant's motion for new trial because he failed to demonstrate the evidence was material. The court held that the claims defendant presented for the first time on appeal also involved constitutional rights for which he sought no relief from the lower court, and was precluded from raising on appeal.

Graham v. State


NO. 09-95-355 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


964 S.W.2d 738; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1465


December 4, 1997, Submitted  
March 4, 1998, Opinion Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted September 16, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 252nd District Court Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Court No. 70800. Honorable Leonard Giblin, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 252nd District Court, Jefferson County (Texas), which entered her guilty plea to aggravated kidnapping and assessed punishment at 10 years' confinement. Appellant contended that she had immunity, based upon an agreement with police in one county, and that denial of her suppression motion was erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant entered into an immunity agreement with the county sheriff. Another county brought charges based on the information given by appellant to the other county sheriff, on the charge of aggravated kidnapping. Appellant alleged that the trial court committed reversible error by not granting her immunity based on the prosecution's promise of immunity from prosecution in exchange for information of a crime unknown to the state. The court found that the immunity agreement was exclusive with the county sheriff and did not apply to the other county. The trial court found that she could be prosecuted because she failed to obtain district court approval or the other county's approval of the agreement. Also, appellant failed to show that the complained of evidence was obtained through the use of information she gave in her confession, which the trial court held was inadmissible. The court did not find that any of the complained of evidence, other than her confession, was illegally obtained thus constituting fruit of the poisonous tree. The court affirmed the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for aggravated kidnapping, based upon her guilty plea and assessed punishment at 10 years' confinement. The court did not find that any of the complained of evidence, other than her confession, was illegally obtained, and suppression was therefore properly denied. Appellant failed to get district approval for immunity, which was not applicable between counties.

Elizondo v. State

February 27, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 229th Judicial District Court, Duval County, Texas. Trial Court No. 5561. Honorable John L. McKellips, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the District Court of Duval County (Texas), that modified and subsequently revoked his probation, alleging the trial court abused its discretion by revoking his probation for failure to perform community service. Appellant also asserted that he was entitled to an attorney when his probation was modified.


OVERVIEW: The trial court sentenced appellant for burglary of a building after it revoked his probation. Appellant sought review, alleging the trial court abused its discretion by revoking his probation for failure to perform community service. Upon review, the court affirmed the revocation. It noted that an unexcused failure to comply with the terms of probation for failure to perform community service was sufficient to support revocation. Furthermore, because the revocation was affirmed, it was unnecessary to consider appellant's allegation that he was entitled to an attorney when his probation was modified, because as probation revocation was upheld on one ground, insufficiency of other grounds would not render the judgment erroneous.


OUTCOME: The order revoking appellant's probation and imposing sentence was affirmed because appellant's unexcused failure to perform community service as required by the terms of his probation was sufficient to support revocation.

Frenzel v. State


No. 10-97-223-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TENTH DISTRICT, WACO


963 S.W.2d 911; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 1119



February 25, 1998, Delivered  
February 25, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 7, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 278th District Court Madison County, Texas. Trial Court # 8372.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order of the 278th District Court, Madison County (Texas), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus and refused to dismiss an indictment against him that was not returned by the end of the next term of court following his arrest and admission to bail as required by statute.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and charged with the offense of deadly conduct in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 22.05 (1994). Appellant was released on bail but was not indicted until a year later. Appellant filed a petition for a writ of habeas corpus and sought to have the indictment dismissed under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01, which required the discharge of indictments not returned before the end of the next term of court after which a defendant was confined or admitted to bail. The trial court denied the petition and the court affirmed the order of the trial court. The court held that art. 28.061 violated the separation of powers provision of Tex. Const. art. II, § 1 because it impermissibly intruded on the prosecution's exclusive discretion to prepare cases for presentation to the grand jury. Because art. 28.061 was unconstitutional and the grand jury returned an indictment against appellant before the trial court ruled on appellant's habeas corpus petition, the court determined that appellant's claim of an untimely indictment was moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that denied appellant's petition for a writ of habeas corpus because a statute that barred further prosecution of offenses which had been discharged for untimely indictment was an unconstitutional infringement of the prosecution's exclusive discretion to prepare cases for presentation to the grand jury.

State v. Powell


No. 05-96-01891-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


971 S.W.2d 577; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 941



February 17, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 380th District Court. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 380-80338-95.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the dismissal of the indictment against defendant from the 380th District Court, Collin County, Texas, a dismissal pursuant to the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act (IADA), Tex. Code. Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 51.14 (1979). The state contended that the trial court erred in dismissal because the 180-day time limit had not expired, the delay was agreed to, excludable time periods were included, and the IADA was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for the property theft. At that time, he was incarcerated in a state correctional institution. Pursuant to the indictment's detainer, defendant was moved to a county justice center. Over five months later, the trial court held a hearing on defendant's motion to dismiss the indictment under the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act (IADA), art. IV(c). The trial court granted the motion, finding that defendant had been in the county justice center for a period of more than 120 days. The trial court amended its order, finding that defendant's dismissal was warranted under a different article and that 180 days had elapsed without justifiable excuse or delay attributable to the state or defendant. The court reversed the trial court's order, finding that defendant's letter to the county district clerk did not satisfy the notice requirements of the IADA and the 180 day deadline did not begin to run. In addition, the record showed that defense counsel agreed to postponements totaling a period of 107 days, a period sufficient to toll the 180 day period well past the date the trial court dismissed the indictment and the day the case was set for jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment because defendant's letter to the county district clerk did not satisfy the notice requirements of the Interstate Agreement on Detainers Act. Also, the 180 day statutory period was tolled 107 days by agreement of defense counsel, a time sufficient to put the case well past the date the trial court dismissed the indictment and the day the case was set for jury trial.

Spellmon v. Collins


NO. 14-97-00032-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


970 S.W.2d 578; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 899



February 12, 1998, Rendered  
February 12, 1998, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 12th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 18,518. William McAdams, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a prison inmate, sought review of an order of 12th District Court of Walker County (Texas), which granted summary judgment to appellees in a suit by appellant alleging that he was falsely charged with a disciplinary case for conspiring to create a disturbance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a prison inmate who sued appellee guards for falsely charging him with a disciplinary case for creating a disturbance, argued trial court error in failing to sanction appellees for the attorney general's lack of strict compliance with the rules of substitution when appellees' counsel changed. The court disagreed, ruling that appellant failed to show how appellees' counsel's failure to file the appropriate documents injured him. Moreover, the refusal to sanction appellees for not serving him with their exceptions to his motion for summary judgment was proper; the exceptions had been sent to his address of record because appellant did not file with the court his new prison address. Moreover, evidence showed that appellant received appellees' cross-motion for summary judgment and that appellant's motion to strike it was properly dismissed, given that the substituted counsel's formal motion for substitution was filed and approved before a ruling on the strike was made. Finally, appellant's challenge of the disciplinary procedures used to impose punishments was not cognizable under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 absent any allegation that the punishments had been invalidated.


OUTCOME: Order affirmed granting appellees summary judgment in appellant inmate's suit alleging that he was falsely charged with a disciplinary case, as a challenge to procedure for imposing punishment was not cognizable under § 1983 unless punishment had been invalidated, as appellant was not injured by appellees' counsel failing to timely file substitution papers, and as appellant was properly served with exceptions to his summary judgment motion.

Fleming Foods v. Sharp


NO. 03-97-00316-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 702



February 5, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 53RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 96-12390, HONORABLE JOHN K. DIETZ, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant buyer sought review of the decision of the District Court of Travis County, 53rd Judicial District (Texas), which ruled in favor of appellee comptroller in appellant's action protesting a deficiency assessment for additional Interstate Motor Carrier Sales and Use Tax pursuant to Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 157.102.


OVERVIEW: Appellant buyer filed suit against appellee comptroller seeking a refund. Appellant purchased from seller a fleet of trucks for use in interstate transportation of goods. The seller previously operated the vehicles on routes through Texas and New Mexico, and appellant used the vehicles along the same routes, serving same points of delivery. Appellant remitted to state, its amount of Interstate Motor Carrier Sales and Use Tax, calculated under Tex. Tax Code Ann. § 157.102. After an audit, appellant was issued a deficiency assessment. Appellant argued that § 157.102 required the use of seller's mileage factor in assessing the tax and that the lower court erred in holding that the tax did not violate the commerce clause. The court affirmed and held that the plain language of the statute required that the carrier's mileage factor be used. The court stated that it was reasonable to anticipate that the acquiring carrier would conform the use of a new vehicle to its existing routes. The court held that the tax was not violative of the commerce clause because the tax was a fair apportionment under § 157.102.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed judgment assessing appellant buyer a deficiency amount for additional Interstate Motor Carrier Sales and Use Tax , in favor of appellee comptroller. The court stated that the tax was correctly computed because the statute stated that carrier's mileage factor be used and that the tax was the carrier's responsibility. The court stated that the tax was not violative of commerce clause because apportionment was reasonable.

 

738 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Reading & Bates Constr. Co. v. Baker Energy Resources Corp.


NO. 01-95-01526-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


976 S.W.2d 702; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 763



February 5, 1998, Opinion Issued


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 334th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 92-56111. Russell Lloyd, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 334th District Court, Harris County (Texas), contending the lower court erred when it denied recognition to and enforcement of a Canadian judgment against appellee under the Uniform Foreign Country Money-Judgment Recognition Act and when it refused to give full faith and credit through the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act to a Louisiana judgment that recognized the same Canadian judgment.


OVERVIEW: A Canadian court entered a judgment that appellee infringed appellant's Canadian patents. Appellant obtained a judgment from a Louisiana court that the Canadian judgment was executory. Appellant later filed the Canadian judgment for recognition under the Uniform Foreign Country Money-Judgment Recognition Act, (UFCMJRA), Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. §§ 36.003, 36.005(b)(3), (7), in the trial court in Texas. The trial court granted appellee's motion for non-recognition. The trial court also refused recognition of the Louisiana judgment under the Uniform Enforcement of Foreign Judgments Act, because it regarded this as a "back door" attempt to domesticate the Canadian judgment. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred if it concluded as a matter of law that recognition of the Canadian judgment should be denied based on lack of reciprocity under the UFCMJRA. However, the Louisiana judgment was not entitled to full faith and credit because the recognition of foreign country judgments involved looking behind the judgment to evaluate both the law upon which it was based and the jurisdictional environment in which it was rendered. The court reversed and remanded.


OUTCOME: While the court refused to recognize the Louisiana judgment, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court denying recognition to and enforcement of the Canadian judgment because there appeared to be reciprocity in Canadian enforcement of judgments. The court remanded.

Benjamin v. State


No. 06-97-00005-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 655


February 2, 1998, Submitted  
February 3, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 71st Judicial District Court. Harrison County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-0094 X.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the decision of the 71st Judicial District Court, Harrison County, Texas, where appellant was convicted of capital murder after the juvenile court waived jurisdiction and transferred her case to the district court for trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant juvenile was convicted of capital murder and given a life sentence after the juvenile court waived jurisdiction and transferred her case to the district court. The court affirmed the judgment. The court held that Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §54.02(f) (1996) was constitutional and did not violate appellant's rights to equal treatment under the law. The court held that the fact that the state had a capital murder facility exclusively for males was not the factor that precluded appellant from being tried as a juvenile. The court also ruled that appellant's contention that her written confession was improperly obtained was not preserved for review because the issue was never presented to the trial court. The court further concluded that appellant was not denied her right to be accompanied by a third party under Tex. Fam. Code. Ann. §52.025(c) because she was with her husband during the proceedings. Finally, the court held that appellant's confession to her husband was not coerced, there was no evidence that her husband was being used as an agent of the police, and the lower court properly admitted the statements into evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant juvenile's conviction for capital murder and held that appellant's constitutional rights were not violated when the juvenile court waived jurisdiction and transferred the matter to the district court. The court further determined that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting appellant's written and oral confessions.

 

740 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Crowder


NO. 03-97-00090-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


959 S.W.2d 732; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 497



January 29, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 1, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TRAVIS COUNTY, 167TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 0960277, HONORABLE MIKE LYNCH, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought review of an order from the 167th Judicial District Court of Travis County (Texas), which denied petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner claimed that his restraint was illegal by reason of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 32.01 because he was not indicted at the very next grand jury term.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the district court's denial of petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus. Petitioner was arrested for sexual indecency with a child and was released the same day on bail. After his indictment petitioner applied for a writ of habeas corpus, which was denied without any stated grounds. Petitioner argued that he was entitled to the writ by virtue of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. art. 32.01 on the grounds that he was not indicted at the very next term of the grand jury. On review the court found that the subject article was restricted by its terms to persons who were restrained for an offense and not charged in an indictment or information. Before he was indicted, he was entitled under that rule to have an order made that would have discharged him from prosecution, but at the time petitioner invoked the article it no longer had application to him because he had since come under indictment.


OUTCOME: Denial of petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus was affirmed because by the very terms of the rule that provided for a discharge if petitioner was not indicted at the very next grand jury no longer applied to petitioner because petitioner waited until after he was indicted to invoke the rule.

 

741 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Slater v. National Med. Enters.


NO. 2-96-342-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


962 S.W.2d 228; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 594



January 29, 1998, Delivered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Denied February 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 153rd DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. KEN CURRY.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient sought review of a decision of the 153rd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas), which entered summary judgment for appellees, hospitals and doctor, on the basis of limitations under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (Supp. 1998), in appellant's suit claiming damages for medical malpractice and fraud in psychiatric treatment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant patient was treated for depression and substance abuse by appellees, hospitals and doctor. After release, appellant was married for a short time to a hospital substance abuse counselor, whom she accused of abusing her during treatment. More than five years after her last treatment, appellant brought suit against appellees, claiming fraud and malpractice. The trial court granted summary judgment to appellees under the limitations provision of Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i (Supp. 1998), and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court found that appellant's claims against appellees accrued on the last day of treatment, and that appellant's deposition established that she was on inquiry notice of any alleged fraud five years before filing suit, so that whether subject to the two-year limitations period of art. 4590i or the four-year period for common law fraud, the claims were time-barred. The court also held that duress by the counselor, a third party, could not toll limitations as to appellees, and that art. 4590i did not violate the open courts provision of Tex. Const. art. I, § 13.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's summary judgment in favor of appellees, hospitals and doctor, in appellant patient's suit claiming damages for medical malpractice and fraud in psychiatric treatment, because appellant's claims were time-barred, under either the two-year limitations period for health care suits or the four-year period for fraud actions, and limitations had not been tolled.

 

742 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Cox v. State


NO. 03-97-00015-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 500



January 29, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 16, 1998.
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 09/16/1998
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by Cox v. Cockrell, 62 Fed. Appx. 557, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 5333 (5th Cir. Tex., 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR-96-0348, HONORABLE CHARLES R. RAMSAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 22nd District Court (Texas) convicting him of theft of property valued at $ 750.00 or more, but less than $ 20,000.00. Appellant argued that the evidence was legally insufficient to establish an essential element of the offense, the intent to permanently deprive the owner of the property, and that the evidence was factually insufficient to prove the tractor's fair market value was greater than $ 750.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted by a jury of the theft of property valued at $ 750 or more, but less than $ 20,000. The evidence at trial established that appellant approached the complainant about taking her tractor in lieu of money she owed him under a contract, but she declined. Five days later, the complainant returned home to find the tractor missing. When she confronted appellant about the tractor, appellant assured her that he would return it, but never did. On appeal, appellant argued that the evidence was legally insufficient to establish the intent to permanently deprive the owner of the property, and that the evidence was factually insufficient to prove the tractor's fair market value was greater than $ 750. The appeals court affirmed because any rational trier of fact could have found the elements of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court also ruled that although there were conflicting opinions as to the value of the tractor, there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's finding. The court reasoned that the owner testified the tractor was an antique valued at $ 1,500 and appellant had offered to take the tractor in lieu of a $ 1,900 contracted agreement.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed appellant's theft conviction because any rational trier of fact could have found the elements of the offense beyond a reasonable doubt. The court ruled that the jury was entitled to infer appellant's intent to permanently deprive the owner of the property, from evidence that he took the property without the owner's permission and never returned it, despite his promise to do so.

Gilmore v. Lopez


No. 96-01029-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


974 S.W.2d 67; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 530



January 28, 1998, Delivered  
January 28, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing Denied April 6, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 37th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-CI-03421. Honorable David H. Peeples, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bondsmen challenged the decision of the 37th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee sheriff, individually and as county sheriff, based on the statute of limitations in an action concerning pre-conviction bail bond approval fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellant bail bondsmen filed a petition against the Texas Attorney General and appellee sheriff, individually and as county sheriff, alleging the unconstitutionality of collecting pre-conviction bail bond fees. Appellee sought summary judgment based on official immunity and limitations. The trial court granted appellee's motion for summary judgment, holding that a two-year statute of limitations barred appellants' claim. Appellants argued that the original petition included three causes of actions; a taking in violation, an extortion claim, and collection of a debt action. Appellants conceded that a two-year statute of limitations governed the taking and extortion causes of action. The collection of debt was governed by a four-year statute of limitations, but the court found that the facts alleged in appellants' petition failed to give notice of a claim for the collection of a debt. Accordingly, the court held that the trial court did not err in applying a two-year statute of limitations and affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting summary judgment in favor of appellee sheriff was affirmed because the trial court properly applied a two-year statute of limitations where appellant bail bondmen had merely pleaded extortion and taking causes of actions, which did not give fair and adequate notice of a debt cause of action.

Manna v. State


No. 06-97-00109-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 479


January 26, 1998, Submitted  
January 27, 1998, Decided


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 202nd Judicial District Court. Bowie County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-F-148-202.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of revocation is affirmed. The cause is remanded to the trial court, which is ordered to credit Manna for the time spent in jail pending his revocation hearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment of the 202nd Judicial District Court, Bowie County (Texas), which revoked his community supervision. Appellant contended that the trial court erred by not giving him credit for time spent in jail pending his revocation hearing, and that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 15(h)(2) (Supp. 1998) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's community supervision was revoked by the lower court. Appellant contended that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, §15(h)(2) (Supp. 1998) was unconstitutional because it gave the lower court discretion to refuse to give him credit for the time spent in jail pending the revocation hearing. The court held that art. 42.12, §15(h)(2) was unconstitutional, and directed that appellant be given credit for the time spent in jail pending the revocation hearing. Furthermore, the court held that the lower court did not abuse its discretion by revoking appellant's community supervision because the evidence was sufficient to support the conclusion that he violated the terms of his community supervision where he failed to report his address change within the requisite 48 hours, and where he failed to pay the supervision fees during the time period that he was gainfully employed. Therefore, the court affirmed the revocation of appellant's community supervision but remanded with directions that he be credited for the time spent in jail pending the revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of appellant's community supervision, but remanded with directions that he be given credit for the time spent in jail pending the revocation hearing, holding that the statute giving the lower court discretion to refuse such credit was unconstitutional. Furthermore, the lower court did not abuse its discretion by revoking community supervision where appellant violated the terms of his community supervision.

746 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Belcher v. State


NO. 03-96-00541-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


962 S.W.2d 653; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 453



January 23, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMAL COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT NO. CR96-027, HONORABLE CHARLES RAMSAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Comal County (Texas), which convicted him of the state jail felony offense of criminal nonsupport, a violation of Tex. Pen. Code § 25.05 (1994). Appellant challenged both the legal and factual sufficiency of the evidence to support the jury's verdict.


OVERVIEW: Appellant and his wife divorced and the court entered an earnings withholding order for child support. Two years later, appellant was charged with failing to provide support for his daughters. During most, but not all, of the time listed in the charge to the jury, appellant was employed and his employer withheld child support but in an amount insufficient to cover his monthly obligation. Appellant was convicted of criminal nonsupport. The court affirmed finding that even if the violation of a child support order did not automatically translate into a violation of the statute, a rational trier of fact could have found appellant knowingly or intentionally failed to provide support during at least some of the time at issue. The court held that even if not all of the months of nonsupport for which appellant was charged were not proved, he was also on notice of allegations of nonsupport during the other months and had no reason to be surprised by evidence presented to support those allegations. The court found that because the evidence established appellant's failure to provide support for his minor children in at least some of the months, it was sufficient to support the conviction.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction was affirmed because, even if the violation of a child support order did not automatically translate into a violation of the criminal nonsupport statute, there was sufficient evidence to find appellant intentionally or knowingly failed to provide support for his children during some of the time in question. The judgment was not so against the great weight and preponderance of the evidence as to be manifestly unjust.

 

747 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. Miller


NO. 14-96-01384-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


964 S.W.2d 159; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 398



January 22, 1998, Rendered  
January 22, 1998, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the 125th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 95-39005-A. John P. Devine, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed a decision from the 125th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted partial summary judgment for defendant doctor based on the two-year statute of limitations in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 in plaintiffs' medical malpractice and loss consortium actions.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff wife sued defendant doctor for failing to diagnose the cause of her multiple personality disorder. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for defendant in plaintiff's medical malpractice action and plaintiff's husband's loss of consortium action. Plaintiffs' actions were barred by the statute of limitations in Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i. The two-year statute of limitations began April 18, 1992. Plaintiffs did not file their action until 1995. Plaintiffs' summary judgment proof, asserted to contest defendant's motion for summary judgment, was incompetent. Plaintiffs' submission of a social security letter stating she was incompetent was unsworn and constituted hearsay. Two doctors' affidavits contending plaintiff was incompetent were conclusory. Plaintiffs therefore failed to raise a factual issue to preclude summary judgment for defendant on the statute of limitations. The court further held that the general statutory tolling provision for persons under a legal disability, Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.001, were inapplicable to medical malpractice claims under Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment for defendant doctor in plaintiffs' medical malpractice and loss of consortium. Plaintiffs' summary judgment proof concerning her legal disability was incompetent because it was based on hearsay and conclusory allegations and therefore did not raise a factual issue as to whether the two-year statute of limitations applied.

Dewillis v. State


NO. 14-96-00855-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 431



January 22, 1998, Rendered  
January 22, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused June 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 9427328.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the County Criminal Court at Law No. 15, Harris County (Texas), which adjudged him guilty of telephone harassment and stalking under Tex. Penal Code. Ann. §§ 42.07(a)(4) and (a)(7)(A) and revoked his probation after finding that he had violated the conditions of his probation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant convicted of telephone harassment and stalking under Tex. Penal Code. Ann. §§ 42.07(a)(4) and (a)(7)(A) challenged the revocation of his probation, alleging that the evidence was insufficient to support the finding that he violated his probation, and that it was error to deny his motion to quash certain allegations in the state's revocation motion. On appeal the court affirmed the revocation. The evidence showed that appellant drove near complainant's house to make visual contact with her and called her, and that this conduct was prohibited by the no contact condition attached to appellant's probation. The court found that the evidence was sufficient for the trial court to have found by a preponderance of the evidence that appellant violated his probation, and, as such, it was not an abuse of its discretion to revoke appellant's probation. The court determined that allegations contained in a motion to revoke probation did not need to be set out with the same particularity as those of an indictment, but that a revocation motion was sufficient if it gave the probationer fair notice of the allegations against him. The court found that the state's motion met this standard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction and the finding that appellant had violated the terms of his probation, concluding that there was no abuse of discretion in reaching the finding and that it was not error to refuse to quash the revocation motion because it gave appellant fair notice of the allegations pending.

Trevino v. State


NO. 2-96-226-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


962 S.W.2d 176; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 232



January 15, 1998, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. TWO OF TARRANT COUNTY. HON. WAYNE SALVANT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and dismissed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Tarrant County Criminal District Court No. 2 (Texas) that revoked his deferred adjudication and entered a conviction and sentence for burglary of a habitation, challenging the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b), which prohibited an appeal from a revocation of deferred adjudication, and complaining that his case had originally been improperly referred to a magistrate.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was brought before a magistrate and he entered a guilty plea to a charge of burglary of a habitation. He was placed on deferred adjudication and, the next day, his case was referred to the same magistrate, without objection. Defendant subsequently violated his probation and the trial court revoked his deferred adjudication and entered a conviction and sentence of 10 years imprisonment. Defendant appealed, arguing that the original referral of his case to the magistrate was improper and that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 42.12, § 5(b), which prohibited an appeal from a revocation of deferred adjudication, violated his equal protection and due process rights under the federal and Texas constitutions. In affirming with respect to the magistrate issue, the court ruled that defendant failed to preserve that issue for appeal by making a timely objection. In dismissing the appeal concerning the constitutional claim, the court ruled that the provision at issue deprived it of jurisdiction to consider the claim.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed with respect to the referral to a magistrate because defendant failed to preserve that issue by a contemporaneous objection. The appeal was dismissed with respect to the constitutional issue because the challenged statute prohibited such an appeal from a revocation of deferred adjudication.

Piselli v. State


NO. 03-96-00102-CR, NO. 03-96-00103-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 203



January 15, 1998, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused July 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF BURNET COUNTY, 33RD JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NOS. 7771 & 7772, HONORABLE CLAYTON E. EVANS, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on Both Causes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision of the District Court of Burnet County, 33rd Judicial District (Texas), which convicted and sentenced him, based on a jury verdict, on charges of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated assault under Tex. Penal Code Ann. §§ 20.04, 22.02 (1998).


OVERVIEW: Appellant assaulted complainant in her apartment. After going to give a statement to the police, complainant found the apartment vandalized. Appellant later called and told complainant that he would kill her if she pressed charges. The next day, at complainant's employer's residence, appellant appeared, assaulted complainant, took complainant's baby, fired a shotgun several times through the door, and drove away. After a chase and a standoff with police, appellant surrendered. The trial court convicted and sentenced appellant on charges of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated assault, and appellant sought review. The court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the evidence of the first day's incidents to give context to appellant's behavior the next day, under Tex. R. Evid. 404(b). The court also held that because safe release was not an element of the offense of aggravated kidnapping but merely a factor that mitigated punishment, it was not unconstitutional for Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 20.04(d) to place the burden of persuasion to show safe release on appellant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing appellant on charges of aggravated kidnapping and aggravated assault, because contextual evidence of appellant's extraneous conduct was properly admitted and it was appropriate for appellant to bear the burden of proof on safe release of the kidnap victim.

Ramos v. State


No. 04-97-00466-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


961 S.W.2d 637; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 144



January 14, 1998, Delivered  
January 14, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] From the 144th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-CR-0561. Honorable Susan D. Reed, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction for capital murder and murder by the 144th Judicial District Court of Bexar County (Texas), pursuant to a plea bargain agreement with the state. Appellant contended error in the trial court's overruling his motion to quash the indictment and motion to suppress his statement to the police.


OVERVIEW: Appellant first asserted that the indictment for the murder of a one-year-old was unconstitutional because the indictment did not allege that he knew his victim was under six, he has in essence been held to strict liability standards for his crime. The court overruled this error because it had previously held that the statute had no knowledge requirement, beyond the requirement that the defendant knowingly killed the victim, to find a person guilty under this provision. Appellant also claimed that the trial judge erred in refusing to suppress his statement regarding the death of the other victim claiming he made this statement shortly after he was arrested for a previous murder. Appellant claimed that, because he was arrested as a juvenile, he should have been given the admonishments statutorily required for juveniles. The court affirmed his conviction and found that admonishment under the criminal code was appropriate because appellant was seventeen when he was being questioned and he was seventeen when he murdered the child.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction because it found no errors by the trial court in denying his motion to suppress his statement because he was at the statutory age where he could be punished as an adult. The court had also rejected his argument as to knowledge of the child's age prior to the murder because knowledge was not statutorily required.

Butler v. State


NO. 14-95-00728-CR, 14-95-00729-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 48



January 8, 1998, Rendered  
January 8, 1998, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1] PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 15, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 248th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause Nos. 568401 and 9423321.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the 248th District Court of Harris County, Texas that convicted her of murder for the second murder and, also, revoked her probation and entered a conviction for the first murder.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with the first murder and entered a plea of no contest. The lower court deferred adjudication of guilt and imposed a sentenced of 10 years probation. Appellant was then charged with a second murder. The lower court granted the state's motion to adjudicate the first murder and held the hearing during the trial for the second murder. The lower court revoked appellant's probation and convicted her for the first and second murder. The court affirmed because during the adjudication of the second murder, appellant claimed self-defense and that she did not intend to kill the victim and, therefore, the state was permitted to introduce extraneous offense evidence in regard to the first murder to refute appellant's explanation. The court held that the first and second murders were substantially similar in that they both involved a fatal stabbing and, therefore, the evidence in regard to the first murder was relevant in the adjudication of the second murder. The court held that appellant failed to preserve error on the claim that her plea to the first murder was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions of the first and second murders because evidence of the first murder was properly admissible as extraneous offense evidence in the trial of the second murder because it was relevant to refute appellant's claim of self-defense and that she lacked the requisite intent. The court found that the probative value of the evidence substantially outweighed any danger of unfair prejudice.
