Wright v. State


NO. 03-97-00231-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


959 S.W.2d 355; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 38



January 8, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Remand May 18, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 4674. State's Petition for Discretionary Review Granted January 27, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY NO. 96-2343-1, HONORABLE KEVIN HENDERSON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a judgment from the County Court at Law No. 1 of Williamson County (Texas), which convicted and sentenced him for possessing less than two ounces of marihuana after accepting his no contest plea to a plea bargain agreement. Appellant contended that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress evidence seized during an illegal traffic stop.


OVERVIEW: The vehicle in which appellant was riding attracted the attention of police because appellant vomited out the vehicle's window. Police stopped the vehicle, and saw a partially burned marihuana cigarette in plain view. Appellant was charged with possession of less than two ounces of marihuana. At trial, he moved to suppress the evidence on grounds that the initial stop was illegal as the officer had no reasonable suspicion that appellant, or any of the vehicle passengers, were engaged in criminal activity. The trial court denied the motion, and appellant was convicted pursuant to a no contest plea agreement. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction and sentence. The court held that the trial court erred in denying appellant's motion to suppress the evidence because the officer failed to present evidence of a reasonable suspicion of criminal activity connected to the vehicle, or that the stop was pursuant to the officer's exercise of any community control function.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction and sentence for possession of marihuana because the trial court erred in denying appellant's motion to suppress evidence obtained as a result of an illegal search and seizure.

Okigbo v. State


NO. 01-96-00930-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


960 S.W.2d 923; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 87



January 8, 1998, Opinion Issued


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 22, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 262nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 572980. L. Doug Shaver, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed for lack of jurisdiction.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, charged with theft, challenged a decision of the 262nd District Court of Harris County (Texas), which found the allegations of appellee state's motion that appellant had violated his probation to be true. The trial court revoked the probation, found appellant guilty of charged offense, and assessed a punishment. Appellant alleged that his motion to dismiss appellee's motion to adjudicate guilt was improperly dismissed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate was found guilty of theft and assessed punishment of five years deferred adjudication and imposed a fine. Appellee state filed a motion to adjudicate guilt, claiming that appellant had violated the terms of probation. The trial court finding the allegations in appellee's motion to adjudicate to be true, revoked appellant's probation, found him guilty of the charged offense, and assessed him a punishment of a fine and 10 years in prison. Appellant complained of the trial court's denial of his motion and the legality of the sentence imposed. On appeal, the court dismissed appellant inmate's appeal for lack of jurisdiction because he did not comply with the extra notice requirements of the Texas rules of appellate procedure and that he did not have the trial court's permission to appeal, which was required unless appellant was challenging a matter raised in a pretrial motion or alleging a jurisdictional defect. However, because appellant sought reversal based on appellee's failure to use due diligence in apprehending him and the legality of the sentence assessed against him, the court lacked jurisdiction over the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed appellant inmate's appeal for lack of jurisdiction because he did not comply with the extra notice requirements and did not have the trial court's permission to appeal. The court held that appellant was not challenging a matter raised in a pretrial motion and that he did not allege a jurisdictional defect but sought reversal based on appellee state's failure to use due diligence in apprehending him.

 

755 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Andrews v. Wilson


NO. 07-97-0104-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SEVENTH DISTRICT, AMARILLO


959 S.W.2d 686; 1998 Tex. App. LEXIS 56



January 6, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE 99TH DISTRICT COURT OF LUBBOCK COUNTY; NO. 96-554,584; HONORABLE WILLIAM R. SHAVER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, city and city officials, appealed from a judgment of the 99th District Court of Lubbock County (Texas), which granted appellee police officer's cross-motion for summary judgment, and declared that Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. § 143.057 (1988) was constitutional and obligated appellant city to proceed with the selection of a hearing examiner to hear and decide appellee's appeal from a suspension.


OVERVIEW: Instead of appealing his suspension to the particular commission under Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. § 143.053 (1988), appellee police officer sought to appeal under Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. § 143.057 (1988) to a qualified and neutral examiner selected from a list provided by the American arbitration association. The trial court granted appellee's cross-motion for summary judgment, declaring that appellant city was obligated to proceed with a proceeding before a privately appointed examiner. The appellate court reversed and held that appellants, city and city officials, were entitled to summary judgment. As part of a recodification of a prior statute that applied to appellant city, Tex. Local Gov't Code Ann. § 143.053 (1988) applied to appellant city even though its citizens did not vote to adopt it. However, insofar as the statutory provision conferred legislative authority on a private entity to determine the standards for selecting qualified and neutral examiners to review disciplinary actions by a police department, it conferred legislative authority on a private entity in contravention of Tex. Const. art. III, § 1.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment for appellee police officer was reversed, and judgment was rendered for appellants, city and city officials, holding that the statutory provision on which the trial court based its decision unconstitutionally delegated legislative authority on a private entity, and appellant city was not obligated to submit appellee police officer's suspension grievance to a proceeding before a private hearing examiner.

Dodrill v. State


No. 05-95-01875-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6608



December 31, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 283rd Judicial District Court. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. F92-36174-RT.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the 283rd Judicial District Court, Dallas County (Texas), which convicted him for burglary of a vehicle. Initially, the trial court deferred a finding of guilt and placed appellant on probation. After the second motion to adjudicate guilt, the trial court sentenced him to 10 years confinement.


OVERVIEW: Initially, the trial court deferred a finding of guilt and placed appellant on probation. After the second motion to adjudicate guilt, the trial court sentenced him to 10 years confinement. After the time appellant was placed on probation but before the time he was adjudicated guilty the offense's classification was dropped from a felony to a misdemeanor. The sentence range was also reduced. Appellant contended that the trial court erred by failing to sentence him within the appropriate punishment range. The court concluded that the trial court correctly sentenced appellant within the punishment range for a third degree felony because amendments made to the penal code were not retroactive. Appellant also argued that his 10 year sentence was unconstitutionally cruel and unusual because it was disproportionate to the offense he committed. Appellant did not raise this argument in the trial court either when punishment was assessed or in his motion for new trial. Therefore, the court concluded that appellant failed to properly preserve the issue for review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, which convicted him for burglary of a vehicle and sentenced him to 10 years confinement. The court concluded that the trial court correctly sentenced appellant within the punishment range for a third degree felony because amendments made to the penal code were not retroactive.

Harris v. State


NO. 12-96-00309-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, TWELFTH DISTRICT, TYLER


986 S.W.2d 619; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6699



December 31, 1997, Opinion Delivered  
December 31, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 30, 1998. Rehearing Denied March 30, 1998.
Certiorari Denied March 1, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1566.
Rehearing denied by, 03/30/1998
Petition for discretionary review refused by, 09/30/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Harris v. Texas, 525 U.S. 1178, 119 S. Ct. 1115, 143 L. Ed. 2d 111, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 1566 (1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Ex parte Harris, 2009 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 556 (Tex. Crim. App., Sept. 16, 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Ex parte Harris, 2009 Tex. Crim. App. Unpub. LEXIS 794 (Tex. Crim. App., Dec. 9, 2009)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied, Dismissed by Harris v. Thaler, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33577 (S.D. Tex., Mar. 30, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT OF CHEROKEE COUNTY, TEXAS. Adamson, Hon. John.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the Second Judicial District Court of Cherokee County, (Texas), for the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle without the consent of the owner, and his sentence of 10 years imprisonment. Appellant contended that his right to speedy trial was violated and that the indictment was defective.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction and sentence of 10 years imprisonment imposed by the trial court for the unauthorized use of a motor vehicle without the owner's consent, and asserted that his indictment was not timely, that he did not receive a speedy trial, as well as other points of error. The court affirmed and found that appellant failed to urge dismissal of the indictment at a pre-trial hearing. The court found that appellant did not assert his right to a speedy trial until three days before the trial, which gave rise to the implication that he did not want a speedy trial because the matter had been pending for 34 months. The court noted further that appellant had been unable to show harm. The court found that appellant did not object to the state's final argument and waived his right to appeal. The court found the defect in the indictment was without merit as the issue of car ownership was not a serious issue. The court found nothing to review on the assertion of counsel rendered ineffective and held that because there were no records of the grand jury proceedings, there was nothing to review.


OUTCOME: A conviction for unauthorized use of a motor vehicle without the owner's consent was affirmed where appellant waited 34 months before he asserted his right to a speedy trial and was then unable to show harm, and because any defect in the indictment as to the issue of car ownership was not a serious issue.

In re R.L.T.


NO. 01-96-00397-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6677

NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 315th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 89686.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile sought review of the order from the 315th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which waived its jurisdiction and transferred appellant to criminal district court.


OVERVIEW: The state filed an original and amended petition that sought transfer to criminal district court which alleged that appellant juvenile had engaged in delinquent conduct when he committed aggravated robbery and attempted capital murder. The trial court held a hearing, waived jurisdiction, and transferred appellant to have been tried as an adult. Appellant contended that the return of service falsely recited that a true copy of the petition and motion to waive jurisdiction was attached, therefore jurisdiction was improperly invoked. The court stated that an officer's return that was valid on its face carried a presumption of the truth of the facts stated on the return and of regularity. The court also stated that appellant could have rebutted this presumption, but his testimony alone was insufficient. The court also held that appellant's argument that the admission of hearsay evidence during a transfer hearing violated his due process rights and fundamental fairness had previously been rejected by the appellate court. Judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Order of the court which waived jurisdiction and transferred appellant juvenile to have been tried as an adult was affirmed. Appellant failed to have rebutted the presumption of truth regarding the facts stated on the return of service when he offered no other evidence than his testimony.

Lee v. State


NO. 01-96-00611-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6680



December 23, 1997, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 176th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 523955.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 176th District Court, Harris County, Texas, to revoke his probation. Appellee state sought to revoke the probation on grounds appellant had failed to remain under custodial supervision or pay restitution and extradition costs. Appellant contended, inter alia, that the statute under which he was originally convicted, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.04(a), was void and unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to theft of service, for retaining a rental car beyond the expiration of the rental period. His sentenced included 10-years probation. Appellee state sought to revoke appellant's probation on two prior occasions. In the third motion to revoke, appellee alleged appellant had not remained under custodial supervision or paid restitution and extradition cost. The trial court revoked appellant's community supervision for failure to remain under custodial supervision and imposed the 10-year sentence. Appellant sought review alleging, inter alia, that Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 31.04(a), under which he was originally charged and convicted, was unconstitutional and void. The court held the statute was not void or unconstitutional. The statute did not constitute imprisonment for debt, because a defendant was punished for acting with intent to avoid paying for services rendered, not for failure to pay for services rendered. The court also held the written sentence controlled over the court's verbal statements; the motions for revocation did not violate double jeopardy; and there was no evidence of ineffective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's revocation of appellant's probation on grounds appellant had failed to remain under custodial supervision or pay restitution and extradition costs. The court held that the statute was not unconstitutional as appellant's punishment was for acting with intent to avoid a debt. Appellant's other claims of error were also overruled.

Shelby Operating Co. v. City of Waskom


No. 06-97-00080-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


964 S.W.2d 75; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6514; 139 Oil & Gas Rep. 388


November 25, 1997, Submitted  
December 19, 1997, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Opinion on Motion for Rehearing Overruled February 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Tex. App. LEXIs 1080.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 71st Judicial District Court. Harrison County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-0830.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant energy company sought review of judgment from 71st Judicial District Court, Harrison County (Texas), which dismissed appellant's suit against appellees city and partnership after appellee city denied appellant drilling permit as moot under City of Waskom, Tex., Ordinance 96 §A-2, well location.


OVERVIEW: Appellant energy company was the operator of an oil, gas, and mineral lease on land annexed by appellee city. Appellee surface owner purchased the surface rights to the land. Appellant sued appellees after appellee city denied appellant a drilling permit, holding that appellant lacked appellee surface owner's written permission as required by Waskom, Tex., Ordinance 96 § A-2. Appellant argued that the lease constituted consent. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellant, but later stayed its judgment. Appellee surface owner filed motion for a new trial and asked the court to take judicial notice of the amendment of Ordinance 96 that deleted the consent requirement provision. The trial court dismissed the suit as moot and appellant sought review. The court affirmed dismissal of appellant's suit because appellant had no vested right under the ordinance where appellant did not meet the consent requirement and the amended ordinance was not applied retroactively to appellant. The court held that the summary judgment in appellant's favor was a nullity as it was supplanted by the later order dismissing the case as moot, and appellant was not entitled to rely on it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order that dismissed appellant energy company's suit as moot because appellant had no vested right under the original ordinance where appellant had not yet met all of the requirements for a permit and therefore the amended ordinance was not retroactively applied to appellant.

OVERVIEW: Appellant sought review after he was convicted of sexually assaulting a child under 17 years of age. The court found that the evidence was sufficient to convict him of the charged offense. Harlan v. Line


NO. 01-96-01292-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6229



December 4, 1997, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 234th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 95-24307.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant injured motorist challenged the decision of the 234th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which proceeded to trial and awarded appellant damages in a pro se negligence action despite appellant's motions for continuance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant injured motorist brought a pro se negligence action against appellee truck company, after firing her attorney. Before trial, the trial court denied appellant's motions for continuance after appellant had missed a pretrial deposition and conference. The jury awarded appellant damages, and appellant challenged the award and the denial of the continuances. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that pro se litigants were required to follow the same procedural rules as other litigants and that because each of her motions was not accompanied by a sworn affidavit, as required by Tex. R. Civ. P. 251, and she had ample time to find an attorney, the trial court was within his discretion in denying them, and the denials did not violate appellant's due process rights. The court also held that defense exhibits were either not used or were properly authenticated, that appellant's medical records were not authenticated or testified to at trial, and that without them the jury's verdict was not against the preponderance of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant injured motorist's damage award and the denial of her motions for continuance because denying them was within the trial court's discretion, and the grounds used did not render the denial a violation of appellant's due process rights. In addition, without the authentication of appellant's medical records or testimony regarding them at trial, the jury's verdict was not against the preponderance of the evidence.

City of Alamo v. Casas


NUMBER 13-94-043-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


960 S.W.2d 240; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6234



December 4, 1997, Delivered  
December 4, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 5, 1998. Rehearing Denied February 5, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 206th Judicial District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the 206th Judicial District Court of Hidalgo County (Texas), which rendered judgment against it for damages resulting from the arrest and abuse of appellee minor child and his parents, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: Appellee parents and child sued appellant city, police department, chief and officers alleging excessive force, malicious conspiracy, and violations of child's rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. Appellees dropped the claims against the individuals and the jury returned awards in favor of appellees. On appeal, appellant city argued there was insufficient evidence to support the awards. The court found no evidence to support the awards in favor of parents. In viewing the decision in the light most favorable to the verdict, the court found the officers actions amounted to excessive force. It also ruled that evidence was relevant which showed that defendant chief, as the policymaker for the police department, had a pattern and practice of abusing his position of authority and acting outside legal parameters, which was necessary to prove the § 1983 claim. Since the claim was one for personal injury, appellee child's mental anguish was compensable, even in the absence of any physical injury. The court also found appellee had been wrongfully deprived of prejudgment interest.

State v. Wagner


No. 05-96-00587-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6157



December 3, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Court at Law Number Two. Collin County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 2-82642-95.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of an order from the County Court at Law Number Two, Collin County (Texas), which suppressed all of its evidence against appellee, in a shoplifting case.


OVERVIEW: In a shoplifting case, the state argued that the trial court erred in suppressing evidence obtained by store employees because those individuals were not law enforcement officers or otherwise acting as agents of the state. Further, the state contended that appellant's statements made to a police officer were voluntary and not the result of a custodial interrogation and, therefore should not have been suppressed. The court found that the store employees were not acting as agents of the state and did not commit any illegal act in obtaining evidence from appellee. Consequently, there was no basis in the record for suppressing any evidence obtained prior to the arrival of the police. However, the court found that suppression of appellee's statements made to the police was proper because appellee was subject to custodial interrogation, and the officer's questioning exceeded any incidental interrogation. Accordingly, the judgment was affirmed in part, and reversed and remanded in part.


OUTCOME: The order, which suppressed the state's evidence against appellee, was reversed and remanded to the extent that the trial court suppressed the evidence obtained by the store employees prior to the arrival of the police because neither the United States nor Texas Constitutions were implicated by the private actions of the store employees. However, to the extent that the order suppressed evidence obtained by the police officer, it was affirmed.

Ex parte Barnes


NO. 2-96-321-CR, NO. 2-96-322-CR, NO. 2-96-323-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


959 S.W.2d 313; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6696



December 2, 1997, Decided  
December 2, 1997, Opinion Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Denied January 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 1 OF TARRANT COUNTY. TRIAL COURT JUDGE: HON. SHAREN WILSON.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order from the Criminal District Court Number 1 of Tarrant County (Texas) that denied a pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus for discharge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 (Supp. 1998) and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01 (1989), because the prosecution had shown good cause for the untimely indictment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was indicted for indecency with a child and aggravated sexual assault of a child. The court reversed the trial court's denial of appellant's pretrial application for writ of habeas corpus, which sought discharge under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 32.01 (1989) and Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 28.061 (1989) because the prosecution untimely filed an indictment. The prosecution failed to meet its burden of showing that good cause existed for the late filing where its evidence indicated that it was merely trying to better prepare its case for the grand jury. However, the prosecution was not barred from refiling the indictment. Although the legislature had ultimate authority of judicial administration under Tex. Const. art V, § 31 (1985), art. 28.061 shifted the focus from releasing the accused for an untimely filing to infringing the prosecution's ability to indict within a certain time frame by barring any further prosecution and thus it violated the separation of powers doctrine. Tex. Const. art. II, § 1. This rendered any dismissal temporary, permitted the prosecution to refile, and because appellant failed to raise an art. 32.01 complaint the issue was moot.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order that denied appellant's pretrial request for a writ of habeas corpus for discharge of an indictment because the prosecution failed to show good cause for the untimely filing of the indictment. However, the state law that precluded refiling of an indictment was held unconstitutional as violating the separation of powers doctrine, and that made appellant's request for discharge moot.

 

768 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Harwood v. State


No. 04-96-00259-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


961 S.W.2d 531; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6099



November 26, 1997, Delivered  
November 26, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] From the 144th District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 94-CR-5317. Honorable Susan D. Reed, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction for voluntary manslaughter following a jury trial in the 44th District Court, Bexar County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant, a 16-year-old boy, shot and killed a man who had been sexually molesting him. The state charged appellant with murder. Appellant claimed that he fired the fatal shots in self-defense and that he was suffering from post-traumatic stress disorder. The jury found appellant guilty of the lesser-included offense of voluntary manslaughter. The court affirmed, concluding that the trial court properly limited defense counsel's cross-examination of several witnesses because the information counsel sought to elicit was either irrelevant or cumulative. The court further ruled that the prosecutor's comments in closing argument did not warrant reversal because the prosecutor properly commented on the evidence and any prejudice arising from improper comments was cured by the judge's instructions. The court also rejected appellant's claim that the prosecution suppressed crime scene evidence, concluding that the police never seized the evidence and that even if the failure to retrieve the evidence could be considered suppression, no harm occurred as counsel was aware of the evidence from the outset and the jury was informed that the items were at the scene.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for voluntary manslaughter, concluding that the trial court's limitation of defense counsel's examination of several witnesses was proper, the prosecutor's comments during closing argument did not unfairly prejudice appellant, and the prosecution did not suppress any crime scene evidence.

Schwenke v. State


NUMBER 13-96-379-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


960 S.W.2d 227; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6134



November 26, 1997, Delivered  
November 26, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled May 8, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 36th District Court of San Patricio County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant constable sought review of the decision of the 36th District Court of San Patricio County (Texas), which removed him from the office of constable under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 415.053 for failure to obtain certification as a law enforcement officer.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was elected to the constitutional office of constable. When he failed to obtain certification as a law enforcement officer the state moved to remove him. After a jury trial appellant was removed from office. The court affirmed the removal and held that Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 415.053 was constitutional. The court gave effect to the express language of the statute and presumed it was constitutional. The court ruled that the language in dispute in § 415.053 was to provide an effective date for the application of the statute to newly elected officers. The court held there was no conflict between § 415.053 and Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 415.060 because § 415.053 dealt with revocation of licenses for constitutionally elected officers and § 415.060 applied to non-constitutional officers. Appellant was not denied procedural due process rights because he did receive notice, was given a trial, and had the opportunity to present evidence and cross-examination witnesses. The court held that the evidence did not support appellant's request for a jury instruction and that his attempt to prove competence through character testimony was irrelevant to the issue of being certified.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant constable's removal from office holding that the law that authorized his removal was constitutional and that the legislature had the authority under the constitution to define incompetence for removal from office.

 

770 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


City of Alamo v. Garcia


NUMBER 13-97-340-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


960 S.W.2d 221; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6138



November 25, 1997, Delivered  
November 25, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 18, 1997. Rehearing Denied December 18, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 92nd District Court of Hidalgo County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: Appellant's first and second points of error sustained, judgment of the trial court reversed, and rendered judgment that the order of injunction be dissolved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought interlocutory review of a decision of the 92nd District Court of Hidalgo (Texas), which issued a temporary injunction prohibiting appellant from swearing in a newly elected commissioner upon appellee former commissioner's forfeiture of his office under Alamo City Charter art. II, § 6, due to lack of attendance.


OVERVIEW: Appellee former commissioner was automatically removed from the board of commissioners, pursuant to appellant city's charter, for failure to attend four consecutive meetings and eight meetings total within an anniversary year. Appellee thereafter filed suit to enjoin the election and seating of a new commissioner; the trial court granted a temporary injunction, and appellant sought interlocutory review. On appeal, the court held that although the trial court could have granted injunctive relief if the automatic forfeiture provision had violated appellee's due process rights or the Open Meetings Act, no such violation had occurred. A postforfeiture hearing was sufficient to protect appellee's due process rights because his interest paled in comparison to the need to fill the vacancy and ensure that the citizens were represented, and because a factual dispute as to the absences was unlikely. Furthermore, due to the fact that the forfeiture provision required no action by the board, the Open Meetings Act did not apply to the actual forfeiture. Accordingly, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and rendered judgment that the order of injunction be dissolved.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court granting the temporary injunction on appellant city's seating of a newly elected commissioner and rendered judgment for dissolution of the injunction, because there was no violation of appellee former commissioner's due process rights or the Open Meetings Act such that the trial court was authorized to grant injunctive relief.

 

771 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Way v. State


No. 05-95-00981-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIFTH DISTRICT, AT DALLAS


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6002



November 20, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the County Criminal Court No. 10. Dallas County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. MB-94-45478-L.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of her conviction in the County Criminal Court No. 10, Dallas County (Texas), for driving while intoxicated on the grounds that the statute under which she was convicted was unconstitutionally vague thereby depriving her of due process of law.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated. Appellant contended, as her sole point of error, that the statute under which she was convicted was unconstitutionally vague, depriving her of due process of law, where it did not adequately define "drug." The court held that, although the reprinted version of the driving while intoxicated statute under which appellant was convicted incorrectly referenced subdivision (14) instead of subdivision (16) of Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.002 as defining "drug," the session laws referred generally to § 481.002 for a definition of "drug." The court held that under Tex. Gov't Code Ann. § 311.029 (1988), where the language of an enrolled version of a statute conflicts with the language of any subsequent reprinting of the statute, the language of the enrolled bill version controlled.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for driving while intoxicated overruling her sole point of error. The court held that appellant was not deprived of due process because of vagueness where the enrolled version of the driving while intoxicated statute under which she was convicted embraced the definition of "drug," even though the reprinted version of the statute cross-referencing an incorrect subdivision of the statute did not.

Trail Enters. v. City of Houston


NO. 14-96-00689-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


957 S.W.2d 625; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6018; 138 Oil & Gas Rep. 454



November 20, 1997, rendered  
November 20, 1997, Opinion filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Motion for Rehearing of Petition for Review Overruled September 3, 1998. Certiorari Denied January 11, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 154.
Petition for review denied by, 07/03/1998
Motion for rehearing on petition for review overruled by, 09/03/1998
Writ of certiorari denied Trail Enters. v. City of Houston, 525 U.S. 1070, 119 S. Ct. 802, 142 L. Ed. 2d 663, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 154 (1999)
Related proceeding at Trail Enters. v. City of Houston, 2002 Tex. App. LEXIS 1872 (Tex. App. Houston 14th Dist., Mar. 14, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 80th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 95-31573.
Trail Enters. v. City of Houston, 907 F. Supp. 250, 1995 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 20127 (S.D. Tex., 1995)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company challenged the decision of the 80th District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment for appellee city on the grounds that the statute of limitations barred appellant's inverse condemnation claim.


OVERVIEW: Appellee city passed an ordinance prohibiting the drilling of wells within a control area. Appellant oil company filed suit, claiming the ordinance was unconstitutional and void, and it resulted in a taking of its property rights without just compensation. Appellant sought damages for inverse condemnation Appellant challenged the decision granting appellee summary judgment. The trial could held that the inverse condemnation claim was barred by the statute of limitations. On appeal, the court affirmed. The action was untimely under the 10-year limitation period in Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code Ann. § 16.026 (1986). Appellant was charged with constructive notice of the ordinance, and appellant did not plead or prove that it did not discover the cause of action until a later time. Appellee was not estopped from asserting its affirmative defense of limitations in an action for inverse condemnation. The ordinance was a valid exercise of appellee's police power as a means to prevent water contamination. There was a rational relationship between the purpose of the statute and its means, so appellant's substantive due process and equal protection rights were not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment for appellee city because appellant oil company's claims for inverse condemnation were barred by the statute of limitations, and a disputed city ordinance was not unconstitutional.

 

773 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Zavala v. State


NO. 01-96-00041-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 6055



November 20, 1997, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused April 29, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 339th District Court Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 681759.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review from the 339th District Court, Harris County, Texas, of his conviction for possession of cocaine with the intent to deliver. Appellant contended that the denial of his motion to require disclosure of the identity of a confidential informant, and the entry of a guilty plea without an agreed recommendation as to punishment, were both erroneous.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with possession of cocaine with the intent to deliver. The court affirmed. Appellant alleged error as to a failure to have disclosed the identification of an informant. However, such error challenged non-jurisdictional errors that occurred before plea entry, and were waived upon a voluntary plea without an agreed recommendation. Such voluntariness, without a recommendation, waived all pre-plea non-jurisdictional errors. Appellant also claimed the trial court committed reversible error by having assessed the sentence when he was not present at the hearing, and was not shown to have been absent voluntarily. Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 33.03 (1989) required a defendant's presence at a felony trial. However, if absence was voluntary, the trial may have proceeded. The trial court had discretion to have decided voluntariness. Appellant could have presented evidence that explained his absence, but he had not, so the trial court had not abused its discretion when it assessed punishment. Appellant then argued error in the assessment of a maximum sentence. However, appellant had not objected at sentencing, nor moved for a new trial, so he waived such an objection.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence for possession of cocaine with intent to deliver was affirmed. A voluntary plea without an agreed recommendation waived all non-jurisdictional errors which may have occurred before the entry of appellant's plea. An objection to the assessment of a maximum sentence was waived by appellant's failure to have objected at sentencing, or to have moved for a new trial.

Thomas v. Patterson


NO. 14-96-01515-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5938



November 13, 1997, Rendered  
November 13, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 12th District Court. Walker County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 19,564.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged an order by the 12th District Court, Walker County, Texas, which dismissed his cause of action when he failed to comply with the trial court's orders granting special exceptions and requiring appellant to replead within 30 days.


OVERVIEW: Appellant inmate contended that due to a conspiracy by appellees he did not receive appellees' documents relative to their summary judgment motion on his cause of action under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 until after the trial court granted summary judgment. The trial court granted special exceptions relative to appellant's failure to meet formal pleading requirements and ordered appellant to replead within 30 days in his cause of action for conspiracy and violation under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and I. Special exceptions could not inject new factual propositions that did not appear in the petition. The court held that appellees fully complied with Tex. R. Civ. P. 91 by pointing out defects and omissions in the allegations in the pleadings. The court found that no hearing prior to dismissal was required under Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. § 14.003. However, the court reversed the judgment because the trial court erred in dismissing the lawsuit for failure to replead in conformance with Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. 14.004 when the cause of action accrued prior to the statute's effective date.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and remanded for further proceedings because appellant's cause of action accrued prior to the effective date of a statute and the trial court improperly granted special exceptions pertinent to the statute. The court affirmed the trial court's rulings that appellee did not file a demurrer, and special exceptions were proper to correct the failure to observe formal pleading requirements.

Schultz v. Rural/Metro Corp.


NO. 14-96-01079-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


956 S.W.2d 757; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5914



November 13, 1997, Rendered  
November 13, 1997, Opinion Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the County Civil Court at Law Number One. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 657,612.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, decedent's estate representative, challenged a summary judgment of the County Civil Court at Law Number One, Harris County (Texas), granted in favor of appellee, an ambulance company, against appellant in a negligence action to recover damages.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, decedent's estate representative, brought a negligence action against appellee, an ambulance company, to recover damages. The court reversed the trial court judgment and remanded the cause for further proceedings. The trial court erred in applying the two year limitations period contained in the Medial Liability and Insurance Improvement Act, Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 4590i, § 10.01 (Supp. 1997), to bar appellant's action because appellee failed to establish as a matter of law that this provision applied as a valid limitations defense. Appellee's summary judgment proof was insufficient to invoke this limitations provision because it failed to establish that appellee was a health care provider under art. 4590i, § 1.03(a)(3) (Supp. 1997). Therefore, the court held that appellant's action was timely brought under the tolling provisions of Tex. Civ. Prac. & Rem. Code §16.062(a) (1997). The court found that the Emergency Medical Service Act, Tex. Admin. Code. Ann. §197.5(c) (1997), did not support appellee's position. The court did not address appellant's argument that art. 4590i was unconstitutional as applied to her action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment granted in favor of appellee, an ambulance company, against the negligence action brought by appellant, decedent's estate representative, because the trial court erred in applying the limitations period contained in the Medical Liability and Insurance Improvement Act when appellee failed to prove that it was health care facility under the act and remanded the cause for further proceedings.

 

776 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Hays County Appraisal Dist. v. Mayo Kirby Springs


NO. 03-97-00029-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5876



November 13, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Motion for Rehearing Overruled December 11, 1997. As Corrected December 11, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF HAYS COUNTY, 22ND JUDICIAL DISTRICT. NO. 91-0620, HONORABLE CHARLES RAMSAY, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant district sought review of a judgment from the 22nd Judicial District, Hays County (Texas), in appellee owner's favor finding that appellee's real estate inventory had to be valued as one unit instead of the sum of the values of all of appellee's individual lots. Appellee sought review of the denial of attorney's fees.


OVERVIEW: Appellee owner acquired undeveloped commercial and residential lots in a subdivision. Appellee filed suit after appellant district assessed taxes by valuing each individual lot. The lower court found that Tex. Tax Code § 23.12(a) (Supp. 1997) (§23.12) required real estate inventory to be valued as one unit instead of the sum of individual lot values. Appellant sought review, and appellee sought review of the denial of attorney's fees. The court found that §23.12 was not unconstitutional. It defined inventory as unoccupied residential real property held in the ordinary course of business. Tex. Tax Code § 23.01(b) (1992) (§23.01) provided that property appraisal was to be based on the individual characteristics that affected the property's market value. The court found that under §23.01, appellee's property had to be valued as a unit. Two appraisers' testimony was sufficient evidence to support the lower court's assessment of property value. The lower court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellee attorney's fees because there was no finding that appellee had any tax savings, which served as a cap on fees under Tex. Tax Code § 42.29 (1992). The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Judgment in appellee owner's favor was affirmed because appellant district had statutory authority to assess taxes against appellees' ownership of undeveloped commercial and residential lots in a subdivision as one unit, not individually. The lower court did not abuse its discretion in denying appellee attorney fees where the award was discretionary and there was no showing that appellee had tax savings as a result of the judgment.

 

777 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Speed v. State


NO. 01-97-00155-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5794



November 6, 1997, Opinion Issued


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 23rd District Court. Brazoria County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 26,812.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 23rd District Court, Brazoria County, Texas, that denied appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus where appellant contended that double jeopardy precluded his re-trial after the lower court had declared a mistrial because of a disabled juror.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was charged with aggravated burglary, and a trial proceeded before a jury. The lower court read the charge to the jury, and after the jury had deliberated for about two hours, a juror received word that there had been a death in her family. The lower court conducted a hearing in chambers to determine whether the juror was disabled from continued service. The lower court determined that the juror was disabled and declared a mistrial. Appellant filed an application for writ of habeas corpus, claiming that double jeopardy precluded his re-trial. The lower court denied the application, and the court affirmed the denial. The court held that Tex. Code Crim. P. Ann. art. 36.29(c) (1997) required the lower court to discharge the jury when a member became disabled after the charge had been read. Appellant did not raise an objection when the mistrial was declared in chambers or when the lower court announced the mistrial in open court. The court held that appellant's consent to the mistrial could be inferred from appellant's actions, and because appellant consented, a re-trial did not violate appellant's constitutional protections against double jeopardy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of appellant's application for writ of habeas corpus and held that appellant's failure to object to the lower court's declaration of a mistrial when a juror was disabled constituted consent to a re-trial without violating appellant's protections against double jeopardy.

Cuellar v. State


NUMBER 13-96-571-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


957 S.W.2d 134; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5791



November 6, 1997, Delivered  
November 6, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Amended December 18, 1997. As Amended February 24, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 117th District Court of Nueces County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged an order from the 117th District Court of Nueces County (Texas), which entered convictions against him for intoxication manslaughter and driving while intoxicated, arising from the death of a baby girl that had been born alive, at the mother's pregnancy of seven and one-half months, from an emergency caesarian section.


OVERVIEW: Appellant crashed into a car driven by a woman who was seven and one-half months pregnant. An emergency caesarian section was performed, and a live baby girl was born. The baby later died due to injury from the collision. Appellant was convicted of intoxication manslaughter and driving while intoxicated, and challenged both convictions. On review, the court found that, in applying the statutory definition of "has been born and is alive" to the facts, the finding that the victim was indeed an "individual" under the criminal law of Texas was sufficient to sustain an indictment and conviction under the intoxication manslaughter statute, Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 49.08 (1994). Nor was the statute unconstitutionally vague as applied to the facts, as appellant accepted the risk that he might cause the death of another and be subject to a conviction by driving intoxicated. There was no double jeopardy argument as to the driving while intoxicated charge, because the conviction for intoxication manslaughter had been appealed at the time appellant filed his special plea, and thus was not a final conviction when the former charge came before the trial court. The order was affirmed.


OUTCOME: Appellant's convictions for intoxication manslaughter and driving while intoxicated were affirmed. The finding that the infant victim born and alive for a period before dying from injuries due to the car collision caused by appellant was sufficient to sustain a conviction under the intoxication manslaughter statute, which was not unconstitutionally vague. Nor was there any ground for appellant's special plea of double jeopardy.

State ex rel. White v. Bradley


NO. 2-97-259-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


956 S.W.2d 725; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5761



November 6, 1997, Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE 342ND DISTRICT COURT OF TARRANT COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of quo warranto judgment denying summary judgment and declaring appellee removed mayor was entitled to hold office as mayor under Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002 (Vernon 1988), in the 242nd District Court of Tarrant County (Texas).


OVERVIEW: Appellant state sought review of the denial of its motion for summary judgment and quo warranto declaration that appellee removed mayor was entitled to hold office under Tex. Loc. Gov't Code Ann. § 21.002 (Vernon 1988). Appellee was removed for incompetence by the individual aldermen presiding at a "trial" under the statute. The court reversed the denial of summary judgment and declaration of entitlement to office, concluding the authority to grant relief in a quo warranto action was exceeded by the declaration that appellee was entitled to hold office instead of his appointed successor. The court determined appellee had been lawfully removed from the mayoral office, the successor was lawfully appointed before the quo warranto action began, and the refusal to vacate the office rendered appellee a usurper. The court concluded the removal procedure used by the special "court" composed of alderman adhered to applicable statutory procedural requirements and was constitutional. The court explained appellee failed to meet the burden of proving all the elements of his quo warranto defense and negating at least one element of appellant's case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed denial of appellant state's summary judgment motion and declaration that appellee removed mayor was entitled to hold office as mayor instead of a successor because appellee failed to meet burden of negating an essential element of appellant's quo warranto action when appellee was lawfully removed from office, his successor was lawfully appointed, and continued tenure established appellee as a usurper.

Jimerson v. State


No. 06-96-00119-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SIXTH DISTRICT, TEXARKANA


957 S.W.2d 875; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5705


November 4, 1997, Submitted  
November 5, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 124th Judicial District Court. Gregg County, Texas. Trial Court No. 22,463-B.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the 124th Judicial District Court, Gregg County (Texas), which revoked his community supervision. Appellant contended that the trial court failed to credit him for time spent in jail following the arrest for his crime, or for jail time following his revocation arrest under Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 15(h)(2) (Supp. 1997). Appellant also asserted that the evidence did not support revocation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled guilty to delivery of a controlled substance and was sentenced to two years' confinement, the statutory maximum, which was probated for five years. Appellant was not credited with time spent in jail before pleading guilty. The court found this to be error, because U.S. Const. amend. XIV required the award of such jail-time credit. Appellant was later arrested when the state sought to revoke his community supervision for failure to pay fees, to report, or to perform community service. The revocation hearing was held six months after the arrest, but no jail-time credit was given. The court again found error, holding Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12, § 15(h)(2) (Supp. 1997) to be unconstitutional under the due course of law provisions of Tex. Const. art. I, § 19, because it was punitive in light of the right to waiver of a revocation hearing, where time otherwise spent awaiting hearing could be applied directly to a sentence. After finding sufficient evidence, the court affirmed the revocation but remanded with instructions to credit appellant with jail time served while awaiting his guilty plea and while awaiting his revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the revocation of appellant's community supervision, but remanded for the trial court to credit appellant with jail time served following his initial arrest, and also for jail time served while awaiting his revocation hearing. The court found that the Fourteenth Amendment and the Texas Constitution required such credit, and a statute making such credit discretionary was unconstitutional.

Brock v. State


No. 04-97-00065-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO

October 31, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: From the 218th Judicial District, La Salle County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-07-00060-CRL. Honorable Stella Saxon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the 218th Judicial District, La Salle County (Texas), which convicted him, upon a guilty plea, of possession of a controlled substance in an amount less than 28 grams, a class A misdemeanor under the Texas Controlled Substance Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.001 et seq. (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant traveled to Mexico, where he obtained a prescription for a controlled substance. Appellant filled the prescription and returned to the United States. When asked by border officials, appellant admitted to possessing the substance and showed his prescription. Appellant was charged under the Texas Controlled Substance Act (TCSA), Tex. The court concluded that the county law enforcement officials had misinterpreted the TCSA, and thus there was no need to determine whether it was preempted. The court held that appellant obtained his controlled substances lawfully under federal law; therefore, the judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss the indictment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court convicting appellant, with instructions to dismiss the indictment, because appellant had obtained his controlled substances lawfully under federal law, and the county law enforcement officials had misinterpreted the Texas Controlled Substance Act.

Hess v. State


No. 04-96-00478-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5605



October 29, 1997, Delivered  
October 29, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 23, 1998. Motion for Rehearing Denied January 26, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 175th Judicial District Court, Bexar County, Texas. Trial Court No. 93-CR-6634. Honorable Mary Roman, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: DISMISSED FOR LACK OF JURISDICTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the 175th Judicial District Court for Bexar County (Texas), which revoked defendant's deferred adjudication probation that was imposed pursuant to a plea agreement for sexual assault.


OVERVIEW: The court dismissed defendant's appeal for lack of jurisdiction. Defendant's deferred adjudication probation was revoked. Defendant challenged the trial court's decision to revoke, argued that revocation was in violation of his right to due process, and claimed that Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 42.12 (1997) was unconstitutional. On review, the court found that art. 42.12 governed deferred adjudication and clearly stated that no appeal could have been taken from a determination under art. 42.12. Therefore, the court simply had no jurisdiction to hear defendant's appeal. The court noted that even if art. 42.12 permitted the court to consider an appeal from the trial court's decision to revoke and adjudicate, the court lacked jurisdiction over defendant's sufficiency claim under Tex. R. App. P. 25.2(b)(3). The court held that was so because there was no jurisdictional defect, the substance of the appeal was not raised by written motion and ruled on before trial, and the trial court did not grant permission to appeal.


OUTCOME: Defendant's appeal was dismissed for lack of jurisdiction because by clear statutory language, no appeal could have been taken from a trial court's decision to revoke probation and adjudicate guilt. The court held that even if it could, it lacked the jurisdiction over the sufficiency claim because the trial court did not grant permission to appeal, the matter was not raised and ruled on at trial, and there was no jurisdictional defect.

 

783 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Henderson County Appraisal Dist. v. HL Farm Corp.


No. 11-96-318-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, ELEVENTH DISTRICT, EASTLAND


956 S.W.2d 672; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5563



October 23, 1997, Decided  
October 23, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from 173rd District Court of Henderson County.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed and rendered in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county appraisal officials sought review of the decision of the 173rd District Court of Henderson County (Texas), which granted appellee corporation open-space designation to land owned by appellee. The trial court also determined appellee was entitled to a refund of excess ad valorem taxes paid during years after appellee had previously filed suit, and state supreme court held Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. §23.56(3) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellee corporation originally filed suit for open-space land designation that was denied. Appellee challenged the validity of Tex. Prop. Tax Code Ann. §23.56(3), and the state supreme court held that the statute was unconstitutional. On remand, the trial court granted appellee open-space designation to land owned and found that appellee was entitled to a refund of excess ad valorem taxes paid during years after statute was deemed unconstitutional. Appellant county appraisal officials challenged that decision. The court affirmed the designation for three of the years complained of because appellee had exhausted its administrative remedies, but reversed for the other three years because appellee did not exhaust its remedies for those years. Appellee had not filed an application for open-space designation or a protest for three of the years; thus, the trial court lacked jurisdiction to determine the designation for those years. Finally, the court held that the retroactive application of the holding of the supreme court's decision in the earlier case where appellee sought review could be retroactively applied because it did not produce substantial inequitable results.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order that granted appellee corporation open-space designation for three of the years that appellee corporation held the land because it exhausted its administrative remedies as required, but the court reversed as to three other years because trial court did not have jurisdiction to consider issue of appellee's entitlement to the designation because appellee did not exhaust its administrative remedies for those years.

 

784 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Jones v. State


NO. 2-96-457-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, SECOND DISTRICT, FORT WORTH


955 S.W.2d 438; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5512



October 23, 1997, DELIVERED


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT NO. 3 OF TARRANT COUNTY.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant criminal defendant sought review of the decision of the Criminal District Court No. 3 of Tarrant County (Texas), which entered judgment against appellant after a jury found him guilty and sentenced him to life in prison for murder in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02 (1994).


OVERVIEW: Appellant criminal defendant was convicted by a jury of murder in violation of Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 19.02(1994). Appellant challenged his conviction and the court affirmed. Appellant alleged that the legislature unconstitutionally shifted the burden of proof from appellee state to appellant by enacting language that reduced a murder charge from a first to a second degree felony provided appellant proved by a preponderance of the evidence that he caused the death under the immediate influence of sudden passion arising from an adequate cause. Appellant also argued that the trial court improperly admitted a photograph of the victim into evidence. The court held that § 19.02 did not lessen appellee's burden to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant committed the crime, and therefore it did not violate appellant's constitutional rights. The court also held that the photograph was properly admitted into evidence and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant criminal defendant's conviction for murder and held that the statute regarding murder did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of poof from appellee state to appellant and did not violate appellant's right to due process of law, and the photograph the trial court admitted of the victim was not an abuse of its discretion.

 

785 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Vie Le v. State


NO. 14-94-01265-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5622



October 23, 1997, Rendered  
October 23, 1997, Opinion Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Opinion on Remand September 14, 2000, Reported at: 2000 Tex. App. LEXIS 6311. Appellant's Petition for Discretionary Review Refused September 23, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the 338th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 670,610.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile sought review from the 338th District Court, Harris County (Texas) for a conviction of capital murder based upon claims that defendant's written confession was inadmissible, the evidence was insufficient to prove an intent to rob the victim, a jury charge was erroneous, weapons were illegally seized, and Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.09 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was convicted of capital murder for killing victim during a robbery. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed. A challenge to the voluntariness of defendant's confession was not preserved; therefore, it was not reviewable. Tex. R. App. P. 52(a). Defendant's signing a confession in the presence of a magistrate, in the magistrate's office, and without the police, met the requirements of Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.09(b)(1)(G) (1996) and Tex. Fam. Code Ann. §§ 52.02(a), 52.025 (1996). The evidence legally and factually supported the conviction because the use of a deadly weapon inferred that defendant intended to kill the victim, and co-conspirator's testimony corroborated defendant's confession that killing occurred during a robbery. The jury was properly not charged on voluntariness under Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 6.01(a) (1994), where it was not raised by evidence. Defendant disavowed any property or possessory interest in a vehicle or weapons seized after a search and, thus, had no expectation of privacy protected by the U.S. Const. amend IV. The Equal Protection Clauses of the United States and Texas constitutions were not violated by Tex. Fam. Code Ann. § 51.09.


OUTCOME: Defendant juvenile's capital murder conviction was affirmed because statutory requirements for obtaining a confession were met, and evidence was sufficient to support an inference that defendant intended to kill the victim during robbery. Also, defendant had no Fourth Amendment right to privacy in a vehicle and weapons, and the Equal Protection Clause was not violated when defendant was tried as an adult and sentenced to life in prison.

McCall v. State


No. 04-96-01010-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5526



October 22, 1997, Delivered  
October 22, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 218th Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-06-00128-CRF. Honorable Stella Saxon, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the 218th Judicial District Court, Frio County (Texas), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health and Safety Code Ann. § 481.001 et seq. (1992).


OVERVIEW: Defendant had gone to Nuevo Laredo, Mexico and obtained a prescription for Valium from a Mexican physician, then filled the prescription at a pharmacy there. Upon returning to Texas, defendant declared his medication and was cleared through customs. He was later stopped for speeding and was asked whether he had any prescription drugs from Mexico. Defendant presented his medication to the officer and was later convicted of possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act), Tex. Health and Safety Code Ann. § 481.001 et seq. (1992). On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court, holding that defendant was in lawful possession of his medication under federal law and was therefore not in violation of the Act. Referring to another case, the court held that the Act was not unconstitutionally vague. The other court noted that the state had been misinterpreting the statute. The Act expressly provided that possession of foreign-prescribed controlled substances obtained pursuant to federal law was lawful conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act (Act). The court found that defendant was in lawful possession of his medication under federal law and was therefore not in violation of the Act. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with instructions to dismiss the indictment.

 

787 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Guillory v. State


NO. 09-95-138 CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, NINTH DISTRICT, BEAUMONT


956 S.W.2d 135; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5448


September 18, 1997, Submitted  
October 15, 1997, Opinion Delivered


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 252nd District Court. Jefferson County, Texas. Trial Cause No. 65,208.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant defendant sought review of his conviction from the 252nd District Court, Jefferson County (Texas), for sexual assault, after the trial court used improper language in a jury instruction during the punishment phase of his trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant defendant was convicted of sexual assault and sought review of his conviction on the ground that the trial court gave an incorrect jury instruction at the punishment stage of the trial. The court found that pursuant to Tex. Const. art. IV, § 11(a), and Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. § 37.07(4) (1993), the trial court was permitted to include instructions on the effects of parole laws in the jury charge. However, the trial court erred in using the phrase "sentence imposed" instead of the statutorily mandated phrase "period of incarceration." Since appellant did not object to this error at trial, his conviction could only be reversed if the error caused egregious harm. The court affirmed the conviction because it found no egregious harm due. The error was mitigated by the fact that there were other instructions given to the jury that clarified the parole laws, the appellant did not receive a maximum sentence, and there were no improper comments from counsel for appellee prosecution regarding parole laws.


OUTCOME: Appellant defendant's conviction for sexual assault from the trial court was affirmed because, even though the jury charge contained an improper instruction, there was no egregious harm to appellant.

Walker v. State


No. 04-96-00716-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5298



October 8, 1997, Delivered  
October 8, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 218th Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-04-00100-CRF. Honorable Olin B. Strauss, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma resident challenged an order by the 218th Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas, which denied appellant's motion to challenge the constitutionality of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §481.117 (1992), in connection with his possession of a scheduled drug prescribed by a foreign physician.


OVERVIEW: Appellant Oklahoma resident was examined by a physician in Mexico and received a prescription for Valium. Appellant correctly declared the medication when reentering the United States. Subsequently, appellant was arrested for felony possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Tex. Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. §481.117(a) (1992) (Act), when appellant informed a Fido County police officer that he was in possession of the prescription drugs. Possession of a controlled substance prescribed by a foreign physician was unlawful under the Act. The court held that the Act was not constitutionally vague because it provided fair warning to an individual of ordinary intelligence of the conduct proscribed. However, the federal Controlled Substances Act, 21 U.S.C.S. §844, provided that an individual was in lawful possession of a controlled substance if it was obtained pursuant to a valid prescription from a practitioner while acting in the course of professional practice. Therefore, the trial court's judgment was reversed because appellant was in lawful possession of a controlled substance pursuant to 21 U.S.C.S. §844 which preempted the Texas statute.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment denying appellant's motion to challenge the constitutionality of an act was reversed and remanded because the possession of his prescription was authorized by federal law.

Willingham v. State


No. 04-96-00713-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5303



October 8, 1997, Delivered  
October 8, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 81st Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas. Trial Court No. 96-02-00011-CRF. Honorable Olin B. Strauss, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the 81st Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas, convicting her of misdemeanor possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Appellant travelled to Mexico where she was examined by a Mexican physician and was prescribed drugs. She filled the prescription at a Mexican pharmacy. After returning to Texas, she was stopped by a police officer who searched her vehicle and found the drugs. Appellant was charged with felony possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act (the Act), Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.117. Pursuant to a plea bargain, appellant pled nolo contendere to misdemeanor possession of a controlled substance. On appeal, appellant contended that the Act was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the Act was not constitutionally vague because it provided fair warning to an individual of ordinary intelligence of the conduct it proscribed. However, the court held that 21 U.S.C.S. § 956 stated that individuals could enter into the United States with a controlled substance which had been lawfully obtained for personal medical use. Further, the court held that an individual was in lawful possession of a controlled substance if the substance was obtained directly from a practitioner while acting in the course of his professional practice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed appellant's conviction for misdemeanor possession of a controlled substance. The court reasoned that she was in lawful possession of drugs because she obtained them through a practitioner and they were obtained for personal medical use.
