Mathis v. State


No. 04-96-00717-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5318



October 8, 1997, Delivered  
October 8, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE

PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY

BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: From the 81st Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas. Trial Court No. 95-08-00099-CRF. Honorable Olin B. Strauss, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the decision of the 81st Judicial District Court, Frio County, Texas, that imposed a six year probated sentence for felony possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.117, after appellant was arrested for possessing medication obtained in Mexico.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was arrested and charged with felony possession of a controlled substance in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act (the Act), Tex. Health & Safety Code § 481.117, after he obtained medications in Mexico without a prescription. Pursuant to a plea bargain, appellant pled nolo contendere, received six years of probation, and was fined $ 2000. Appellant contended that the Act was unconstitutionally vague or preempted by federal law. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court and held that the Act was not unconstitutionally vague because it provided a fair warning to an individual of ordinary intelligence of the conduct it proscribed. The court held that the Act provided sufficient guidelines to law enforcement authorities to obviate capricious application. The court held that the Act was not preempted by federal law because the Act provided that it was to be harmonized with federal law, and persons who obtained a foreign prescription, as allowed by federal statute, were not guilty under the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment against appellant for felony possession of a controlled substance and held that the controlling statute was not unconstitutionally vague and was not preempted by comparable federal law.

Wright v. State


Nos. 04-96-00687, 04-96-00688-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTH DISTRICT, SAN ANTONIO

October 8, 1997, Delivered

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the 218th Judicial District Court, Frio County (Texas), which found her guilty of felony possession of controlled substances in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.001 et seq. (1992).


OVERVIEW: Appellant obtained a prescription for drugs from a physician in Mexico and had the prescription filled there. At the border, appellant presented her medication and related papers to U.S. Custom officials who cleared her and allowed her to proceed. Thereafter, during a traffic stop, appellant was arrested for felony possession of a Mexican prescription. The court reversed a judgment that convicted appellant of felony possession of controlled substances in violation of the Texas Controlled Substances Act, Tex. Health & Safety Code Ann. § 481.001 et seq. (1992). The record established that appellant was in lawful possession of her prescription medication as defined by the act in § 481.002(24) because her actions were authorized under federal law in 21 U.S.C.S. § 844(a) (1988) and 21 C.F.R. § 1311.27 (1966).


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court were reversed, and the causes were remanded with instructions to dismiss the indictment. Appellant was in lawful possession of the prescription medication because her actions were authorized under federal law.

Rose v. State


NO. 03-96-00234-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRD DISTRICT, AUSTIN


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5206



October 2, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: FROM THE COUNTY COURT AT LAW NO. 1 OF WILLIAMSON COUNTY. NO. 95-1792-1, HONORABLE KEVIN HENDERSON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction from the County Court at Law No. 1 of Williamson County (Texas) for communicating with complainant in a threatening and harassing manner, in violation of a protective order. Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.07(a)(2) (1997). Defendant claimed that § 25.07(a)(2) was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain the conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for communicating with complainant in a threatening and harassing manner, in violation of a protective order. Tex. Penal Code Ann. § 25.07(a)(2) (1997). Defendant claimed that § 25.07(a)(2) was unconstitutionally vague and that the evidence was legally insufficient to sustain the conviction. The court reversed defendant's conviction on grounds that, as the state conceded, the evidence, when viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, did not support a finding beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant communicated with complainant in either a threatening or harassing manner. The court did not address defendant's constitutional challenge to § 25.07(a)(2) because that issue was not absolutely necessary to decide the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for communicating with complainant in a threatening and harassing manner, in violation of a protective order. The state conceded that the evidence in the case, when viewed in the light most favorable to the verdict, did not support a finding beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant communicated with complainant in either a threatening or harassing manner.

Downum v. State


NUMBER 13-96-328-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, THIRTEENTH DISTRICT, CORPUS CHRISTI


1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5226



October 2, 1997, Delivered  
October 2, 1997, Filed


NOTICE:   [*1]  PURSUANT TO THE TEXAS RULES OF APPELLATE PROCEDURE, UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS SHALL NOT BE CITED AS AUTHORITY BY COUNSEL OR BY A COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the 36th District Court of San Patricio County, Texas.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the order of the 36th District Court of San Patricio County (Texas) which revoked community supervision and imposed punishment of four years in prison. Appellant argued that the trial court denied him a preliminary hearing, that the Texas Adult Probation Statute was unconstitutional, and that he was incompetent to stand trial at the time of the revocation hearing.


OVERVIEW: Appellant pled nolo contendere to, and was convicted on, a charge of felony criminal mischief. The trial court, however, suspended the imposition of sentence and placed him on community supervision. The state moved to revoke community supervision on the ground that he violated a condition thereof by refusing to participate in a substance abuse treatment program. The trial court heard the motion on appellant's plea of not true, and the state presented written reports, without objection, showing that he was a discipline problem and failed to cooperate in the substance abuse treatment program. The court affirmed and rejected his first point, finding that the trial court had sufficient authority to revoke his probation because he had an adversarial hearing prior to the revocation and the statute was constitutional. Further, the trial court properly heard his testimony and it had specifically found and recited into the record that appellant was competent to stand trial at the time of the revocation hearing.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed because appellant failed to show that the trial court had erred in revoking his probation for refusing to participate in a substance abuse treatment program in accordance with his probation.

 

798 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Tien Tao Ass'n v. Kingsbridge Park Community Ass'n


NO. 01-96-00395-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FIRST DISTRICT, HOUSTON


953 S.W.2d 525; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5141



September 25, 1997, Opinion issued


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 234th District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 95-020758.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowner sought review of the decision of the 234th District Court. Harris County, Texas, which issued an injunction to enforce various deed restrictions on the use of their residential property.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowner was a religious organization that operated out of two adjacent residential properties situated in appellee homeowner's association's subdivision. In violation of various deed restrictions, appellant constructed flagpoles, replaced the backyard with limestone and repainted the home's shutters. Appellant was also using the home as a temple, which caused an influx of traffic in the subdivision. Appellee community filed a complaint against appellant seeking to enjoin it from violating the deed restrictions. The trial court entered a final judgment in favor of appellee. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding the deed restrictions did apply to the "use" of the properties, not just its architectural form. The court also overruled appellant's objection regarding notice of the deed restrictions, holding that appellant had construction notice, by virtue of owning the property. Moreover, the court held that deed restrictions were not contrary to public policy and were not violative of the Religious Freedom Restoration Act and the Federal and Texas Fair Housing Acts, because the deed restrictions did not equate to religious discrimination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision, holding the appellee homeowner's deed restrictions applied to the use of the property, not just its architectural form. The court further found that appellant was charged with constructive notice of the deed restrictions by virtue of owning the property. Moreover, the court held that the deed restriction did not qualify as religion discrimination.

 

799 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Chavez v. State


No. 08-95-00254-CR


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, EIGHTH DISTRICT, EL PASO


960 S.W.2d 829; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 5152



September 25, 1997, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the 120th District Court of El Paso, Texas. (TC # 75020). Trial Court Judge: Hon. Robert Dinsmoor.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, convicted of murder in the 120th District Court of El Paso, Texas, sought review, arguing that appellee state impermissibly commented on appellant's failure to testify, and that Tex. Crim. Proc. Code Ann. art. 37.07, § 3(a) (1997) unconstitutionally conferred on the trial court unfettered discretion to admit evidence at the punishment stage of the trial.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of murder. Evidence of extraneous offenses of aggravated assault, attempted murder, and possession of marijuana were admitted at the punishment stage of the trial. During the punishment stage, appellee state argued to the jury that appellant showed no sorrow or regret. Appellant objected, arguing that the remark impermissibly commented on his failure to testify. The trial court sustained, and instructed the jury to completely disregard the comment. Appellant sought review. The court held that the constitutionality of Tex. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 37.07 § 3(a) (1997), addressing the admissibility of evidence at sentencing, was not properly before the court because appellant made no argument as to how the statute was unconstitutional as applied in his case. The court held that the trial court's instruction that the jury disregard appellee's remark during the punishment phase cured the error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for murder. The court held that the constitutionality of a state law determining the admissibility of evidence at sentencing was not properly before the court, and that appellee state's remarks to the jury regarding appellant's failure to testify were cured by the trial court's instruction that the remarks be disregarded.

 

800 of 1793 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. APS, Inc.


NO. 14-95-01504-CV


COURT OF APPEALS OF TEXAS, FOURTEENTH DISTRICT, HOUSTON


969 S.W.2d 433; 1997 Tex. App. LEXIS 4949



September 11, 1997, rendered  
September 11, 1997, Opinion filed


PRIOR HISTORY:   [**1] On Appeal from the 152nd District Court. Harris County, Texas. Trial Court Cause No. 94-52072-A.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employee challenged a decision from the 152nd District Court, Harris County (Texas), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in appellant's personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: Appellant employee worked for a staffing service. Appellant was assigned to do inventory for appellee employer. While doing such work, appellant injured her back. Appellant was awarded workers' compensation benefits through appellee. Appellant then initiated a personal injury action against appellee. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of appellee on the grounds that appellant elected her remedy by receiving workers' compensation benefits. Appellant contended that she retained her common law action and appellee's notices regarding election of coverage were unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision. Appellant was precluded from proceeding with her common law action because she elected to receive workers' compensation benefits. Appellant had sufficient notice of her opportunity to proceed with a common law action because appellee posted the statutory coverage notices at its place of business, as required by Tex. Rev. Civ. Stat. Ann. art. 8308-3.24.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision because appellant employee was precluded from proceeding in her personal injury action after she chose to receive workers' compensation benefits. Appellant was given sufficient notice of her right to proceed under the workers' compensation statutes or to pursue a common law right of action.
